(1, 66, 4, 17, 121715) He inspected various places on the hill and in the forests to select a site, and finally suggested the present Skandasramam site and then Bhagavan also approved of it.
(1, 66, 4, 18, 121883) Thereupon Kandaswami began converting what was a thick forest of prickly pear on the mountain slope.
(1, 66, 4, 19, 121984) The result of his labours, unaided by any at the time, is the Asramam we see now.
(1, 66, 4, 20, 122066) He added, You cannot imagine the state the site was in originally.
(1, 66, 4, 21, 122133) Kandaswami worked with almost superhuman effort, achieved by his own hands what even four people together could not have done.
(1, 66, 4, 22, 122260) He removed all the prickly pear, reduced stone and boulder to level ground,
(1, 67, 0, 1, 122336) created a garden and raised the Asramam.
(1, 67, 0, 2, 122377) We got four coconut trees for planting.
(1, 67, 0, 3, 122417) To plant them properly Kandaswami dug huge square pits about ten feet deep.
(1, 67, 0, 4, 122493) That would give you an idea of the amount of labour he put into the work he took on hand.

(1, 70, 1, 9, 128905) Bhagavan related to me once the following incident that happened when he was living on the hill: A cartman was engaged one night by a lady new to this town to take her to some street.
(1, 70, 1, 10, 129089) The cartman purposely took her to some out of the way place near the hill and was about to attack her for her jewels or molest her.
(1, 70, 1, 11, 129221) Then two constables appeared on the scene and threatened the cartman and escorted the lady to her proper destination.
(1, 70, 1, 12, 129339) The lady noted the numbers of the constables and made enquiries afterwards about them and it was ascertained that no human police constable had ever done such a service on that night. Ranga Aiyar believes that this was also really Bhagavans work.

(1, 71, 1, 2, 129978) As I was entering the hall about 2 50 p.m., Bhagavan was reading out from the Tamil Arunachala Puranam the verses in which it is said that Gauri, after crossing the several streets of Arunachalam, reached Gautamas Asramam.
(1, 71, 1, 3, 130201) When Bhagavan came to the verses dealing with Gautamas joy at Gauris coming to his Asramam, Bhagavan could not go on, for tears filled his eyes and emotion choked his voice.
(1, 71, 1, 4, 130375) So he laid aside the book and Desai continued his reading of the manuscript.
(1, 71, 1, 5, 130452) I may here record that I have noticed on more than one occasion in the past how Bhagavan could not proceed with the reading of any deeply devotional portions of Tamil works such as Thevaram and devotional hymns of Thayumanavar.
(1, 71, 1, 6, 130680) This afternoon when I took from Bhagavan the above Arunachala Puranam and referred to the portion which moved him so deeply and told him, in effect, that I had discovered his plight which he tried to hide from us all, he remarked, I dont know how those people who perform kalakshepam and explain such passages to audiences manage to do it without breaking down.
(1, 71, 1, 7, 131042) I suppose they must first make their hearts hard like stone before starting their work.
(1, 71, 2, 8, 131130) In the course of Mr. Desais reading of the manuscripts, he read about the holy hill having eight faces.
(1, 71, 2, 9, 131234) To a question of mine whether as a matter of fact this hill has eight faces, Bhagavan replied, The purana says that the Ashta Vasus having flattered themselves in Brahmas presence lost all their merit, and to regain it they came and did penance here all round Arunachala.
(1, 71, 2, 10, 131506) They were given darshan by Siva at one and the same time by Siva assuming eight faces in this hill.
(1, 71, 2, 11, 131606) All those eight Vasus are still in the shape of eight spurs round this hill.
(1, 71, 2, 12, 131683) What is meant by saying all those Vasus are still here as hills and doing penance round this holy hill, it is difficult to understand.
(1, 71, 2, 13, 131818) Does it only mean they are living on these hills and doing penance, or are they themselves these hills? He added, It is difficult now for us to locate where the Ashta Dikpalakas actually stood sentry, whether at the spots
(1, 72, 0, 1, 132040) where the Ashta Dik Lingams are now found or whether the lingams are those which were installed and worshipped by them.
(1, 72, 0, 2, 132160) We cannot be sure where exactly Gauri did penance and where Gautama had his Asramam.
(1, 72, 0, 3, 132245) But it would be safe to assume that Gauri did her penance in the region covered by Pavalakunru, Durga temple and Pachaiamman Koil and that Gautamas Asramam must have also been near this region.
(1, 72, 1, 4, 132439) Bhagavan also said that whatever temple might have originally existed on or about Pavalakunru would seem to have disappeared probably on account of Tippus invasion, that the present temple there was built only about fifty years ago and that he once discovered the remains of an old cannon between Pavalakunru and the northern wall of the Big Temple.
(1, 72, 1, 5, 132789) It would appear that Tippu Sultan placed cannon near Pavalakunru and attacked the northern wall of the temple which was then used as a fort.
(1, 72, 1, 6, 132930) The northern wall still bears traces of cannon shots.
(1, 72, 1, 7, 132984) It seems the information given by Bhagavan was conveyed to the Government and the cannon was carried away and kept as a relic.

(1, 77, 1, 2, 141451) To the visitor who pursued the question about pranayama, Bhagavan said, The aim is to make the mind one pointed.
(1, 77, 1, 3, 141564) For that pranayama is a help, a means.
(1, 77, 1, 4, 141603) Not only for dhyana but in every case where we have to make the mind one pointed, it may be even for a purely secular or material purpose, it is good to make pranayama and then start the other work.
(1, 77, 1, 5, 141802) The mind and prana are the same, having the same source.
(1, 77, 1, 6, 141859) If one is controlled, the other is also controlled at the same time.
(1, 77, 1, 7, 141928) If one is able to make the mind one pointed without the help of pranayama, he need not bother about pranayama.
(1, 77, 1, 8, 142039) But one who cannot at once control the mind, may control the breath and that will lead to control of the mind.
(1, 77, 1, 9, 142150) It is something like pulling a horse by the reins and making it go in one direction.
(1, 77, 2, 10, 142235) Bhagavan asked Mr. Osborne if Mons.
(1, 77, 2, 11, 142271) Le Bot had mentioned the name of the French philosopher who had helped him to attain the experience referred to by him.

(1, 77, 3, 15, 142693) But why should there be any motto?
(1, 77, 3, 16, 142728) Liberation is our very nature.
(1, 77, 3, 17, 142759) We are that.
(1, 77, 3, 18, 142772) The very fact that we wish for liberation shows that freedom from all bondage is our real nature.
(1, 77, 3, 19, 142870) That has not got to be freshly acquired.
(1, 77, 3, 20, 142911) All that is necessary is to get rid of the false notion that we are bound.
(1, 77, 3, 21, 142986) When we achieve that, there will be no desire or thought of any sort.
(1, 77, 3, 22, 143056) So long as one desires liberation, so long, you may take it, one is in bondage. He also said, People are afraid that when ego or mind is killed, the result may be a mere blank and not happiness.
(1, 77, 3, 23, 143251) What really happens is that the thinker, the object of
(1, 78, 0, 1, 143306) thought and thinking, all merge in the one Source, which is Consciousness and Bliss itself, and thus that state is neither inert nor blank.
(1, 78, 0, 2, 143446) I dont understand why people should be afraid of that state in which all thoughts cease to exist and the mind is killed.
(1, 78, 0, 3, 143567) They are every day experiencing that state in sleep.
(1, 78, 0, 4, 143620) There is no mind or thought in sleep.
(1, 78, 0, 5, 143658) Yet when one rises from sleep one says, I slept happily.
(1, 78, 0, 6, 143715) Sleep is so dear to everyone that no one, prince or beggar, can do without it.
(1, 78, 0, 7, 143794) And when one wants to sleep, nothing however high in the range of all the worldly enjoyments can tempt him from much desired sleep.
(1, 78, 0, 8, 143926) A king wants to go to sleep, let us say.
(1, 78, 0, 9, 143967) His queen, dear to him above all other things, comes then and disturbs him.
(1, 78, 0, 10, 144043) But even her, he then brushes aside and prefers to go to sleep.
(1, 78, 0, 11, 144107) That is an indication of the supreme happiness that is to be had in that state where all thoughts cease.
(1, 78, 0, 12, 144212) If one is not afraid of going to sleep, I dont see why one should be afraid of killing the mind or ego by sadhana. (1, 81, 0, 2, 149141) It seems that somebody, to test whether Echammas mind was clear and not wandering, asked the question Has food been sent to Bhagavan today? and Echammal at once showed recognition).
(1, 81, 0, 3, 149323) Her body was cremated.

(1, 81, 0, 5, 149453) Bhagavan replied, It seems she herself had mentioned that her body should be cremated and that her bones alone should be taken and buried in her village. I also asked Bhagavan what he meant by his statement last night that she would often remain with closed eyes.
(1, 81, 0, 6, 149717) He explained, She practised concentrating on the head centre and would be in a trance like state for even two or three days with breath fully controlled.
(1, 81, 0, 7, 149871) I told her it was only laya and one should not be satisfied with it, but must get out of it and beyond it.
(1, 81, 1, 8, 149978) One Mr. Joshi, introduced by our Chaganlal Yogi, put the following questions and Bhagavan gave the following answers:
(1, 81, 2, 9, 150096) Question 1: When I think Who am I?, the answer comes I am not this mortal body but I am chaitanya, atma, or paramatma. And suddenly another question arises  Why has atma come into maya? or in other words Why has God created this world?
(1, 81, 3, 10, 150332) Answer: To enquire Who am I? really means trying to find out the source of the ego or the I thought.
(1, 81, 3, 11, 150433) You are not to think of other thoughts, such as I am not this body, etc. Seeking the source of I serves as a means of getting rid of all other thoughts.
(1, 81, 3, 12, 150586) We should not give scope to other thoughts, such as you mention, but must keep the attention fixed on finding out the source of the I thought, by asking (as each thought arises) to whom the thought arises and if the answer is I get the thought by asking further who is this I and whence its source?
(1, 82, 0, 1, 150885) Question 2: Is atma a subject of sakshatkara?
(1, 82, 1, 2, 150931) Answer: The atma is as it is.
(1, 82, 1, 3, 150961) It is sakshat always.
(1, 82, 1, 4, 150983) There are not two atmas, one to know and one to be known.
(1, 82, 1, 5, 151041) To know it is to be it.
(1, 82, 1, 6, 151065) It is not a state where one is conscious of anything else.
(1, 82, 1, 7, 151124) It is consciousness itself.
(1, 82, 2, 8, 151152) Question 3: I do not understand the meaning of brahma satyam jagat mithya (Brahman is real, the world is unreal).
(1, 82, 2, 9, 151266) Does this world have real existence or not?
(1, 82, 2, 10, 151310) Does the jnani not see the world or does he see it in a different form?
(1, 82, 3, 11, 151382) Answer: Let the world bother about its reality or falsehood.
(1, 82, 3, 12, 151443) Find out first about your own reality.
(1, 82, 3, 13, 151482) Then all things will become clear.
(1, 82, 3, 14, 151517) What do you care how the jnani sees the world?
(1, 82, 3, 15, 151564) You realise yourself and then you will understand.
(1, 82, 3, 16, 151615) The jnani sees that the world of names and forms does not limit the Self, and that the Self is beyond them.
(1, 82, 4, 17, 151723) Question 4: I do not know how to worship.
(1, 82, 4, 18, 151765) So kindly show me the way to worship.
(1, 82, 5, 19, 151803) Answer: Is there a worshipper and a worshipped?
(1, 82, 5, 20, 151851) Find out the I, the worshipper; that is the best way.
(1, 82, 5, 21, 151905) Always the seer must be traced.

(1, 83, 0, 1, 152491) there is such a thing as the mind.

(1, 85, 3, 9, 156712) Mr. Joshi has submitted what Bhagavan calls a question paper, and Bhagavan answers the same.
(1, 85, 4, 10, 156805) First about the jnanis doing work, without the mind: You imagine one cannot do work if the mind is killed.
(1, 85, 4, 11, 156912) Why do you suppose that it is the mind alone that can make one do work.
(1, 85, 4, 12, 156984) There may be other causes which can also produce activity.
(1, 85, 4, 13, 157043) Look at this clock, for instance.
(1, 85, 4, 14, 157077) It is working without a mind.
(1, 85, 4, 15, 157107) Again suppose we say the jnani has a mind.
(1, 85, 4, 16, 157150) His mind is very different from the ordinary mans mind.
(1, 85, 4, 17, 157206) He is like the man who is hearing a story told with his mind all on some distant object.
(1, 85, 4, 18, 157295) The mind rid of vasanas, though doing work, is not doing work.
(1, 85, 4, 19, 157358) On the other hand, if the mind is full of vasanas, it is doing work even if the body is not active or moving.
(1, 85, 5, 20, 157468) Question 2: Is soham the same as Who am I?
(1, 85, 6, 21, 157511) Answer: Aham alone is common to them.
(1, 85, 6, 22, 157549) One is soham.
(1, 85, 6, 23, 157563) The other is koham.
(1, 85, 6, 24, 157583) They are different.
(1, 85, 6, 25, 157603) Why should we go on saying soham?
(1, 85, 6, 26, 157637) One must find out the real I.
(1, 85, 6, 27, 157667) In the question Who am I?, by I is meant the ego.
(1, 85, 6, 28, 157717) Trying to trace it and find its source, we see it has no separate existence but merges in the real I.
(1, 86, 0, 1, 157819) Question 3: I find surrender is easier.
(1, 86, 0, 2, 157859) I want to adopt that path.
(1, 86, 1, 3, 157886) Answer: By whatever path you go, you will have to lose yourself in the One.
(1, 86, 1, 4, 157962) Surrender is complete only when you reach the stage Thou art all and Thy will be done.
(1, 86, 2, 5, 158049) The state is not different from jnana.
(1, 86, 2, 6, 158088) In soham there is dvaita.
(1, 86, 2, 7, 158114) In surrender there is advaita.
(1, 86, 2, 8, 158145) In the Reality there is neither dvaita nor advaita, but That which is, is.
(1, 86, 2, 9, 158220) Surrender appears easy because people imagine that, once they say with their lips I surrender and put their burdens on their Lord, they can be free and do what they like.
(1, 86, 2, 10, 158391) But the fact is that you can have no likes or dislikes after your surrender and that your will should become completely non existent, the Lords Will taking its place.
(1, 86, 2, 11, 158558) Such death of the ego is nothing different from jnana.
(1, 86, 2, 12, 158613) So by whatever path you may go, you must come to jnana or oneness.
(1, 86, 3, 13, 158680) Question 4: How am I to deal with my passions?
(1, 86, 3, 14, 158727) Am I to check them or satisfy them?
(1, 86, 3, 15, 158763) If I follow Bhagavans method and ask, To whom are these passions? they do not seem to die but grow stronger.
(1, 86, 4, 16, 158872) Answer: That only shows you are not going about my method properly.
(1, 86, 4, 17, 158940) The right way is to find out the root of all passions, the source whence they proceed, and get rid of that.
(1, 86, 4, 18, 159048) If you check the passions, they may get suppressed for the moment, but will appear again.
(1, 86, 4, 19, 159138) If you satisfy them, they will be satisfied only for the moment and will again crave satisfaction.
(1, 86, 4, 20, 159237) Satisfying desires and thereby trying to root them out is like trying to quench fire by pouring kerosene oil over it.
(1, 86, 4, 21, 159355) The only way is to find the root of desire and thus remove it.
(1, 86, 5, 22, 159418) Another visitor asked Bhagavan, If I try to make the Who am I? enquiry, I fall into sleep.
(1, 86, 5, 23, 159509) What should I do?
(1, 86, 6, 24, 159527) Bhagavan: Persist in the enquiry throughout your waking hours.
(1, 86, 6, 25, 159590) That would be quite enough.
(1, 86, 6, 26, 159618) If you keep on making
(1, 87, 0, 1, 159640) the enquiry till you fall asleep, the enquiry will go on during sleep also.
(1, 87, 0, 2, 159716) Take up the enquiry again as soon as you wake up.
(1, 87, 1, 3, 159766) Another visitor asked Bhagavan if it was not necessary that the varnasrama differences should go if the nation was to progress.
(1, 87, 2, 4, 159894) Bhagavan: How can one say whether it is necessary or not necessary?
(1, 87, 2, 5, 159962) I never say anything on such subjects.
(1, 87, 2, 6, 160001) People often come and ask me for my opinion on varnasrama.
(1, 87, 2, 7, 160060) If I say anything they will at once go and publish in the papers, So and so also is of such and such an opinion. The same scriptures which have laid down varnasrama dharma have also proclaimed the oneness of all life and abheda buddhi as the only reality.
(1, 87, 2, 8, 160316) Is it possible for anyone to teach a higher truth than the Unity or Oneness of all life?
(1, 87, 2, 9, 160405) There is no need for anyone to start reforming the country or the nation before reforming himself.
(1, 87, 2, 10, 160504) Each mans first duty is to realise his true nature.
(1, 87, 2, 11, 160556) If after doing it, he feels like reforming the country or nation, by all means let him take up such reform.
(1, 87, 2, 12, 160664) Ram Tirtha advertised, Wanted reformers  but reformers who will reform themselves first. No two persons in the world can be alike or can act alike.
(1, 87, 2, 13, 160812) External differences are bound to persist, however hard we may try to obliterate them.
(1, 87, 2, 14, 160899) The attempts of so called social reformers, to do away with such classes or divisions as varnasrama has created, have not succeeded, but have only created new divisions and added a few more castes or classes to the already existing ones, such as the Brahmo Samajists and the Arya Samajists.
(1, 87, 2, 15, 161190) The only solution is for each man to realise his true nature.
(1, 87, 3, 16, 161252) Another visitor said, Jnanis generally retire from active life and do not engage in any worldly activity.
(1, 87, 4, 17, 161358) Bhagavan: They may or may not.
(1, 87, 4, 18, 161389) Some, even after realising, carry on trade or business or rule over a kingdom.
(1, 87, 4, 19, 161468) Some retire into forests and abstain from all acts except those absolutely necessary to keep life in the body.
(1, 87, 4, 20, 161579) So, we cannot say all jnanis give up activity and retire from life.
(1, 88, 0, 1, 161647) Visitor: I want to know if Bhagavan can give concrete examples, like the butcher Dharmavyadha mentioned in our books, of jnanis now living and doing their ordinary daily work in life.
(1, 88, 1, 2, 161831) Bhagavan did not answer.
(1, 88, 2, 3, 161856) Visitor: Is renunciation necessary for Self realisation?
(1, 88, 3, 4, 161913) Bhagavan: Renunciation and realisation are the same.
(1, 88, 3, 5, 161966) They are different aspects of the same state.
(1, 88, 3, 6, 162012) Giving up the non self is renunciation.
(1, 88, 3, 7, 162052) Inhering in the Self is jnana or Self realisation.
(1, 88, 3, 8, 162103) One is the negative and the other the positive aspect of the same, single truth.
(1, 88, 3, 9, 162184) Bhakti, jnana, yoga  are different names for Self realisation or mukti which is our real nature.
(1, 88, 3, 10, 162281) These appear as the means first.
(1, 88, 3, 11, 162314) They eventually are the goal.
(1, 88, 3, 12, 162344) So long as there is conscious effort required on our part to keep up bhakti, yoga, dhyana, etc., they are the means.
(1, 88, 3, 13, 162461) When they go on without any effort on our part, we have attained the goal.
(1, 88, 3, 14, 162536) There is no realisation to be achieved.
(1, 88, 3, 15, 162576) The real is ever as it is.
(1, 88, 3, 16, 162603) What we have done is, we have realised the unreal, i.e., taken for real the unreal.
(1, 88, 3, 17, 162687) We have to give up that.
(1, 88, 3, 18, 162712) That is all that is wanted.
(1, 88, 4, 19, 162740) Visitor: How has the unreal come?
(1, 88, 4, 20, 162774) Can the unreal spring from the real?
(1, 88, 5, 21, 162811) Bhagavan: See if it has sprung.
(1, 88, 5, 22, 162843) There is no such thing as the unreal, from another standpoint.
(1, 88, 5, 23, 162906) The Self alone exists.
(1, 88, 5, 24, 162929) When you try to trace the ego, based on which alone the world and all exist, you find the ego does not exist at all and so also all this creation.

(1, 89, 5, 21, 164854) Mr. Joshi put five questions.
(1, 89, 5, 22, 164884) I give below the questions and Bhagavans answers.
(1, 89, 6, 23, 164934) Question 1: Should I go on asking Who am I? without answering?
(1, 89, 6, 24, 164997) Who asks whom?
(1, 89, 6, 25, 165012) Which bhavana (attitude) should be in the mind at the time of enquiry?
(1, 89, 6, 26, 165083) What is I the Self or the ego?
(1, 90, 0, 1, 165114) Answer: In the enquiry Who am I?, I is the ego.
(1, 90, 0, 2, 165162) The question really means, what is the source or origin of this ego?
(1, 90, 0, 3, 165231) You need not have any bhavana in the mind.
(1, 90, 0, 4, 165274) All that is required is, you must give up the bhavana that you are the body, of such and such a description, with such and such a name, etc.
(1, 90, 0, 5, 165415) There is no need to have a bhavana about your real nature.
(1, 90, 0, 6, 165474) It exists as it always does; it is real and no bhavana.
(1, 90, 1, 7, 165530) Question 2: I cannot be always engaged in this enquiry, for I have got other work to do, and when I do such work I forget this quest.

(1, 90, 4, 11, 165835) Answer: It can be done.
(1, 90, 4, 12, 165859) Work without attachment.

(1, 90, 6, 15, 166038) Answer: Dont bother.
(1, 90, 6, 16, 166059) What is destined as work to be done by you in this life will be done by you, whether you like it or not.
(1, 90, 7, 17, 166164) Question 5: Why should I try to realise?
(1, 90, 7, 18, 166205) I will emerge from this state, as I wake up from a dream.
(1, 90, 7, 19, 166263) We do not make an attempt to get out of a dream during sleep.
(1, 90, 8, 20, 166325) Answer: In a dream, you have no inkling that it is a dream and so you dont have the duty of trying to get out of it by your effort.
(1, 90, 8, 21, 166457) But in this life you have some intuition, by your sleep experience, by reading and hearing, that this life is something like a dream, and hence the duty is cast on you to make an effort and get out of it.
(1, 90, 8, 22, 166662) However, who wants you to realise the
(1, 91, 0, 1, 166700) Self, if you dont want it?
(1, 91, 0, 2, 166727) If you prefer to be in the dream, stay as you are.
(1, 91, 1, 3, 166778) With reference to question 4, Mrs. P. C. Desai quoting the Bhagavad Gita asked Bhagavan, If (as Arjuna was told) there is a certain work destined to be done by each and we shall eventually do it however much we do not wish to do it or refuse to do it, is there any free will?
(1, 91, 2, 4, 167054) Bhagavan said, It is true that the work meant to be done by us will be done by us.
(1, 91, 2, 5, 167137) But it is open to us to be free from the joys or pains, pleasant or unpleasant consequences of the work, by not identifying ourselves with the body or that which does the work.
(1, 91, 2, 6, 167314) If you realise your true nature and know that it is not you that does any work, you will be unaffected by the consequences of whatever work the body may be engaged in according to destiny or past karma or divine plan, however you may call it.
(1, 91, 2, 7, 167557) You are always free and there is no limitation of that freedom.

(1, 91, 4, 10, 167822) Bhagavan read out to us a few extracts from it, viz., the following quotation from Paul Brunton: I remain perfectly calm and fully aware of who I am and what is occurring.

(1, 91, 4, 12, 168048) Something that is far superior to my unimportant personality rises into consciousness and becomes me.

(1, 91, 4, 15, 168324) It can alter the course of events in a mysterious manner through its own unknown laws, which are superior to all natural laws, and can modify the latter by interaction.
(1, 91, 4, 16, 168493) It is the most powerful force in the universe.

(1, 92, 1, 7, 168983) It is a voice spoken out of cosmic silence .

(1, 92, 3, 10, 169161) Dr. Syed read out to Bhagavan a Sufi story from this months Vision whose moral is that there must be implicit, unquestioning faith in and obedience to the Masters direction.
(1, 92, 4, 11, 169335) When all others would not obey Muhammad Ghaznis command to destroy a precious gem of his, one servant unhesitatingly destroyed it and, when taken to task for it by the others, said, Nothing is more precious to me than my masters command. I was reminded by this of the following incident in Ramanujas life and so related it to Dr. Syed and others.
(1, 92, 4, 12, 169682) It seems God Ranganatha was being taken out in procession in Srirangam and Ramanuja called out to a disciple to come out and see the procession.
(1, 92, 4, 13, 169827) The disciple was boiling Ramanujas milk and would not come out however often he was called, and later explained to his Master, Ranganatha is your Master and he is important to you.
(1, 92, 4, 14, 170008) You alone are important to me and I couldnt leave off your service, i.e., boiling milk for you, to go and see Ranganatha.
(1, 92, 5, 15, 170130) With reference to Bhagavans answer to Mrs. Desais question on the evening of 3 1 46, I asked him, Are only important events in a mans life, such as his main occupation or profession, predetermined, or are trifling acts in his life,
(1, 93, 0, 1, 170362) such as taking a cup of water or moving from one place in the room to another, also predetermined?
(1, 93, 1, 2, 170461) Bhagavan: Yes, everything is predetermined.
(1, 93, 2, 3, 170505) I: Then what responsibility, what free will has man?
(1, 93, 3, 4, 170558) Bhagavan: What for then does the body come into existence?
(1, 93, 4, 5, 170617) It is designed for doing the various things marked out for execution in this life.
(1, 93, 4, 6, 170700) The whole programme is chalked out.
(1, 93, 4, 7, 170736) @Y]u JWm @NV (Not an atom moves except by His Will) expresses the same truth, whether you say @Y]u @NV (Does not move except by His Will) or LoUu @NV (Does not move except by karma).
(1, 93, 4, 8, 170919) As for freedom for man, he is always free not to identify himself with the body and not to be affected by the pleasures or pains consequent on the bodys activities.

(1, 93, 6, 10, 171177) When I entered the hall Bhagavan was answering some question saying, There is no difference between dream and the waking state except that the dream is short and the waking long.
(1, 93, 6, 11, 171356) Both are the result of the mind.
(1, 93, 6, 12, 171389) Because the waking state is long, we imagine that it is our real state.
(1, 93, 6, 13, 171461) But, as a matter of fact, our real state is what is sometimes called turiya or the fourth state which is always as it is and knows nothing of the three avasthas, viz., waking, dream or sleep.
(1, 93, 6, 14, 171653) Because we call these three avasthas we call the fourth state also turiya avastha.
(1, 93, 6, 15, 171736) But it is not an avastha, but the real and natural state of the Self.
(1, 93, 6, 16, 171806) When this is realised, we know it is not a turiya or fourth state, for a fourth state is only relative, but turiyatita, the transcendent state called the fourth state.
(1, 93, 7, 17, 171974) A visitor asked Bhagavan, Priests prescribe various rituals and pujas and people are told that unless they properly
(1, 94, 0, 1, 172090) observe these with fasts, feasts, etc., sin will accrue, and so on.
(1, 94, 0, 2, 172158) Is there any necessity to observe such rituals and ceremonial worship?
(1, 94, 1, 3, 172229) Bhagavan: Yes.
(1, 94, 1, 4, 172244) All such worship is also necessary.
(1, 94, 1, 5, 172280) It may not be necessary for you.
(1, 94, 1, 6, 172313) But that does not mean it is necessary for nobody and is no good at all.
(1, 94, 1, 7, 172386) What is necessary for the infant class pupil is not necessary for the graduate.
(1, 94, 1, 8, 172466) But even the graduate has to make use of the very alphabet he learnt in the infant class.
(1, 94, 1, 9, 172556) He knows the full use and significance of the alphabet now.
(1, 94, 2, 10, 172616) The same visitor asked, I do Omkara puja.
(1, 94, 2, 11, 172658) I say Om Ram.
(1, 94, 2, 12, 172672) Is that good?
(1, 94, 3, 13, 172686) Bhagavan: Yes.
(1, 94, 3, 14, 172701) Any puja is good.
(1, 94, 3, 15, 172719) Om Ram or any other name will do.
(1, 94, 3, 16, 172753) The point is to keep away all other thoughts except the one thought of Om or Ram or God.
(1, 94, 3, 17, 172842) All mantra or japa helps that.
(1, 94, 3, 18, 172873) He who does the japa of Ram, for example, becomes Rama maya.
(1, 94, 3, 19, 172934) The worshipper becomes in course of time the worshipped.
(1, 94, 3, 20, 172991) It is only then that he will know the full meaning of the Omkar which he was repeating.
(1, 94, 4, 21, 173079) Our real nature is mukti.
(1, 94, 4, 22, 173105) But we are imagining we are bound and are making various strenuous attempts to become free, while we are all the while free.
(1, 94, 4, 23, 173230) This will be understood only when we reach that stage.
(1, 94, 4, 24, 173285) We will be surprised that we were frantically trying to attain something which we have always been and are.
(1, 94, 4, 25, 173393) An illustration will make this clear.
(1, 94, 4, 26, 173431) A man goes to sleep in this hall.
(1, 94, 4, 27, 173465) He dreams he has gone on a world tour, is roaming over hill and dale, forest and country, desert and sea, across various continents and after many years of weary and strenuous travel, returns to this country, reaches Tiruvannamalai, enters the Asramam and walks into the hall.
(1, 94, 4, 28, 173742) Just at that moment he wakes up and finds he has not moved an inch but was sleeping where he lay down.
(1, 94, 4, 29, 173845) He has not returned after great effort to this hall, but is and always has been in the hall.
(1, 94, 4, 30, 173938) It is exactly like that.
(1, 94, 4, 31, 173963) If it is asked, why being free we
(1, 95, 0, 1, 173997) imagine we are bound, I answer, Why being in the hall did you imagine you were on a world adventure, crossing hill and dale, desert and sea?
(1, 95, 0, 2, 174138) It is all mind or maya.
(1, 95, 1, 3, 174162) Another visitor, who said that he was from Sri Aurobindos Ashram, asked Bhagavan: But we see pain in the world.
(1, 95, 1, 4, 174274) A man is hungry.
(1, 95, 1, 5, 174291) It is a physical reality.
(1, 95, 1, 6, 174317) It is very real to him.
(1, 95, 1, 7, 174341) Are we to call it a dream and remain unmoved by his pain?
(1, 95, 2, 8, 174399) Bhagavan: From the point of view of jnana or the reality, the pain you speak of is certainly a dream, as is the world of which the pain is an infinitesimal part.
(1, 95, 2, 9, 174561) In the dream also you yourself feel hunger.
(1, 95, 2, 10, 174605) You see others suffering hunger.
(1, 95, 2, 11, 174638) You feed yourself and, moved by pity, feed the others that you find suffering from hunger.
(1, 95, 2, 12, 174729) So long as the dream lasted, all those pains were quite as real as you now think the pain you see in the world to be.
(1, 95, 2, 13, 174847) It was only when you woke up that you discovered that the pain in the dream was unreal.
(1, 95, 2, 14, 174935) You might have eaten to the full and gone to sleep.
(1, 95, 2, 15, 174987) You dream that you work hard and long in the hot sun all day, are tired and hungry and want to eat a lot.
(1, 95, 2, 16, 175093) Then you get up and find your stomach is full and you have not stirred out of your bed.
(1, 95, 2, 17, 175181) But all this is not to say that while you are in the dream you can act as if the pain you feel there is not real.
(1, 95, 2, 18, 175295) The hunger in the dream has to be assuaged by the food in the dream.
(1, 95, 2, 19, 175364) The fellow beings you found in the dream so hungry had to be provided with food in that dream.
(1, 95, 2, 20, 175459) You can never mix up the two states, the dream and the waking state.
(1, 95, 2, 21, 175528) Till you reach the state of jnana and thus wake out of this maya, you must do social service by relieving suffering whenever you see it.
(1, 95, 2, 22, 175665) But even then you must do it, as we are told, without ahamkara, i.e., without the sense I am the doer, but feeling, I am the Lords tool. Similarly one must not be conceited, I am helping a man below me.
(1, 95, 2, 23, 175868) He needs help.
(1, 95, 2, 24, 175883) I am in a position to help.
(1, 95, 2, 25, 175911) I am superior and he inferior. But you must help the man as a means of worshipping God in that man.
(1, 95, 2, 26, 176011) All such service too is for the Self, not for anybody else.
(1, 95, 2, 27, 176071) You are not helping anybody else, but only yourself.
(1, 96, 0, 1, 176124) Mr. T.P. Ramachandra Aiyar said in this connection, There is the classic example of Abraham Lincoln, who helped a pig to get out of a ditch and in the process had himself and his clothes dirtied.
(1, 96, 0, 2, 176320) When questioned why he took so much trouble, he replied, I did it to put an end not so much to the pigs trouble, as to my own pain in seeing the poor thing struggle to get out of the ditch.

(1, 101, 0, 1, 183789) As it was said in that, Only when there is complete devotion, the Lord will respond and take complete charge of the devotee, Mr. P. Bannerji (who has recently come after a stay at Aurobindos) asked Bhagavan, Is it a condition precedent for the Lord showing grace that one must be completely devoted?
(1, 101, 0, 2, 184089) Would not the Lord naturally in his grace be kind towards all his children whether they are devoted or not?
(1, 101, 1, 3, 184197) Bhagavan: How can one help being devoted?
(1, 101, 1, 4, 184239) Everyone loves himself.
(1, 101, 1, 5, 184263) That is experience.
(1, 101, 1, 6, 184283) If the Self were not his dearest object, would one love it?
(1, 101, 1, 7, 184343) The Self or Lord is not somewhere else but is inside each of us and in loving oneself, one loves only the Self.
(1, 101, 2, 8, 184455) The visitor could not understand how this was an answer to his question.
(1, 101, 2, 9, 184528) I explained, Bhagavan has told us more than once, The Lords grace is always flowing.

(1, 101, 2, 11, 184704) But only those can receive it who have developed the capacity.
(1, 101, 2, 12, 184767) Devotion is a condition precedent, not for the flowing of grace from the Lord, but for your being able to receive and assimilate the grace which is there always flowing.
(1, 101, 3, 13, 184937) In this connection Dr. Syed quoted the verse in Bhagavad Gita which says that the Lord is the friend of all, the sinner and the saint alike, but that he is specially in the heart of those who cherish him and that such people are dear to Him.

(1, 101, 5, 15, 185272) Mr. Mahtani again asked Bhagavan about his question (found recorded under 7 1 46).

(1, 101, 5, 17, 185514) The text also says the Supreme Self, when identified with the mind, appears changeful.
(1, 101, 5, 18, 185601) To the seer, the ego, the Self seems changeful.
(1, 101, 5, 19, 185649) But the Self is the same ever, unchanging and unchangeable.
(1, 101, 5, 20, 185709) It is like this: There is a screen.
(1, 101, 5, 21, 185745) On that screen
(1, 102, 0, 1, 185760) first appears the figure of a king.
(1, 102, 0, 2, 185796) He sits on a throne.
(1, 102, 0, 3, 185817) Then before him in that same screen a play begins with various figures and objects and the king on the screen watches the play on the same screen.
(1, 102, 0, 4, 185964) The seer and the seen are mere shadows on the screen, which is the only reality supporting these pictures.
(1, 102, 0, 5, 186071) In the world also, the seer and the seen together constitute the mind and the mind is supported by, or based on, the Self.

(1, 102, 2, 7, 186287) Mr. P. Bannerji asked Bhagavan, What is the difference between jivanmukti and videhamukti?
(1, 102, 3, 8, 186378) Bhagavan: There is no difference.
(1, 102, 3, 9, 186412) For those who ask, it is said, A jnani with body is a jivanmukta and he attains videhamukti when he drops off this body. But this difference is only for the onlooker, not for the jnani.
(1, 102, 3, 10, 186598) His state is the same before and after the body is dropped.
(1, 102, 3, 11, 186658) We think of the jnani as a human form or as being in that form.
(1, 102, 3, 12, 186722) But the jnani knows he is the Self, the one reality which is both inside and outside, and which is not bound by any form or shape.
(1, 102, 3, 13, 186853) There is a verse in the Bhagavata (and here Bhagavan quoted the Tamil verse) which says, Just as a man who is drunk is not conscious whether his upper cloth is on his body or has slipped away from it, the jnani is hardly conscious of his body, and it makes no difference to him whether the body remains or has dropped off.
(1, 102, 4, 14, 187176) Mr. P.B. asked, What is the difference between a devotee and a disciple?
(1, 102, 4, 15, 187249) A friend here told me I should not call myself a disciple of Bhagavan and that I can only be a devotee.
(1, 102, 5, 16, 187353) Bhagavan: If we worship an object or person then we are devotees.
(1, 102, 5, 17, 187419) If we have a Guru then we are disciples.
(1, 102, 6, 18, 187460) I added that his friend must have told him so, for the reason that Bhagavan takes no disciples, i.e., formally initiates none, and so it may be misleading if any one says, I am Bhagavans disciple.
(1, 103, 0, 1, 187657) P.B.: But what if I accept his teaching and regard myself as his disciple because I try to follow his teaching?
(1, 103, 1, 2, 187769) I replied, Of course you may do that, as Ekalavya learnt archery from an image of Drona.
(1, 103, 2, 3, 187858) Bhagavan then added, After all, as in the above case everything comes from within.
(1, 103, 2, 4, 187941) First the man feels that he is bound, in the bondage of samsara, that he is weak and miserable and that unless he leans upon and gets help from God who is all powerful and can save him, he cannot get out of bondage and misery.
(1, 103, 2, 5, 188168) Thus he makes bhakti to Ishwara.
(1, 103, 2, 6, 188201) When this bhakti develops and the intensity of his devotion is so great that he forgets his entire self and becomes Iswaramaya and complete surrender has been achieved, God takes human shape and comes as Guru and teaches the devotee that there is but one Self and that That is within him.
(1, 103, 2, 7, 188490) Then the devotee attains jnana by realizing the Self within him and then he understands that the Ishwara or Lord whom he worshipped and had bhakti for, the Guru who came in human shape, and the Self are all the same.
(1, 103, 3, 8, 188707) Mr. P.B.s first question led Bhagavan to speak further about realisation and he said, There are no stages in realisation or mukti.
(1, 103, 3, 9, 188838) There are no degrees of jnana.
(1, 103, 3, 10, 188869) So that there cannot be one stage of jnana with the body and another stage when the body is dropped.
(1, 103, 3, 11, 188970) The jnani knows he is the Self and that nothing, neither his body nor anything else exists, but the Self.
(1, 103, 3, 12, 189076) To such one what difference could the presence or absence of body make?
(1, 103, 4, 13, 189148) It is false to speak of Realisation.
(1, 103, 4, 14, 189185) What is there to realise?
(1, 103, 4, 15, 189211) The real is as it is, ever.
(1, 103, 4, 16, 189239) How to real ise it?
(1, 103, 4, 17, 189259) All that is required is this.
(1, 103, 4, 18, 189289) We have real ised the unreal, i.e., regarded as real what is unreal.
(1, 103, 4, 19, 189358) We have to give up this attitude.
(1, 103, 4, 20, 189392) That is all that is required for us to attain jnana.
(1, 103, 4, 21, 189445) We are not creating anything new or achieving something which we did not have before.
(1, 103, 4, 22, 189531) The illustration given in books is this.
(1, 103, 4, 23, 189572) We dig a well and create a huge pit.
(1, 103, 4, 24, 189609) The akasa in the pit or well has not been created by
(1, 104, 0, 1, 189662) We have just removed the earth which was filling the akasa there.
(1, 104, 0, 2, 189728) The akasa was there then and is also there now.
(1, 104, 0, 3, 189776) Similarly we have simply to throw out all the age long samskaras which are inside us, and when all of them have been given up, the Self will shine, alone. He also said, Mukti, jnana, dhyana is our real nature.
(1, 104, 0, 4, 189986) They are other names for the Self.

(1, 105, 1, 2, 191832) A young man from Colombo asked Bhagavan, J. Krishnamurti teaches the method of effortless and choiceless awareness as distinct from that of deliberate concentration.
(1, 105, 1, 3, 191998) Would Sri Bhagavan be pleased to explain how best to practise meditation and what form the object of meditation should take?
(1, 105, 2, 4, 192123) Bhagavan: Effortless and choiceless awareness is our real nature.
(1, 105, 2, 5, 192189) If we can attain it or be in that state, it is all right.
(1, 105, 2, 6, 192247) But one cannot reach it without effort, the effort of deliberate meditation.
(1, 105, 2, 7, 192324) All the age long vasanas carry the mind outward and turn it to external objects.
(1, 105, 2, 8, 192405) All such thoughts have to be given up and the mind turned inward.
(1, 105, 2, 9, 192471) For that, effort is necessary for most people.
(1, 105, 2, 10, 192518) Of course everybody, every book says, mU B i.e., Be quiet or still.
(1, 105, 2, 11, 192586) But it is not easy.
(1, 105, 2, 12, 192606) That is why all this effort is necessary.
(1, 105, 2, 13, 192648) Even if we find one who has at once achieved the mauna or Supreme state indicated by mU B, you may take it that the effort necessary has already been finished in a previous life.
(1, 105, 2, 14, 192827) So that, effortless and choiceless awareness is reached only after deliberate meditation.
(1, 105, 2, 15, 192917) That meditation can take any form which appeals to you best.
(1, 105, 2, 16, 192978) See what helps you to keep away all other thoughts and adopt that method for your meditation.
(1, 105, 3, 17, 193072) In this connection Bhagavan quoted verses 5 and 52 from DPp Tn\ and 36 from TVl   of Saint Thayumanavar.
(1, 105, 3, 18, 193177) Their gist is as follows.
(1, 105, 3, 19, 193203) Bliss will follow if you are still.
(1, 105, 3, 20, 193239) But however much you may tell your mind about this truth, the mind will not keep quiet.
(1, 105, 3, 21, 193327) It is the mind that wont keep quiet.
(1, 105, 3, 22, 193364) It is the mind which tells the mind, Be quiet and you will attain bliss.
(1, 105, 3, 23, 193437) Though all the scriptures have said it, though we hear about it every day from the great ones, and though even our Guru says it, we never are quiet, but stray into the world of maya and sense objects.
(1, 105, 3, 24, 193638) That is why conscious, deliberate effort or meditation is required to attain that mauna state or the state of being quiet.
(1, 106, 0, 1, 193761) Another young man from Colombo asked Bhagavan, How are the three states of consciousness inferior in degree of reality to the fourth?
(1, 106, 0, 2, 193895) What is the actual relation between these three states and the fourth?
(1, 106, 1, 3, 193966) Bhagavan: There is only one state, that of consciousness or awareness or existence.
(1, 106, 1, 4, 194050) The three states of waking, dream and sleep cannot be real.
(1, 106, 1, 5, 194110) They simply come and go.
(1, 106, 1, 6, 194135) The real will always exist.
(1, 106, 1, 7, 194163) The I or existence that alone persists in all the three states is real.
(1, 106, 1, 8, 194235) The other three are not real and so it is not possible to say they have such and such a degree of reality.
(1, 106, 1, 9, 194342) We may roughly put it like this.
(1, 106, 1, 10, 194375) Existence or consciousness is the only reality.
(1, 106, 1, 11, 194423) Consciousness plus waking, we call waking.
(1, 106, 1, 12, 194466) Consciousness plus sleep, we call sleep.
(1, 106, 1, 13, 194507) Consciousness plus dream, we call dream.
(1, 106, 1, 14, 194548) Consciousness is the screen on which all the pictures come and go.
(1, 106, 1, 15, 194615) The screen is real, the pictures are mere shadows on it.
(1, 106, 1, 16, 194672) Because by long habit we have been regarding these three states as real, we call the state of mere awareness or consciousness as the fourth.
(1, 106, 1, 17, 194813) There is however no fourth state, but only one state.
(1, 106, 1, 18, 194867) In this connection Bhagavan quoted verse 386 from TWTWd Li of Thayumanavar and said this so called fourth state is described as waking sleep or sleep in waking  meaning asleep to the world and awake in the Self.
(1, 106, 2, 19, 195079) Mr. O. P. Ramaswami Reddiar (the Congress leader) asked Bhagavan, But why should these three states come and go on the real state or the screen of the Self?
(1, 106, 3, 20, 195236) Bhagavan: Who puts this question?
(1, 106, 3, 21, 195270) Does the Self say these states come and go?
(1, 106, 3, 22, 195314) It is the seer who says these states come and go.
(1, 106, 3, 23, 195364) The seer and the seen together constitute the mind.
(1, 106, 3, 24, 195416) See if there is such a thing as the mind.
(1, 106, 3, 25, 195458) Then, the mind merges in the Self, and there is neither the seer nor the seen.
(1, 106, 3, 26, 195537) So the real answer to your question is, Do they come and go?
(1, 106, 3, 27, 195598) They neither come nor go. The Self alone remains as it ever is.
(1, 106, 3, 28, 195662) The three states owe their existence to @NW (non 
(1, 107, 0, 1, 195712) enquiry) and enquiry puts an end to them.
(1, 107, 0, 2, 195754) However much one may explain, the fact will not become clear until one attains Self realisation and wonders how he was blind to the self evident and only existence so long.
(1, 107, 1, 3, 195927) Another visitor asked Bhagavan, What is the difference between the mind and the Self?
(1, 107, 2, 4, 196013) Bhagavan: There is no difference.
(1, 107, 2, 5, 196047) The mind turned inwards is the Self; turned outwards, it becomes the ego and all the world.
(1, 107, 2, 6, 196139) The cotton made into various clothes, we call by various names.
(1, 107, 2, 7, 196203) The gold made into various ornaments, we call by various names.
(1, 107, 2, 8, 196267) But all the clothes are cotton and all the ornaments gold.
(1, 107, 2, 9, 196326) The one is real, the many are mere names and forms.
(1, 107, 3, 10, 196378) But the mind does not exist apart from the Self, i.e., it has no independent existence.
(1, 107, 3, 11, 196466) The Self exists without the mind, never the mind without the Self.

(1, 113, 2, 4, 206199) Mr. P.C. Desai asked Bhagavan, In verse 14, they have translated the second line of the Sanskrit verse as If the mind is continuously fixed on meditation of the Self, etc. Is that all right, seeing that neither continuously nor Self is found in the original?
(1, 113, 3, 5, 206458) Bhagavan: Eka chintana involves continuous thought.
(1, 113, 3, 6, 206510) If no other thought is to come, the one thought has to be continuous.
(1, 113, 3, 7, 206580) What is meant by the verse is as follows: The previous verses have said that for controlling the mind breath control or pranayama may be helpful.
(1, 113, 3, 8, 206726) This verse says that the mind so brought under control or to the state of laya should not be allowed to be in mere laya or a state like sleep, but that it should be directed towards eka chintana or one thought, whether that one thought is of the Self, the ishta devata or a mantram.
(1, 113, 3, 9, 207009) What the one thought may be will depend on each mans pakva or fitness.
(1, 113, 3, 10, 207080) The verse leaves it as one thought.
(1, 113, 4, 11, 207116) Mr. Desai wanted to know if in the next edition verse 14 in the Gujarati should be corrected or if it might stand as now.
(1, 113, 4, 12, 207238) Bhagavan said nothing.
(1, 113, 4, 13, 207261) He had said enough on the subject.
(1, 113, 4, 14, 207296) (I concluded that there could be no harm in introducing continuous in the second line, but there was no justification for bringing in thought or Self as all that Bhagavan said in the original was that the mind brought to laya should be made to occupy itself with eka chintana, one thought).

(1, 114, 0, 2, 207833) I again asked Bhagavan about the meaning of the first line in the Tamil stanza, There seems to be no point in saying whether the body remains in a place or moves about, it is impermanent. Thereupon, he told me that the first line is not to be read as though the whole of it was one sentence and that the first sentence stops with half the line.
(1, 114, 0, 3, 208178) I give below a literal translation for the correct understanding of the stanza:
(1, 114, 1, 4, 208258) The body is impermanent (not real).
(1, 114, 1, 5, 208294) Whether it is at rest or moves about and whether by reason of prarabdha it clings to him or falls off from him, the Self realised siddha is not aware of it, even as the drunken man blinded by intoxication is unaware whether his cloth is on his body or not.

(1, 114, 5, 11, 208957) Dr. Srinivasa Rao asked whether in Stanza 10 of the Supplement to Reality in Forty Verses Bhagavan does not teach us to affirm soham.
(1, 114, 5, 12, 209091) Bhagavan explained it as follows:
(1, 114, 6, 13, 209125) It is said the whole Vedanta can be compressed into the four words, deham, naham, koham, soham.
(1, 114, 6, 14, 209221) This stanza says the same.
(1, 114, 6, 15, 209248) In the first two lines, it is explained why deham is naham, i.e., why the body is not I or na aham.
(1, 114, 6, 16, 209348) The next two lines say, If one enquires ko aham, i.e., Who am I, i.e., if one enquires whence this I springs and realises it, then in the heart of such a one the omnipresent God Arunachala will shine as I, as sa aham or soham: i.e., he will know That I am, i.e., That is I.
(1, 115, 0, 1, 209622) In this connection Bhagavan also quoted two stanzas, one from Thayumanavar and the other from Nammalvar, the gist of both of which is: Though I have been thinking I was a separate entity and talking of I and mine, when I began to enquire about this I, I found you alone exist. The two stanzas and their meaning are given below:
(1, 115, 1, 2, 209950) 1. S] RuUVu SPUp SPuT Y u\{  Y TWTWU(RU]Yo)
(1, 115, 2, 3, 209994) 2. V] Vu{ VV XR V] Vu\] RVu kRu V] Fu PU V Y] VjUm Y]Y W\.(SmUrYo)
(1, 115, 3, 4, 210061) (1) Searching who this I was, Soon I found You only standing as the heaven of bliss, You only, blessed Lord!
(1, 115, 3, 5, 210170)  (Thayumanavar)
(1, 115, 4, 6, 210186) (2) Not knowing who I was, I used to speak of I and mine But I am You and mine is You, Lord whom all the gods adore.
(1, 115, 4, 7, 210303)  (Nammalvar)
(1, 115, 5, 8, 210316) 222224 1 46 Mor 4 1 46 Mor 4 1 46 Mor 4 1 46 Mor 4 1 46 Morning ning ning ning ning

(1, 120, 1, 13, 219761) That is not the cave where she lived.
(1, 120, 1, 14, 219799) She lived only in the mantapam in the Guhai Namasivayar Temple nearby.

(1, 121, 0, 1, 220090) and created Skandasramam later. Then Bhagavan, in a reminiscent mood, added, This Keerai Patti was at the Big Temple even when I first came and was sitting at the Subrahmanyar Temple there.
(1, 121, 0, 2, 220280) She used to provide food to Sadhus in the Temple.
(1, 121, 0, 3, 220330) Later, she began bringing food to me from one Kammala (blacksmith) lady who used to send it.
(1, 121, 0, 4, 220423) After some time that Kammala lady herself began bringing the food to me, instead of sending it through Keerai Patti.
(1, 121, 0, 5, 220540) Then Keerai Patti used to have a big jata (matted locks).
(1, 121, 0, 6, 220598) When I afterwards came to live in Virupakshi Cave, she was living in the Guhai Namasivayar Temple and she had then removed all her hair.
(1, 121, 0, 7, 220735) She lived in the mantapam there and used to worship the images of Namasivayar, etc., carved on the walls and pillars of the mantapam.
(1, 121, 0, 8, 220869) The priest would come and worship the image inside.
(1, 121, 0, 9, 220921) But she worshipped and offered food to the images on the wall in the mantapam where she lived.
(1, 121, 0, 10, 221016) She would get up in the morning, go out for a stroll on the small hill, proceed towards the place where our Asramam is now and go round to where Skandasramam is and come down to her place.
(1, 121, 0, 11, 221205) By that time she would have collected fuel, cow dung, etc., and bundle them up behind her back; and in her lap she would have gathered a lot of green leaves of all sorts for cooking.
(1, 121, 0, 12, 221388) She had only one pot.
(1, 121, 0, 13, 221410) She would first boil water in that pot and bathe.
(1, 121, 0, 14, 221460) In the same pot she would cook her rice, make her sauce, prepare any side dish such as the leaves she had brought, each by turns, offer the food to the images on the wall or pillar, bring them to me and then go and have her own meal.
(1, 121, 0, 15, 221694) In the evening she would go into the town.
(1, 121, 0, 16, 221737) There was not a house in the town which she did not know.
(1, 121, 0, 17, 221795) She would go and ask for various things and get them.
(1, 121, 0, 18, 221849) Coming to me, she would say, A good soul gave me a handful of broken rice.
(1, 121, 0, 19, 221924) I have made porridge out of it.
(1, 121, 1, 20, 221956) But if one went and looked, there would be in her place various provisions and a big pot full of broken rice.
(1, 121, 1, 21, 222066) That was the sort of woman she was.
(1, 121, 1, 22, 222102) She was very fond of me.
(1, 122, 0, 1, 222127) used to go to her now and then.
(1, 122, 0, 2, 222159) I would help her sometimes to gather green leaves, e.g., from a drumstick tree.
(1, 122, 0, 3, 222239) I would also help her sometimes in cleaning and plucking the leaves preparatory to their being cooked.
(1, 122, 0, 4, 222342) Sometimes I used to stay there and eat with her. I asked Bhagavan when she died.

(1, 123, 0, 1, 224154) honey forming in them, so that the same honey released in huge quantities flows in streams and waters the adjoining forest of shambaga trees. All this was explained by Bhagavan.

(1, 124, 1, 14, 227449) Bhagavan was reading Dinamani and, coming across an article there on the temple at Perur (near Coimbatore), read it out to us and said, It is news to me.
(1, 124, 1, 15, 227603) We do not hear of this in the life of Sundaramurti or in the Periyapuranam.
(1, 124, 1, 16, 227679) But it may be in the Sthalapuranam. This is the story: On a particular day in the year, the God and the Goddess are taken out to an adjoining field and the festival of the God and Goddess transplanting seedlings on behalf of a devotee is celebrated, in memory of the fact, that one day Sundaramurti Swami entered the temple and found to his dismay that neither God nor Goddess was there and that on

(1, 127, 5, 9, 232544) A visitor, Ananda Swami, brought a reprint from The Hindu of some date in 1940, in which Maurice Frydman (a devotee of Bhagavan for the last ten years) gives an account of how, under circumstances beyond suspicion of fraud, two women prayed, went into a sort of trance, and then got into their hands mysteriously and from nowhere some sugar candy and almonds.
(1, 127, 5, 10, 232904) The Swami also mentioned that he had seen other instances himself like this where people received fruits, etc., and asked Bhagavan what could be the explanation of such occurrences.

(1, 127, 5, 16, 233262) In the Periyapuranam also is mentioned a similar occurrence.
(1, 127, 5, 17, 233323) A merchant sent his wife two mangoes saying he would eat them later with his meal.
(1, 127, 5, 18, 233406) Before he returned from his business, a sadhu came saying he was very hungry and the wife, pitying him, gave him some rice, and, as she had nothing else ready to give with the rice, one of the mangoes.
(1, 127, 5, 19, 233608) She hoped the husband would be
(1, 128, 0, 1, 233639) satisfied with only one mango.
(1, 128, 0, 2, 233670) The husband returned later and during the meal asked for the mangoes, finished one and finding it very sweet asked for the other one also.
(1, 128, 0, 3, 233809) The wife was in a fix, dreaded her husbands fury and went into the room where she had kept the two fruits before and prayed to God for help in this situation.
(1, 128, 0, 4, 233968) And lo!
(1, 128, 0, 5, 233976) One more fruit lay where she had kept the two fruits, and so she brought it and gave it to her husband.
(1, 128, 0, 6, 234080) He ate it and found it much more delicious and giving him an ecstasy and shanti which he had never before known.
(1, 128, 0, 7, 234193) So he pressed the wife to tell the truth about this fruit and got it out of her.
(1, 128, 0, 8, 234274) In wonder and still a little incredulous, he asked his wife to pray for and get another fruit.
(1, 128, 0, 9, 234369) The wife said she would try, and by Gods grace got another fruit also.
(1, 128, 0, 10, 234440) Then it dawned on him she was a saint and he prostrated himself before her and thinking it was sacrilege for him to treat her further as his wife, left the village, and went and lived in some other village.
(1, 128, 0, 11, 234647) The wife after some time traced him out and thinking that, as he was her Lord, it was her duty to go to him, and it was for him to do what he liked with her, she went towards that village.
(1, 128, 0, 12, 234836) The husband, getting scent of it, told the villagers there, A great saint is coming.
(1, 128, 0, 13, 234921) We must receive her with due respect, ceremony and pomp, taking out a palanquin and music with drums, etc. Thus he organised a big welcome and marching at the head of the reception party prostrated himself first before his wife.
(1, 128, 1, 14, 235150) The wife did not know what to do.
(1, 128, 1, 15, 235184) She shed the mortal body and lived in the astral body and eventually reached heaven taking her husband also there.

(1, 132, 0, 18, 243315) Mr. Balaram came across a passage in Ramana Lila in which it was mentioned that once at Virupakshi Cave Bhagavan alone was present and was working at putting up a small wall and
(1, 133, 0, 1, 243493) that when some visitor came there and asked Bhagavan where was the Swami, Bhagavan told him Swami has gone out. Balaram asked Bhagavan Is it so? Bhagavan said Yes.

(1, 133, 1, 3, 244331) This led Bhagavan to talk of his early days, how when he went about with only an old cod piece and a small, tattered towel, it was naturally not easy for anyone to think of him as a Swami.
(1, 133, 1, 4, 244520) He said, When I was at Pachaiamman Koil I had a small towel which was tattered and torn, almost to rags, with threads having come out in most places.
(1, 133, 1, 5, 244670) Once a cow herd boy made fun of this torn rag, by telling me, The governor wants this towel.
(1, 133, 1, 6, 244763) I replied, Tell him I wont give it to him! I never used to spread it out in public.
(1, 133, 1, 7, 244847) I used to keep it rolled into a ball and wipe my body, hands or mouth as the occasion demanded with the towel so rolled up into a ball.
(1, 133, 1, 8, 244983) I used to wash it and dry it in a place between two rocks, which place was never visited by any of those who were with me.
(1, 133, 1, 9, 245106) Even my cod piece would be tattered.
(1, 133, 1, 10, 245143) When the top end used to become worn out, I would reverse the cod piece and use it with the bottom end topmost.
(1, 133, 1, 11, 245255) When going into the forest I would secretly mend my cod piece with thread taken out of it with prickly pear thorn for needle.
(1, 133, 1, 12, 245381) So, nobody knew or suspected the wretched state of my towel and cod piece.
(1, 133, 1, 13, 245456) One day somehow, one of those who used to be with me in those days went to the place where I used
(1, 134, 0, 1, 245554) to dry my clothes and thus by chance discovered the state of my clothes.
(1, 134, 0, 2, 245627) They then wept that they had allowed such a state of things, that they had committed an inexcusable sacrilege (apachara) and so on.
(1, 134, 0, 3, 245759) They had with them, in trunks, whole pieces of cloth and so many towels, etc., all meant by them to be used for me.
(1, 134, 0, 4, 245875) Only they did not know how badly torn my towel and cod piece were; otherwise they would have long ago substituted others for them. He added, Our Muruganar has mentioned these facts in his songs and has described that I had Indra for my towel, (i.e., a towel with thousand eyelets or holes) and a cod piece stitched by means of a prickly pear spike.

(1, 135, 1, 3, 247876) One Ananda Swami, from Mount Abu, put questions and got the following answers:
(1, 135, 2, 4, 247955) Question: It is said in books that the purusha is angushtha pramana.
(1, 135, 2, 5, 248024) What is it that is meant by it?
(1, 135, 3, 6, 248056) Answer: Evidently the books must be referring to the upadhi in which the purusha is manifesting.
(1, 135, 3, 7, 248153) They cannot mean that the all pervading purusha is angushtha pramana.
(1, 135, 4, 8, 248223) Question: Is that purusha in the heart?
(1, 135, 5, 9, 248263) Answer: If you mean the physical heart, it cannot be.
(1, 135, 5, 10, 248317) But the books describe a heart which is an inverted lotus with a cavity inside and a flame in that cavity and all that.
(1, 135, 5, 11, 248437) In such a psychic heart, the purusha may be said to abide and the flame may be of that angushtha pramana.
(1, 135, 6, 12, 248543) Question: Is seeing that light Self realisation?
(1, 135, 7, 13, 248592) Answer: Abiding in it and being it, not seeing it, is Self realisation.
(1, 135, 8, 14, 248664) Question: In nirvikalpa samadhi what happens to the prana?
(1, 135, 9, 15, 248723) Answer: It goes and merges where it came from.
(1, 135, 10, 16, 248770) Question: I wish to know if there will be breathing then.
(1, 135, 11, 17, 248828) Answer: It may not be then in the form of respiration, but in some sukshma form.

(1, 136, 0, 1, 249156) Question: What is the difference between sushupti ananda and turiya ananda?
(1, 136, 1, 2, 249232) Answer: There are not different anandas.
(1, 136, 1, 3, 249273) There is only one ananda including the ananda enjoyed during the waking state, the ananda, of all kinds of beings from the lowest animal to the highest Brahma, the ananda of the Self.
(1, 136, 1, 4, 249457) The bliss which is enjoyed unconsciously in sleep is enjoyed consciously in turiya.

(1, 136, 1, 6, 249565) The ananda enjoyed during jagrat is upadhi ananda.

(1, 160, 1, 2, 295966) A visitor told Bhagavan, Even in my dream I sometimes feel that I am dreaming, i.e., I am conscious that it is a dream and that a fall for instance there cannot hurt me and so on.

(1, 160, 3, 8, 296409) Another visitor told Bhagavan that some of his dream experiences stood very firmly rooted in his mind, while others were not remembered at all.
(1, 160, 3, 9, 296553) Bhagavan remarked, All that we see is a dream, whether we see it in the dream state or in the waking state.
(1, 160, 3, 10, 296661) On account of some arbitrary standards about the duration of experience and so on, we call one experience dream experience and another waking experience.
(1, 160, 3, 11, 296815) With reference to Reality, both the experiences are unreal.
(1, 160, 3, 12, 296875) A man might have such an experience as getting anugraha (grace) in his dream and the effect and influence of it on his entire subsequent life may be so profound and so abiding that one cannot call it unreal, while calling real some trifling incident in the waking life, that just flits by, is casual, of no moment whatever and is soon forgotten.

(1, 161, 0, 4, 298143) What Muruganar meant to say was: In the classical example, a hand is necessary, a hand that will and can feel a fruit on it, a fruit, an eye that can see, a person that has already known what fruit it is, and so on and so forth.

Thereupon I told Mr. Desai, Bhagavan has told us that the analogy is wrong and misleading.
(1, 167, 0, 2, 309458) The honey is something inert and unconscious, a conscious being is required to taste it and enjoy it.
(1, 167, 0, 3, 309560) On the other hand, the Self is consciousness and bliss itself and it is absurd to argue that when one becomes that, the Self, one will not be able to enjoy bliss and that one must remain separate to enjoy it. Mr. Desai asked, Why then have some saints said so?
(1, 167, 0, 4, 309821) That is our difficulty. I replied, You must ask those saints.
(1, 167, 0, 5, 309883) Bhagavan has given us his opinion quite unambiguously that it is not necessary to remain separate to enjoy complete bliss, and that, on the other hand, the bliss cannot be complete till the merger in the Self is complete.
(1, 167, 1, 6, 310105) 6 3 46 Af 6 3 46 Af 6 3 46 Af 6 3 46 Af 6 3 46 Afttttter er er er ernoon noon noon noon noon
(1, 167, 2, 7, 310198) When I entered the hall, Bhagavan was telling Balaram, Different books and different schools have located the kundalini at different centres in the body.
(1, 167, 2, 8, 310352) While the usual centre with which it is associated is muladhara, there are books which locate it in the heart, and other books which locate it in the brain. Thereupon I asked Bhagavan, You say different people or schools differ on this matter.
(1, 167, 2, 9, 310596) But as Mr. Desai asked Bhagavan yesterday, the difficulty we feel is this.
(1, 167, 2, 10, 310671) If people who have mere book or theoretical knowledge say such contradictory things, we may simply brush them aside.
(1, 167, 2, 11, 310788) But when they come from persons whom we regard as saints who have realised the Self, i.e., those who have had direct or immediate knowledge of the Self, the doubt assails us, Why such difference of opinion among saints? Yesterday I tried to silence Desai simply by saying, If others have given opinions different from Bhagavans, you must ask them why they gave such opinions, not Bhagavan.
(1, 167, 2, 12, 311178) Bhagavan has told us what is the correct opinion. But now, I
(1, 168, 0, 1, 311239) too want to know why different saints differ on such important points.
(1, 168, 0, 2, 311310) Thereupon Bhagavan was pleased to say, They may be Self realised saints and they may know the truth.
(1, 168, 0, 3, 311411) But they have to suit their teaching to those who ask for it and the differences in the teachings are to be explained by the differences in the pakva or fitness of those to whom such teachings are addressed.
(1, 168, 1, 4, 311619) Balaram was reading a collection of Upanishads and, coming across a passage dealing with sahaja samadhi or sahaja sthiti, asked me, Did you not say that Mr. K. S. Ramaswami Sastri once told you that he did not believe in sahaja state and that sahaja state is not mentioned in the earlier books, but is a later innovation?
(1, 168, 1, 5, 311941) I find it mentioned here in the Varaha Upanishads themselves. I said, Yes.
(1, 168, 1, 6, 312016) He thought so.
(1, 168, 1, 7, 312031) He argued with me, How can one be in two planes at the same time?
(1, 168, 1, 8, 312097) Either he sees the absolute and nothing else or sees the world and then does not see the absolute.
(1, 168, 1, 9, 312196) And he said that the sahaja sthiti is not mentioned in the earlier books, but is found only in later works. Balaram said, Where are these two planes for the jnani?
(1, 168, 1, 10, 312360) He is only in one plane and so there is no point in Mr. Sastris argument that one cant be in two planes at the same time. I said, How can we say the jnani is not in two planes?
(1, 168, 1, 11, 312537) He moves about with us like us in the world and sees the various objects we see.
(1, 168, 1, 12, 312618) It is not as if he does not see them.
(1, 168, 1, 13, 312656) For instance he walks along.
(1, 168, 1, 14, 312685) He sees the path he is treading.
(1, 168, 1, 15, 312718) Suppose there is a chair or table placed across that path.
(1, 168, 1, 16, 312777) He sees it, avoids it and goes round.
(1, 168, 1, 17, 312815) So, have we not to admit he sees the world and the objects there, while of course he sees the Self? Bhagavan thereupon said, You say the jnani sees the path, treads it, comes across obstacles, avoids them, etc.
(1, 168, 1, 18, 313026) In whose eyesight is all this, in the jnanis or yours? He continued, He sees only the Self and all in the Self. Thereupon I asked Bhagavan, Are there not illustrations given in our books to explain this sahaja state clearly to us?
(1, 168, 2, 19, 313257) Bhagavan: Why not?
(1, 168, 2, 20, 313276) There are.
(1, 168, 2, 21, 313287) For instance you see a reflection in the mirror and the mirror.
(1, 168, 2, 22, 313351) You know the mirror
(1, 169, 0, 1, 313371) to be the reality and the picture in it a mere reflection.
(1, 169, 0, 2, 313430) Is it necessary that to see the mirror we should cease to see the reflection in it?
(1, 169, 0, 3, 313514) Or again take the screen illustration.
(1, 169, 0, 4, 313553) There is a screen.
(1, 169, 0, 5, 313572) On that screen first a figure appears.
(1, 169, 0, 6, 313611) Before that figure on the same screen other pictures appear and the first figure goes on watching the other pictures.
(1, 169, 0, 7, 313729) If you are the screen and know yourself to be the screen, is it necessary not to see the first figure and the subsequent pictures?
(1, 169, 0, 8, 313860) When you dont know the screen you think the figure and pictures to be real.
(1, 169, 0, 9, 313936) But when you know the screen and realise it is the only reality on which as substratum the shadows of the figure and pictures have been cast, you know these to be mere shadows.
(1, 169, 0, 10, 314113) You may see the shadows, knowing them to be such and knowing yourself to be the screen which is the basis for them all.
(1, 169, 1, 11, 314233) 9 3 46 Mor 9 3 46 Mor 9 3 46 Mor 9 3 46 Mor 9 3 46 Morning ning ning ning ning
(1, 169, 2, 12, 314312) Dr. Masalavala, retired Chief Medical Officer of Bhopal, who has been here for more than a month now and who is now also in temporary charge of the Asramam Hospital in the absence of Dr. Shiva Rao, put the following questions to Bhagavan and got the following answers:
(1, 169, 3, 13, 314581) Question: Bhagavan says, The influence of the jnani steals into the devotee in silence. Bhagavan also says, Contact with great men, exalted souls, is one efficacious means of realising ones true being.
(1, 169, 4, 14, 314783) Bhagavan: Yes.
(1, 169, 4, 15, 314798) What is the contradiction?
(1, 169, 4, 16, 314825) Jnani, great men, exalted souls  does he (Dr.) differentiate between these?
(1, 169, 5, 17, 314901) Thereupon I said, No.
(1, 169, 6, 18, 314923) Bhagavan: Contact with them is good.
(1, 169, 6, 19, 314960) They will work through silence.
(1, 169, 6, 20, 314992) By speaking, their power is reduced.
(1, 169, 6, 21, 315029) Silence is most powerful.
(1, 169, 6, 22, 315055) Speech is always less powerful than silence.
(1, 169, 6, 23, 315100) So mental contact is the best.
(1, 170, 0, 1, 315131) Question: Does this hold good even after the dissolution of the physical body of the jnani or is it true only so long as he is in flesh and blood?
(1, 170, 1, 2, 315278) Bhagavan: Guru is not the physical form.
(1, 170, 1, 3, 315319) So the contact will remain even after the physical form of the Guru vanishes.
(1, 170, 2, 4, 315397) Question: Similarly, does the contact of a devotee with his Guru continue after the passing of the Guru or does it stop?
(1, 170, 2, 5, 315518) It is possible that for a ripe soul his Self may act as his Guru after the going away of the Guru, but what is the unripe soul to do?
(1, 170, 2, 6, 315652) Bhagavan has said that an outer Guru is also needed to push the mind of the devotee towards the Self.
(1, 170, 2, 7, 315754) Can he come in contact with another adept?
(1, 170, 2, 8, 315797) Is this contact to be necessarily physical or will a mental contact do?
(1, 170, 2, 9, 315869) Which is better?
(1, 170, 3, 10, 315886) Bhagavan: As already explained, Guru not being physical form, his contact will continue after his form vanishes.
(1, 170, 3, 11, 315999) If one jnani exists in the world, his influence will be felt by or benefit all people in the world and not simply his immediate disciples.
(1, 170, 3, 12, 316138) All the people in the world are divided into his disciples, bhaktas, those who are indifferent to him and those who are even hostile to him and it is said in the following verse that all these classes will be benefited by the existence of the jnani.
(1, 170, 4, 13, 316388) From Vedanta Chudamani:
(1, 170, 5, 14, 316412) SU PW TjRR]o ~p T L[u SpYL VPj \]dWLm Yk UsLs YujR XuTYWY\ ]j WlTm.
(1, 170, 5, 15, 316480) Bhagavan quoted the next verse, viz., RYV YudRuR{ SmU Rt Pod j UuT YTPR{l  VoTjRod Sp{ UYu\u R NRU LiP R]odV iV l UYu\u Y{d LiRu RX]Ytp TLh TY  UuTo.
(1, 170, 5, 16, 316630) The gist is: Four classes of people are benefited by jivanmuktas.
(1, 170, 5, 17, 316696) By his faith in the jivanmukta, the disciple attains mukti, the
(1, 171, 0, 1, 316760) bhakta who worships his Guru attains merit, the indifferent who have seen the sacred life of the jivanmukta acquire desire for righteousness and even the sinners (i.e., the hostile in the first verse) get rid of their sins by the mere fact of their having had darshan of such saints. God, Guru and the Self are the same.
(1, 171, 0, 2, 317081) After your bhakti to God has matured you, God comes in the shape of Guru and from outside pushes your mind inside, while being inside as Self he draws you there from within.
(1, 171, 0, 3, 317255) Such a Guru is needed generally, though not for very rare and advanced souls.
(1, 171, 0, 4, 317333) One can go to another Guru after his Guru passes away.
(1, 171, 0, 5, 317388) But all Gurus are one, as none of them is the form.
(1, 171, 0, 6, 317440) Always mental contact is the best.
(1, 171, 1, 7, 317475) Question: My practice has been a continuous japa of the names of God with the incoming breath and the name of Baba (i.e., Upasani Baba or Sai Baba) with the outgoing breath.
(1, 171, 1, 8, 317649) Simultaneously with this I see the form of Baba always.
(1, 171, 1, 9, 317705) Even in Bhagavan, I see Baba.
(1, 171, 1, 10, 317735) The external appearances are also much alike.
(1, 171, 1, 11, 317781) Bhagavan is thin.
(1, 171, 1, 12, 317799) Baba was a little stout.
(1, 171, 1, 13, 317824) Now, should I continue this or change the method, as something from within says that if I stick to the name and form I shall never go above name and form?
(1, 171, 1, 14, 317979) But I cant understand what further to do after giving up name and form.
(1, 171, 1, 15, 318051) Will Bhagavan please enlighten me on the point?
(1, 171, 2, 16, 318099) Bhagavan: You may continue in your present method.
(1, 171, 2, 17, 318150) When the japa becomes continuous, all other thoughts cease and one is in ones real nature, which is japa or dhyana.
(1, 171, 2, 18, 318266) We turn our mind outwards on things of the world and are therefore not aware of our real nature being always japa.
(1, 171, 2, 19, 318381) When by conscious effort or japa or dhyana as we call it, we prevent our mind from thinking of other things, then what remains is our real nature, which is japa.
(1, 171, 3, 20, 318543) So long as you think you are name and form, you cant escape name and form in japa also.
(1, 171, 3, 21, 318631) When you realise you are
(1, 172, 0, 1, 318656) not name and form, then name and form will drop off themselves.
(1, 172, 0, 2, 318720) No other effort is necessary.
(1, 172, 0, 3, 318750) Japa or dhyana will naturally and as a matter of course lead to it.
(1, 172, 0, 4, 318818) What is now regarded as the means, japa, will then be found to be the goal.
(1, 172, 0, 5, 318894) Name and God are not different.
(1, 172, 0, 6, 318926) See the teaching of Nama Dev on the significance of Gods name, extracted in the September, 1937, issue of the Vision.
(1, 172, 0, 7, 319044) (This was read out in the hall).
(1, 172, 1, 8, 319077) Bhagavan also quoted the Bible, In the beginning was the Word and the Word was with God and the Word was God.
(1, 172, 2, 9, 319187) Question: Is liberation to be achieved before the dissolution of the body or can it be had after death?
(1, 172, 2, 10, 319291) What is the meaning of a verse like II, 72 or VIII, 6 of the Gita?
(1, 172, 3, 11, 319358) Bhagavan: Is there death for you?
(1, 172, 3, 12, 319392) For whom is death?
(1, 172, 3, 13, 319411) The body which dies, were you aware of it, did you have it, during sleep?
(1, 172, 3, 14, 319485) The body was not, when you slept, but you existed even then.
(1, 172, 3, 15, 319546) When you awoke, you got the body and even in the waking state you exist.
(1, 172, 3, 16, 319619) You existed both in sleep and waking.
(1, 172, 3, 17, 319657) But the body did not exist in sleep and exists only in waking.
(1, 172, 3, 18, 319720) That which does not exist always, but exists at one time and not at another, cannot be real.
(1, 172, 3, 19, 319813) You exist always and you alone are therefore real.
(1, 172, 4, 20, 319864) Liberation is another name for you.
(1, 172, 4, 21, 319900) It is always here and now with you.
(1, 172, 4, 22, 319936) It has not to be won or reached hereafter or somewhere.
(1, 172, 4, 23, 319992) Christ has said, The Kingdom of God is within you here and now.
(1, 172, 4, 24, 320056) You have no death.
(1, 172, 4, 25, 320075) Thayumanavar has sung, NkRRm YRU_L kRm UWQi PuT NRxPo {Yp~ (i.e., even when living in the world those who are always in nishta do not think there is such a thing as death).
(1, 172, 5, 26, 320248) The Gita verse only means in the context of the whole Gita (Ch. II, for instance) that you must achieve liberation during your lifetime.
(1, 172, 5, 27, 320385) Even if you fail to do it during your lifetime, you must think of God at least at the time of death, since one becomes
(1, 173, 0, 1, 320504) what he thinks of at the time of death.
(1, 173, 0, 2, 320544) But unless all your life you have been thinking of God, unless you have accustomed yourself to dhyana of God always during life, it would not at all be possible for you to think of God at the time of death.

(1, 173, 5, 12, 321758) A visitor from Poona, who has been here for the last two or three days, asked some questions, and Bhagavan told him, Mukti or liberation is our nature.

(1, 174, 2, 4, 322594) Dr. Masalawala placed in Bhagavans hands a letter he had received from his friend V.K. Ajgaonkar, a gentleman of about 35 (a follower of Jnaneswar Maharaj) who is said to have attained jnana in his 28th year.
(1, 174, 2, 5, 322803) The letter said, You call me purna.
(1, 174, 2, 6, 322839) Who is not purna in this world? Bhagavan agreed and continued in the vein in which he discoursed this morning, and said, We limit ourselves first, then seek to become the unlimited that we always are.
(1, 174, 2, 7, 323040) All effort is only for giving up the notion that we are limited. The letter further said, The first verse in the Isavasyopanishad says the world is purna.
(1, 174, 2, 8, 323195) It simply cannot be anything else, as its very existence is built on the purna. Bhagavan approved of this also, and said, There is this typed letter, for instance.
(1, 174, 2, 9, 323359) To see the world alone and not the purna or Self would be something like saying.
(1, 174, 2, 10, 323440) I see the letters, but not the paper, while it is the existence of the paper that makes the existence of the letters possible! Dr. M. said, In the letter we see the paper.
