(1, 174, 2, 13, 323741) Then you alone or the Self alone existed.
(1, 174, 3, 14, 323783) The letter also said, Jnaneswar Maharaj has said God will never forsake his bhakta who has undivided love for him. Bhagavan said, Every saint, every book says so.
(1, 174, 3, 15, 323946) I have been reading Ram Dass writings.

(1, 174, 4, 17, 324111) The letter went on to say, Ramana Maharshi is an exponent of ajata doctrine of Advaita Vedanta.
(1, 174, 4, 18, 324207) Of course it is a bit difficult.
(1, 175, 0, 1, 324240) Bhagavan remarked on this, Somebody has told him so.
(1, 175, 0, 2, 324293) I do not teach only the ajata doctrine.
(1, 175, 0, 3, 324333) I approve of all schools.
(1, 175, 0, 4, 324359) The same truth has to be expressed in different ways to suit the capacity of the hearer.
(1, 175, 0, 5, 324448) The ajata doctrine says, Nothing exists except the one reality.
(1, 175, 0, 6, 324512) There is no birth or death, no projection or drawing in, no sadhaka, no mumukshu, no mukta, no bondage, no liberation.
(1, 175, 0, 7, 324631) The one unity alone exists ever. To such as find it difficult to grasp this truth and who ask, How can we ignore this solid world we see all around us?, the dream experience is pointed out and they are told, All that you see depends on the seer.
(1, 175, 0, 8, 324877) Apart from the seer, there is no seen. This is called the drishti srishti vada or the argument that one first creates out of his mind and then sees what his mind itself has created.
(1, 175, 0, 9, 325059) To such as cannot grasp even this and who further argue, The dream experience is so short, while the world always exists.
(1, 175, 0, 10, 325181) The dream experience was limited to me.
(1, 175, 0, 11, 325221) But the world is felt and seen not only by me, but by so many, and we cannot call such a world non existent, the argument called srishti drishti vada is addressed and they are told, God first created such and such a thing, out of such and such an element, and then something else, and so forth. That alone will satisfy this class.
(1, 175, 0, 12, 325552) Their mind is otherwise not satisfied and they ask themselves, How can all geography, all maps, all sciences, stars, planets and the rules governing or relating to them and all knowledge be totally untrue? To such it is best to say, Yes.
(1, 175, 0, 13, 325790) God created all this and so you see it. Dr.M. said, But all these cannot be true; only one doctrine can be true. Bhagavan said, All these are only to suit the capacity of the learner.
(1, 175, 0, 14, 325974) The absolute can only be one.
(1, 175, 1, 15, 326004) The letter further said, Avyabhicharini bhakti is the only necessary thing. As Dr.M. did not understand what avyabhicharini bhakti meant, Bhagavan explained that it only meant bhakti to God without any other thought occupying the mind.
(1, 175, 1, 16, 326240) Bhagavan said, This word, ananya bhakti, ekagrata bhakti, all mean the same thing. The letter continued, In the
(1, 176, 0, 1, 326352) mind two things do not exist at the same time.
(1, 176, 0, 2, 326399) Either God or samsar.
(1, 176, 0, 3, 326421) Samsar is already there.
(1, 176, 0, 4, 326446) That is to be reduced little by little and God is to be entered in its stead. Bhagavan remarked on this.
(1, 176, 0, 5, 326551) God is there already, not samsar.
(1, 176, 0, 6, 326585) Only you do not see it on account of the samsar rubbish you have filled your mind with.
(1, 176, 0, 7, 326673) Remove the rubbish and you will see God.
(1, 176, 0, 8, 326714) If a room is filled with various articles, the space in the room has not vanished anywhere.
(1, 176, 0, 9, 326806) To have space we have not to create it, but only to remove the articles stocked in the room.
(1, 176, 0, 10, 326899) Even so, God is there.
(1, 176, 0, 11, 326922) If you turn the mind inward, instead of outward on things, then you see the mind merges in the one unity which alone exists.
(1, 176, 1, 12, 327047) Bhagavan also agreed with the writer when he said that to see God, Gurus grace is necessary, for which again Gods anugraha is necessary, which in its turn, could be had only by upasana.
(1, 176, 2, 13, 327233) The letter conveyed the writers namaskar to Bhagavan.
(1, 176, 2, 14, 327287) Thereupon, Bhagavan said, The mind merging in its source, the one unity, is the only true namaskar.

(1, 177, 4, 24, 329730) Let us try to find out that which is changeless and which always exists.
(1, 177, 4, 25, 329803) How will it benefit us to know that the kaliyuga started in such and such a year and that it would end so many years after now?
(1, 177, 5, 26, 329931) Girdhari Lal: I know, from the standpoint of one whose level of consciousness is beyond time and space, such
(1, 178, 0, 1, 330040) questions are useless.
(1, 178, 0, 2, 330063) But to us, struggling souls, it may be important in this way.
(1, 178, 0, 3, 330125) It is said that in the previous yugas e.g.
(1, 178, 0, 4, 330168) satya yuga, man had not fallen to the low level in which he now is in this kaliyuga and that it was much easier for him then to attain liberation than now.
(1, 178, 1, 5, 330324) Bhagavan: On the other hand, it is said it is much easier to secure salvation in this yuga than in the satya yuga.
(1, 178, 1, 6, 330439) Some days or hours of penance in this yuga would secure what several years of penance alone could have secured in those yugas.
(1, 178, 1, 7, 330566) That is what the books say.
(1, 178, 1, 8, 330594) Further, there is nothing to attain and no time within which to attain.
(1, 178, 1, 9, 330666) You are always that.
(1, 178, 1, 10, 330687) You have not got to attain anything.
(1, 178, 1, 11, 330724) You have only to give up thinking you are limited, to give up thinking you are this upadhi or body.
(1, 178, 2, 12, 330824) Girdhari Lal: Then, why do these puranas give the exact duration of each yuga in so many years?
(1, 178, 3, 13, 330920) Bhagavan: There might be an allegorical meaning in the number of years mentioned for each yuga.
(1, 178, 3, 14, 331016) Or, the immensity of the periods of time assigned to each yuga may be a mere device to draw mans attention to the fact that, though he should live up to his full span of a hundred years, his life would be such a trifling, insignificant fraction in the entire life of the universe, and that he should therefore take a proper view of his own humble place in the entire scheme and not go about with a swollen head, deeming himself as of great importance.
(1, 178, 3, 15, 331468) Instead of saying, What is mans life compared to eternity? they have taught him to consider how short his span is.
(1, 178, 3, 16, 331583) Further, it is said there is a regular cycle of such yugas.
(1, 178, 3, 17, 331643) And who knows how many such cycles have come and gone.
(1, 178, 3, 18, 331698) Again, each yuga is sub divided into four yugas.
(1, 178, 3, 19, 331747) There is no end to all such calculations; and different schools have their theory as to when the present kaliyuga is to end.
(1, 178, 3, 20, 331872) When time itself does not exist, as for instance in sleep, what is the use of bothering oneself with all such questions?

(1, 189, 2, 3, 351071) A visitor wrote some questions in Tamil and presented them to Bhagavan.
(1, 189, 2, 4, 351143) Bhagavan said, He wants to know how to turn the mind from sense enjoyments and realise that bliss which is said to be so much above sense enjoyments.
(1, 189, 2, 5, 351293) There is only one way, making the mind merge in That which is not sense enjoyment.
(1, 189, 2, 6, 351376) As you concentrate on That, the sense attractions will fall of their own accord.
(1, 189, 2, 7, 351457) Again, he asks, When can I attain that bliss? He is daily enjoying that bliss in sleep.
(1, 189, 2, 8, 351545) There, no sense object is present, and he still enjoys great bliss.
(1, 189, 2, 9, 351613) We have not got to attain bliss.
(1, 189, 2, 10, 351646) We are bliss.
(1, 189, 2, 11, 351660) Bliss is another name for us.
(1, 189, 2, 12, 351690) It is our nature.
(1, 189, 2, 13, 351708) All that we have to do is to turn the mind, draw it from the sense objects every time it goes towards them, and fix it in the Self.
(1, 189, 2, 14, 351840) He asks whether he will attain bliss after death.
(1, 189, 2, 15, 351890) There is no need to die to attain bliss.
(1, 189, 2, 16, 351931) Merging of the mind alone is necessary.
(1, 189, 2, 17, 351971) Death is also another name for us.
(1, 189, 2, 18, 352006) For what is death but giving up the body?
(1, 189, 2, 19, 352048) Our real nature is to be without the body.
(1, 189, 3, 20, 352091) After a pause Bhagavan added, The story of Indra and Ahalya in Yoga Vasishta strongly illustrates how, by the force of the mind being merged in one thing, all other things will cease to affect one.
(1, 189, 3, 21, 352289) There Ahalya, the wife of a king, falls in love with a rake called Indra and they passionately love each other.
(1, 189, 3, 22, 352401) The matter reached the kings ears and attains the magnitude of a great public scandal.
(1, 189, 3, 23, 352488) The king then orders the couple to be put through various cruel tortures.
(1, 189, 3, 24, 352562) But neither of them is affected by the tortures.
(1, 189, 3, 25, 352611) Their faces do not even show a twitch of pain but are blissfully smiling at each other.
(1, 189, 3, 26, 352699) The king, baffled by all this, asks them what the secret of their strength and resistance is.
(1, 189, 3, 27, 352793) They said, What!
(1, 189, 3, 28, 352810) dont you know?
(1, 190, 0, 1, 352825) looking at each other, and so engrossed are we with each other, that our mind has no room in it for any other thoughts.
(1, 190, 0, 2, 352945) So far as we are concerned, we two alone exist, each for the other, and nothing else exists.
(1, 190, 0, 3, 353038) How then can we be affected by other things? Such is the power of the merged mind.

(1, 190, 5, 9, 353984) A visitor said, In the Pondicherry Aurobindo Ashram it is said that the final stage of spiritual progress is to become the purushottama and it would seem that activity is predicated of that purushottama i.e., some vritti would seem to be associated with that state, whereas it is believed by other schools that cessation of all vrittis is liberation.
(1, 190, 6, 10, 354335) Bhagavan said, You say, all schools advise you to give up all vrittis so that you can reach your final goal, whether it is becoming purushottama or something else.
(1, 190, 6, 11, 354499) You must cease to be the three kinds of ordinary purusha i.e., the adhama, madhyama, uttama and become that purushottama.
(1, 190, 6, 12, 354621) This is
(1, 191, 0, 1, 354629) accepted.

(1, 191, 0, 8, 355425) I also advise it.
(1, 191, 0, 9, 355443) After making such surrender, i.e., complete surrender and not any partial or conditional surrender, you will be able to see for yourself whether there are two purushas, whether power comes from anywhere and gets into anywhere, etc. For we know nothing about God or any source from which power comes and gets into us.
(1, 191, 0, 10, 355760) All that is not known.
(1, 191, 0, 11, 355783) But I exist is known beyond all dispute by all men.
(1, 191, 0, 12, 355835) So let us know who that I is.
(1, 191, 0, 13, 355865) If, after knowing it, there still remain any doubts such as are now raised, it will be time enough then to try and clear such doubts.
(1, 191, 1, 14, 355999) From this point, the talk drifted to the various schools of thought, one saying there is only reality, others saying there are three eternal entities such as jagat, jiva and Ishwara, or pati, pasu and pasam.
(1, 191, 1, 15, 356207) In this connection, Bhagavan observed humorously, It is not at all correct to say that Advaitins or the Shankara school deny the existence of the world or that they call it unreal.
(1, 191, 1, 16, 356388) On the other hand, it is more real to them than to others.
(1, 191, 1, 17, 356447) Their world will always exist, whereas the world of the other schools will have origin, growth and decay and as such cannot be real.
(1, 191, 1, 18, 356580) Only, they say the world as world is not real, but that the world as Brahman is real.
(1, 191, 1, 19, 356666) All is Brahman, nothing exists but Brahman, and the world as Brahman is real.
(1, 191, 1, 20, 356744) In this way,
(1, 192, 0, 1, 356757) they claim they give more reality to the world than the other schools do.
(1, 192, 0, 2, 356831) For example, according to schools which believe in three entities, the jagat is only one third of the reality whereas according to Advaita, the world as Brahman is reality, the world and reality are not different.
(1, 192, 0, 3, 357045) Similarly, even to God or Brahman, the other schools give only one third sovereignty.
(1, 192, 0, 4, 357131) The other two entities necessarily limit the reality of God.
(1, 192, 0, 5, 357192) So, when Shankara is called mayavadi it may be retorted, Shankara says maya does not exist.
(1, 192, 0, 6, 357284) He who denies the existence of maya and calls it mithya or non existent cannot be called a mayavadi.
(1, 192, 0, 7, 357385) It is those who grant its existence and call its product, the world, a reality who should rightly be called mayavadis.
(1, 192, 0, 8, 357504) One who denies Ishwara is not called Ishwaravadi, but only one who affirms the existence of Ishwara. Bhagavan went on to add, All these are of course vain disputations.
(1, 192, 0, 9, 357673) There can be no end to such disputations.
(1, 192, 0, 10, 357715) The proper thing to do is to find out the I, about whose existence nobody has any doubt, and which alone persists when everything else vanishes, as during sleep, and then see if there is any room for such doubts or disputes.

(1, 194, 2, 13, 361679) In the afternoon Mr. Narayanaswamy Aiyars daughter, married to our Sundaresa Aiyars son, sang a few songs and then related the following miracle:
(1, 194, 3, 14, 361825) In Cawnpore, we are living on the third floor of a house and we are the only residents on that floor.
(1, 194, 3, 15, 361927) We have a tap there, but water rarely rises up to that level and we have daily to go down several flights of stairs and climb up with all the water necessary for us.
(1, 194, 3, 16, 362093) My husband used to do this work daily for me.
(1, 194, 3, 17, 362139) It was too much for him.
(1, 194, 3, 18, 362164) And I was too weak to be able to help him in this daily task.
(1, 194, 3, 19, 362226) One day, when I was alone in the house and my husband was in his office, I was pondering over this hard situation of ours and how we were to find a solution for this.
(1, 194, 3, 20, 362393) I had kept the empty vessel before the tap and was singing in a pensive mood.
(1, 194, 3, 21, 362471) Then I began singing the song Saranagati.
(1, 195, 0, 1, 362513) is a song well known among Bhagavans devotees.
(1, 195, 0, 2, 362560) It was composed by Mr. M.V. Ramaswami Aiyar and is sung by him and the members of his family whenever they want Bhagavan to interpose and avert evil from them or bring them good).
(1, 195, 0, 3, 362740) It says, in brief, We take shelter under you and you are our sole refuge.
(1, 195, 0, 4, 362814) Who else is there to whom we can turn?
(1, 195, 0, 5, 362853) If you delay to come to our rescue, we can bear it no longer.
(1, 195, 0, 6, 362915) So, come at once, end my misery, give me happiness! Then the water began to trickle down the tap and kept on flowing more as I went on with the song.
(1, 195, 0, 7, 363065) So I sang the song till all our vessels were filled with water.
(1, 195, 0, 8, 363129) When my husband returned home, he was surprised to find so much water and could not conceive how I could have got all that water.
(1, 195, 0, 9, 363259) Then I told him, I have discovered now a secret device for getting water.
(1, 195, 0, 10, 363333) If I sing Saranagati I can get water. My husband naturally could not believe it and so I tried the same device again in his presence and the water flowed from the tap.
(1, 195, 0, 11, 363501) Ever since then, my water problem has ceased.
(1, 195, 0, 12, 363547) I had only to sing Saranagati, and water will flow from the tap.
(1, 195, 0, 13, 363612) I have tried other songs.
(1, 195, 0, 14, 363638) But they dont give the same result.
(1, 195, 0, 15, 363674) Afterwards, when I fell ill and father came to see me, I told him about this and he too could not believe it, till I again repeated the experiment before him and he saw it succeeded.
(1, 195, 0, 16, 363857) He asked me to try other songs.
(1, 195, 0, 17, 363889) But none of them produced the same result. The girl told all this with great glee and there was such a ring of truth about the whole narration that I consider it would be absurd to doubt the truth of the experience.

(1, 197, 4, 17, 367900) A visitor had given Bhagavan a piece of paper on which he had scribbled in pencil a number of questions.
(1, 197, 4, 18, 368005) When I went into the hall about 3 p.m., Bhagavan was trying to decipher them and turning round to me said, Here is a question paper.
(1, 197, 5, 19, 368138) Question 1: How to get rid of credulousness?
(1, 197, 5, 20, 368183) The visitors problem was that he starts with some ideal recommended to him, but when others come and recommend other ideals, he feels inclined to believe them and give up his old ideals.
(1, 198, 0, 1, 368370) Bhagavan: Yes.
(1, 198, 0, 2, 368385) Our whole trouble is that we are credulous.
(1, 198, 0, 3, 368429) We believe in everything except the reality.
(1, 198, 0, 4, 368474) We must give up all our false beliefs, and that is the only thing we have to do.
(1, 198, 0, 5, 368555) Then the reality will shine by itself.
(1, 198, 1, 6, 368594) Question 2: I start with great keenness towards some ideal.
(1, 198, 1, 7, 368654) But gradually I get slack.
(1, 198, 1, 8, 368681) What should I do to prevent it, and what is the reason for this happening?
(1, 198, 2, 9, 368756) Bhagavan: Just as there must have been a reason for your keenness at one time, there must be a reason for getting slack also later on.
(1, 198, 3, 10, 368891) Question 3: There are a number of spiritual teachers, teaching various paths.
(1, 198, 3, 11, 368969) Whom should one take for ones Guru?
(1, 198, 4, 12, 369005) Bhagavan: Choose that one where you find you get shanti or peace.
(1, 198, 5, 13, 369071) Question 4: What is the best way of dealing with desires, with a view to getting rid of them  satisfying them or suppressing them?
(1, 198, 6, 14, 369202) Bhagavan: If a desire can be got rid of by satisfying it, there will be no harm in satisfying such a desire.
(1, 198, 6, 15, 369311) But desires generally are not eradicated by satisfaction.
(1, 198, 6, 16, 369369) Trying to root them out that way is like pouring spirits to quench fire.
(1, 198, 6, 17, 369442) At the same time, the proper remedy is not forcible suppression, since such repression is bound to react sooner or later into forceful surging up with undesirable consequences.
(1, 198, 6, 18, 369619) The proper way to get rid of a desire is to find out Who gets the desire?
(1, 198, 6, 19, 369693) What is its source? When this is found, the desire is rooted out and it will never again emerge or grow.
(1, 198, 6, 20, 369798) Small desires such as the desire to eat, drink and sleep and attend to calls of nature, though these may also be classed among desires, you can safely satisfy.
(1, 198, 6, 21, 369958) They will not implant vasanas in your mind, necessitating further birth.
(1, 198, 6, 22, 370031) Those activities are just necessary to carry on life and are not likely to develop or leave behind vasanas or tendencies.
(1, 199, 0, 1, 370153) a general rule, therefore, there is no harm in satisfying a desire where the satisfaction will not lead to further desires by creating vasanas in the mind.
(1, 199, 1, 2, 370309) Question 5: What is the meaning of Om?
(1, 199, 2, 3, 370348) Bhagavan: Om is everything.
(1, 199, 2, 4, 370376) It is another name for Brahmam.
(1, 199, 3, 5, 370408) I was looking into the January issue of Vision and came across a story about Kulasekhara Alwar.
(1, 199, 3, 6, 370504) Having heard during a kalakshepam that Ravana had taken away Sita, Kulasekhara identified himself so much with the situation in the story that he thought it was his duty as a worshipper of Rama at once to hasten to Lanka and release Sita, that he ran up and had entered the sea to cross over to Lanka, that then Rama appeared with Sita and Lakshmana showered His grace on him.
(1, 199, 3, 7, 370881) I remembered another version, that Kulasekhara started on a campaign with his army to succour Rama, that meanwhile the Bhagavatar doing the kalakshepam, sensing the situation, passed on at once to Rama emerging victoriously from the battle, killing all his enemies, etc.
(1, 199, 3, 8, 371152) Bhagavan also thought the version I had in mind was the correct one and that the matter referred to Ramas battle with Khara and Dushana and not with Ravana for Sita.
(1, 199, 3, 9, 371318) Bhagavan looked up a history of the Alwars and told us that both incidents are found in Kulasekharas life.
(1, 199, 3, 10, 371425) This led me to make the following remark, Some Maratha Saint also did a similar thing.
(1, 199, 3, 11, 371512) He leaped up to the roof, I think. Thereupon, Dr. S. Rao asked Bhagavan, I dont know that story.
(1, 199, 3, 12, 371609) What is that story? Thereupon Bhagavan said, Ekanath was writing the Ramayana and when he came to the portion in which he was graphically describing that Hanuman jumped across the ocean to Lanka, he so identified himself with his hero Hanuman, that unconsciously he leaped into the air and landed on the roof of his neighbour.
(1, 199, 3, 13, 371936) This neighbour had always a poor opinion of Ekanath, taking him for a humbug and religious hypocrite.
(1, 199, 3, 14, 372038) He heard a thud on his roof and, coming out to see what it was,
(1, 200, 0, 1, 372102) discovered Ekanath lying down on the roof with the cadjan leaf in one hand and his iron stile in the other, and the cadjan leaf had verses describing how Hanuman leapt across the sea.
(1, 200, 0, 2, 372286) This incident proved to the neighbour what a genuine bhakta Ekanath was and he became his disciple.
(1, 200, 1, 3, 372386) After a pause, Bhagavan also related, God appeared in a dream to Ekanath and asked him to go and repair the tomb of Jnaneswar.
(1, 200, 1, 4, 372513) When Ekanath went there accordingly, he found a contractor ready to do all the work and take payment at the end.
(1, 200, 1, 5, 372626) The contractor opened a big account, in which all expenses were entered, with the names of all the workmen and wages paid to them.
(1, 200, 1, 6, 372757) Everything went on systematically and when the work of repairs having been completed, the accounts had to be looked into and the contractor paid his dues, the contractor and his big account book totally disappeared.
(1, 200, 1, 7, 372973) Then alone Ekanath came to know God was his contractor and did the work.
(1, 200, 1, 8, 373046) Such things have happened.

(1, 201, 3, 14, 375003) Nagamma came into the hall and prostrated herself before Bhagavan, after having gone round the hall a few times.

(1, 201, 3, 19, 375280) If one goes round like that, everybody who comes here thinks Apparently the proper thing here is to go round and starts going round.
(1, 201, 3, 20, 375413) Thus all people go round.
(1, 201, 3, 21, 375439) After all, the proper pradakshina is going round the Self, or, more accurately, to realise that we are the Self and that within us all the countless spheres revolve, going round and round, as described in the following stanza of Ribhu Gita (3rd Chapter, 39th Verse).

(1, 202, 2, 3, 375848) An English translation of this stanza is as follows:
(1, 202, 3, 4, 375901) Reflecting I am the all blissful Self Is worship as with words and flowers.
(1, 202, 3, 5, 375977) True circumambulation is the thought, In me the million universes roll, He who knows all beings bow to him And he to none, He bows before the Mahalinga Self.
(1, 202, 4, 6, 376135) Some go on doing a number of namaskarams, e.g.
(1, 202, 4, 7, 376182) that Janaki, she goes on striking her head down countless times along with namaskarams.
(1, 202, 4, 8, 376270) She goes round a number of times.
(1, 202, 4, 9, 376304) At each window she falls down and does a number of namaskarams.
(1, 202, 4, 10, 376368) However much I tell her, she wont leave off such practices. Somebody here interjected, It seems she is known to Bhagavan since her childhood. Bhagavan said, Yes, yes, and continued, There are others who come and fall before me while I am moving.

(1, 202, 4, 14, 376790) After all, true namaskaram is only the giving up the I sense, or killing the ego.
(1, 202, 5, 15, 376872) I said, Bhagavan himself advises us to go round the Hill, for instance.
(1, 202, 5, 16, 376944) I know Bhagavan is also not against going round the image in a temple.

(1, 203, 0, 1, 377236) going round is going round yourself, or the bhava expressed in the verse quoted.
(1, 203, 0, 2, 377317) The other pradakshinams are not condemned.
(1, 203, 0, 3, 377360) The jnani, though he knows that meditation on the Self is the best worship, will join in all the other kinds of worship for the good of others and as an example to them.
(1, 203, 0, 4, 377530) In fact, he may observe all the other ways even more correctly and steadfastly than those who follow only those paths and know nothing of jnana.
(1, 203, 0, 5, 377675) That is referred to in the following verse, also occurring in Ribhu Gita.

(1, 206, 4, 5, 383248) Mr. Nanavati of Bombay asked Bhagavan, In the fifth stanza of Arunachala Pancharatna reference is made to seeing Your form in everything.
(1, 206, 4, 6, 383386) What is the form referred to? Bhagavan said, The stanza says that one should completely surrender ones mind, turn it inwards and see you the Self within and then see the Self in you in everything.
(1, 206, 4, 7, 383583) It is only after seeing the Self within that one will be able to see the Self in everything.
(1, 206, 4, 8, 383676) One must first realise there is nothing but the Self and that he is that Self, and then only he can see everything as the form of the Self.
(1, 206, 4, 9, 383816) That is the meaning of saying, See the Self in everything and everything in the Self, as is stated in the Gita and other books.
(1, 206, 4, 10, 383944) It is the same truth that is taught in stanza 4 of the Reality in Forty Verses.
(1, 206, 4, 11, 384024) If you have the idea that you are something with form, that you are limited by this body, and that being within this body you have to see through these eyes, God and the world also will appear to you as form.
(1, 206, 4, 12, 384233) If you realise you are without form, that you are unlimited, that you alone exist, that you are the eye, the infinite eye, what is there to be seen apart from the infinite eye?
(1, 206, 4, 13, 384410) Apart from the eye, there is nothing to be seen.
(1, 206, 4, 14, 384459) There must be a seer for an object to be seen, and there must be space, time, etc.
(1, 206, 4, 15, 384542) But if the Self alone exists, it is both seer and seen, and above seeing or being seen.

(1, 207, 3, 11, 386427) A Muslim visitor put some questions and got the following answers:

(1, 208, 1, 2, 386767) Question: It is said the Lords light resides in the eye.
(1, 208, 2, 3, 386824) Answer: The eye does not see.

(1, 208, 3, 5, 386948) Question: The Lord has created all this, has He not?
(1, 208, 3, 6, 387001) What was created first?
(1, 208, 3, 7, 387025) It is said light or sound was created first.
(1, 208, 4, 8, 387070) Answer: All these things, which you say have been created have to be seen by you before you say they exist.
(1, 208, 4, 9, 387178) There must be a seer.
(1, 208, 4, 10, 387200) If you find out who that seer is, then you will know about creation and which was created first.
(1, 208, 4, 11, 387297) Of course various theories as to what came into existence first from God are given out.
(1, 208, 4, 12, 387385) Most, including scientists, agree that all has come from light and sound.
(1, 208, 5, 13, 387459) Question: Can we call anything created, like this piece of wood, for example, God?
(1, 208, 5, 14, 387542) It is said it is very wrong to do so.
(1, 208, 6, 15, 387580) Answer: Even this piece of wood, does it exist apart from God?
(1, 208, 6, 16, 387643) Can we confine God to any time or place, since He is everywhere and in everything?
(1, 208, 6, 17, 387726) We should not see anything as apart from God.
(1, 208, 6, 18, 387772) That is all.

(1, 212, 2, 19, 395433) A visitor asked Bhagavan, When I try to be without all thoughts, I pass into sleep.
(1, 212, 2, 20, 395517) What should I do about it?
(1, 212, 3, 21, 395544) Bhagavan: Once you go to sleep, you can do nothing in that state.
(1, 212, 3, 22, 395610) But while you are awake, try to keep away all thoughts.
(1, 212, 3, 23, 395666) Why think about sleep?
(1, 212, 3, 24, 395689) Even that is a thought, is it not?

(1, 212, 3, 26, 395803) When you pass into sleep, that state, in
(1, 213, 0, 1, 395844) which you were before falling asleep, will continue and again, when you wake up, you will continue from where you had left off when you fell into slumber.
(1, 213, 0, 2, 395999) So long as there are thoughts of activity, so long would there be sleep also.
(1, 213, 0, 3, 396077) Thought and sleep are counterparts of one and the same thing.
(1, 213, 1, 4, 396139) Bhagavan quoted the Gita and said, We should not sleep very much or go without it altogether, but sleep only moderately.
(1, 213, 1, 5, 396260) To prevent too much sleep, we must try and have no thoughts or chalana (movement of the mind), we must eat only sattvic food and that only in moderate measure, and not indulge in too much physical activity.
(1, 213, 1, 6, 396467) The more we control thought, activity and food the more shall we be able to control sleep.
(1, 213, 1, 7, 396558) But moderation ought to be the rule, as explained in the Gita, for the sadhak on the path.
(1, 213, 1, 8, 396649) Sleep is the first obstacle, as explained in the books, for all sadhaks.
(1, 213, 1, 9, 396722) The second obstacle is said to be vikshepa or the sense objects of the world which divert ones attention.
(1, 213, 1, 10, 396828) The third is said to be kashaya or thoughts in the mind about previous experiences with sense objects.
(1, 213, 1, 11, 396931) The fourth, ananda, is also called an obstacle, because in that state a feeling of separation from the source of ananda, enabling the enjoyer to say I am enjoying ananda is present.
(1, 213, 1, 12, 397113) Even this has to be surmounted and the final stage of samadhana or samadhi has to be reached, where one becomes ananda or one with the reality and the duality of enjoyer and enjoyment ceases in the ocean of sat chit ananda or the Self.

(1, 220, 2, 9, 409557) In answer to a visitor, Bhagavan said, Find out to whom is Viyoga.
(1, 220, 2, 10, 409624) That is yoga.

(1, 220, 3, 16, 410450) He read out passages from a Tamil book called @jYR DiU (The Truth of Advaita) in which all doubts about the state of the jivanmukta are raised and answered.
(1, 220, 3, 17, 410607) Then he said:
(1, 220, 4, 18, 410621) Various illustrations are given in books to enable us to understand how the jnani can live and act without the mind,
(1, 221, 0, 1, 410738) although living and acting require the use of the mind.
(1, 221, 0, 2, 410794) The potters wheel goes on turning round even after the potter has ceased to turn it because the pot is finished.
(1, 221, 0, 3, 410907) In the same way, the electric fan goes on revolving for some minutes after we switch off the current.
(1, 221, 0, 4, 411009) The prarabdha which created the body will make it go through whatever activities it was meant for.
(1, 221, 0, 5, 411108) But the jnani goes through all these activities without the notion that he is the doer of them.
(1, 221, 0, 6, 411204) It is hard to understand how this is possible.
(1, 221, 0, 7, 411251) The illustration generally given is that the jnani performs actions in some such way as a child that is roused from sleep to eat, eats but does not remember next morning that it ate.
(1, 221, 0, 8, 411434) It has to be remembered that all these explanations are not for the jnani.
(1, 221, 0, 9, 411509) He knows and has no doubts.
(1, 221, 0, 10, 411537) He knows that he is not the body and is not doing anything even though his body may be engaged in some activity.
(1, 221, 0, 11, 411650) These explanations are for the onlookers who think of the jnani as one with a body and cannot help identifying him with his body.
(1, 221, 1, 12, 411780) There are various controversies or schools of thought as to whether a jnani can continue to live in his physical body after realization.
(1, 221, 1, 13, 411917) Some hold that one who dies cannot be a jnani, because his body must vanish into air, or some such thing.
(1, 221, 1, 14, 412023) They put forward all sorts of funny notions.
(1, 221, 1, 15, 412068) If a man must at once leave his body when he realises the Self, I wonder how any knowledge of the Self or the state of realisation can come down to other men.
(1, 221, 1, 16, 412227) And that would mean that all those who have given us the fruits of their Self realisation in books cannot be considered jnanis because they went on living after realisation.
(1, 221, 1, 17, 412401) And if it is held that a man cannot be considered a jnani so long as he performs actions in the world (and action is impossible without the mind), then not only the great Sages who carried on various kinds of work after attaining jnana must not be considered jnanis, but the gods also, and Ishwara Himself, since He continues looking after the world.
(1, 221, 1, 18, 412752) The fact is that any amount of action can be performed, and performed quite well, by the
(1, 222, 0, 1, 412841) jnani without his identifying himself with it in any way or ever imagining that he is the doer.
(1, 222, 0, 2, 412937) Some power acts through his body and uses his body to get the work done.
(1, 222, 1, 3, 413010) Bhagavan has said the same on previous occasions also.
(1, 222, 1, 4, 413065) He continued to speak about mukti and said, Mukti is not anything to be attained.
(1, 222, 1, 5, 413147) It is our real nature.
(1, 222, 1, 6, 413170) We are always That.
(1, 222, 1, 7, 413190) It is only so long as one feels that he is in bondage that he has to try to get released from bondage.
(1, 222, 1, 8, 413293) When a man feels that he is in bondage he tries to find out for whom is the bondage and by that enquiry discovers that there is no bondage for him but only for the mind, and that the mind itself disappears or proves non existent when turned inwards instead of outwards towards sense objects; it merges into its source, the Self, and ceases to exist as a separate entity.
(1, 222, 1, 9, 413664) In that state there is no feeling either of bondage or liberation.
(1, 222, 1, 10, 413731) So long as one speaks of mukti he is not free from the sense of bondage.
(1, 222, 2, 11, 413804) The visitor who had asked about yoga in the morning now pursued his questions further.
(1, 222, 3, 12, 413891) Visitor: I did not quite grasp all that Bhagavan said this morning.
(1, 222, 3, 13, 413959) What am I to do when the mind strays in various directions during dhyana?
(1, 222, 4, 14, 414033) Bhagavan: Simply draw the mind back each time it strays and fix it in dhyana.
(1, 222, 4, 15, 414111) There is no other way.
(1, 222, 4, 16, 414134) (Bhagavan also quoted Chapter VI, Verse 26 from the Bhagavad Gita which says the same thing).
(1, 222, 5, 17, 414228) Visitor: Then is there no use in pranayama (breath control)?
(1, 222, 5, 18, 414289) Should I not practise it?
(1, 222, 6, 19, 414315) Bhagavan: Pranayama is also a help.
(1, 222, 6, 20, 414351) It is one of the various methods that are intended to help us attain ekagratha or one pointedness of mind.
(1, 222, 6, 21, 414458) Pranayama can also help to control the wandering mind and attain this one pointedness and therefore it can be used.
(1, 222, 6, 22, 414574) But one should not stop there.
(1, 223, 0, 1, 414605) After obtaining control of the mind through pranayama one should not rest content with any experiences which may accrue therefrom but should harness the controlled mind to the question Who am I? till the mind merges in the Self.
(1, 223, 1, 2, 414834) The visitor further asked whether in his meditation he could use forms and images of God and mantras.
(1, 223, 2, 3, 414936) Bhagavan: Yes, of course.
(1, 223, 2, 4, 414962) All these things can help, or why should they be recommended in the books?
(1, 223, 2, 5, 415037) Various things are prescribed to suit various natures.
(1, 223, 2, 6, 415092) Each person must choose what seems easiest and appeals to him most.

(1, 224, 2, 3, 416443) In the afternoon there was the following talk with a young sadhu from North India: Sadhu: I want to know who I am.
(1, 224, 2, 4, 416558) The Arya Samajists say that I am the jivatma and that if I purify the mind and buddhi I can see God.
(1, 224, 2, 5, 416659) I dont know what to do.
(1, 224, 2, 6, 416683) If Bhagavan thinks fit, will Bhagavan please tell me what to do?
(1, 224, 2, 7, 416748) Bhagavan: You have used a number of terms.
(1, 224, 2, 8, 416791) What do you mean by jivatma, mind, buddhi and God?
(1, 224, 2, 9, 416842) And where is God and where are you that you should want to go and see God?
(1, 224, 3, 10, 416917) Sadhu: I dont know what all these terms mean.
(1, 224, 4, 11, 416963) Bhagavan: Then never mind what the Arya Samajists tell you.
(1, 224, 4, 12, 417023) You dont know about God and other things, but you do know that you exist.
(1, 224, 4, 13, 417097) You can have no doubt about that.
(1, 224, 4, 14, 417131) So find out who you are.
(1, 224, 5, 15, 417156) Sadhu: That is what I want to know.
(1, 224, 5, 16, 417192) How can I find out?
(1, 224, 6, 17, 417212) Bhagavan: Keep all other thoughts away and try to find out in what place in your body the I arises.
(1, 224, 7, 18, 417312) Sadhu: But I am unable to think about this.
(1, 224, 8, 19, 417356) Bhagavan: Why?
(1, 224, 8, 20, 417371) If you can think about other things you can think about I and where in your body it arises.
(1, 224, 8, 21, 417463) If you mean that other thoughts distract you, the only way is to draw your mind back each time it strays and fix it on the I.
(1, 224, 8, 22, 417589) As each thought arises, ask yourself: To whom is this thought? The answer will be, to me; then hold on to that me.
(1, 224, 9, 23, 417704) Sadhu: Am I to keep on repeating Who am I? so as to make a mantra of it?
(1, 225, 0, 1, 417777) Bhagavan: No.
(1, 225, 0, 2, 417791) Who am I? is not a mantra.
(1, 225, 0, 3, 417818) It means that you must find out where in you arises the I thought which is the source of all other thoughts.
(1, 225, 0, 4, 417927) But if you find this vichara marga too hard for you, you can go on repeating I, I and that will lead you to the same goal.
(1, 225, 0, 5, 418050) There is no harm in using I as a mantra.
(1, 225, 0, 6, 418091) It is the first name of God.
(1, 225, 1, 7, 418120) God is everywhere, but it is difficult to conceive Him in that aspect, so the books have said, God is everywhere.
(1, 225, 1, 8, 418234) He is also within you.
(1, 225, 1, 9, 418257) You are Brahman. So remind yourself: I am Brahman.
(1, 225, 1, 10, 418308) The repetition of I will eventually lead you to realise I am Brahman.

(1, 225, 3, 12, 418386) A young man called Krishna Jivrajani from Karachi said, When I reach the thoughtless stage in my sadhana I enjoy a certain pleasure, but sometimes I also experience a vague fear which I cannot properly describe.
(1, 225, 4, 13, 418598) Bhagavan: You may experience anything, but you should never rest content with that.
(1, 225, 4, 14, 418682) Whether you feel pleasure or fear, ask yourself who feels the pleasure or the fear and so carry on the sadhana until pleasure and fear are both transcended and all duality ceases and the Reality alone remains.
(1, 225, 5, 15, 418892) There is nothing wrong in such things happening or being experienced, but you must never stop at that.
(1, 225, 5, 16, 418995) For instance, you must never rest content with the pleasure of laya experienced when thought is quelled but must press on until all duality ceases.

(1, 226, 1, 15, 420595) As Nayana used to say: In going forward one can run any distance at any speed, but when it is a question of going backward, that is turning inwards, even one step is hard to take.
(1, 226, 2, 16, 420775) Somehow it never occurs to me to write any book or compose poems.
(1, 226, 2, 17, 420841) All the songs I have made were made at the request of someone or other in connection with some particular event.
(1, 226, 2, 18, 420954) Even the Reality in Forty Verses, of which so many commentaries and translations now exist, was not planned as a book but consists of verses composed at different times and afterwards arranged as a book by Muruganar and others.
(1, 226, 2, 19, 421182) The only poems that came to me spontaneously and compelled me, as it were, to compose them, without anyone urging me to do so, are the Eight Verses to Arunachala and the Eleven Verses to Arunachala.
(1, 226, 2, 20, 421381) The first day the opening words of the Eleven Verses suddenly came to me one morning, and even if I tried to suppress them, saying, What have I to do with these words? they would not be suppressed till I composed a song beginning with them,
(1, 227, 0, 1, 421622) and all the words flowed easily without any effort.
(1, 227, 0, 2, 421674) In the same way the second stanza was made the next day and the succeeding ones the following days, one each day.

(1, 230, 3, 20, 428489) L.N. Sastri, who had taken leave of Bhagavan on the 8th, returned today.

(1, 231, 0, 1, 428724) Pudukottai Pundit had, and Bhagavan said: He also would have explained them if you had asked him. So today I asked him, and at about 3 oclock in the afternoon he gave the gist of the poems as follows:
(1, 231, 1, 2, 428925) You, Bhagavan have realized the Self, turning away from the world and going inwards into yourself.
(1, 231, 1, 3, 429024) You have come into the world for its benefit and uplift.
(1, 231, 1, 4, 429081) I am always going out, attracted by the world and its objects; nor is there anything strange in this, since God has given me the senses and sense organs, between which and the things of the world he has created a natural and irresistible attraction.
(1, 231, 1, 5, 429331) It is not possible to escape from this without the aid of a Guru who has himself escaped.
(1, 231, 1, 6, 429421) I have been in search of a Guru, and today it has at last been my lot to come face to face with one, and I feel that today all my misery is ended.
(1, 231, 1, 7, 429568) I have read books about the Self but had no actual experience.
(1, 231, 1, 8, 429631) It is for you, endowed, as the great ones have said, with the nature and power of Lord Subrahmanya, as the embodiment of tenderness and mercy, come here for the uplift and enlightenment of the world, to take me up and bless me and save me, as I surrender myself completely to you.

(1, 232, 1, 2, 430620) At 11 oclock this morning, the Asramam lunch time, Boses mother brought various dishes that she had specially prepared for Bhagavan and was serving them herself.
(1, 232, 1, 3, 430782) She has brought food like this a number of times during recent weeks, and it means a good deal of cooking, since Bhagavan will not take anything unless there is enough for all to partake of it alike.
(1, 232, 1, 4, 430982) Bhagavan asked me to tell her not to take all this trouble and to say that it was work enough to prepare food for her family and it was unnecessary to send things for so many people.

(1, 232, 1, 7, 431353) All food is the same to me.

(1, 232, 1, 9, 431594) Time was when I took pleasure in variety, but after realizing unity all that disappeared.

(1, 232, 3, 11, 431724) In answer to a visitor Bhagavan made the following remarks:
(1, 232, 4, 12, 431784) You can have, or rather you will yourself be, the highest imaginable kind of happiness.
(1, 232, 4, 13, 431872) All other kinds of happiness which you have spoken of as pleasure, joy, happiness, bliss are only reflections of the ananda which, in your true nature, you are.
(1, 232, 5, 14, 432033) You need not bother about the lights which you say you see around things and people.
(1, 232, 5, 15, 432118) Whether lights are seen or sounds are heard or whatever may happen, never let go the enquiry Who am I? Keep on asking inwardly: Who sees these lights or hears these sounds?
(1, 232, 6, 16, 432291) What do you mean by taking sannyasa?
(1, 232, 6, 17, 432328) Do you think it means leaving your home or wearing robes of a certain
(1, 233, 0, 1, 432398) colour?
(1, 233, 0, 2, 432406) Wherever you go, even if you fly up into the air, will your mind not go with you?
(1, 233, 0, 3, 432488) Or can you leave it behind you and go without it?

(1, 234, 2, 10, 434971) Then I said that the stomach had more cause to complain against us than we against it.
(1, 234, 2, 11, 435058) It can be expected to work but it should be given some rest too and after taking rest it can work again.

(1, 234, 2, 14, 435428) So it has just cause for complaint.
(1, 234, 2, 15, 435464) That is why I composed a stanza like that.

(1, 235, 1, 2, 436204) When I entered the hall in the afternoon Bhagavan was already explaining in answer to some questions put by Mr. Poonja, a Punjabi:
(1, 235, 2, 3, 436335) I ask you to see where the I arises in your body, but it is really not quite correct to say that the I rises from and merges in the heart in the right side of the chest.
(1, 235, 2, 4, 436505) The heart is another name for the Reality and it is neither inside nor outside the body; there can be no in or out for it, since it alone is.
(1, 235, 2, 5, 436647) I do not mean by heart any physiological organ or any plexus of nerves or anything like that, but so long as one identifies oneself with the body and thinks he is in the body he is advised to see where in the body the I thought rises and merges again.
(1, 235, 2, 6, 436899) It must be the heart at the right side of the chest since every man, of whatever race and religion and in whatever language he may be saying I, points to the right side of the chest to indicate himself.
(1, 235, 2, 7, 437102) This is so all over the world, so that must be the place.
(1, 235, 2, 8, 437160) And by keenly watching the daily emergence of the I thought on waking and its subsiding in sleep, one can see that it is in the heart on the right side.
(1, 235, 3, 9, 437313) In the course of the day, G.V. Subbaramayya asked Bhagavan how Ganapati Sastri wrote his Ramana Gita, whether he took notes on the conversations and then wrote them out.
(1, 235, 3, 10, 437483) Bhagavan replied, Remembering such talks was childs play to him.
(1, 235, 3, 11, 437548) He could listen to a long and learned lecture on some intricate subject and then at the end reproduce the gist of it accurately in the form of sutras, not omitting anything of importance that had been said.
(1, 235, 3, 12, 437755) Once he and Arunachala Sastri, who was also a learned man, had a discussion.
(1, 235, 3, 13, 437832) Ganapati Sastri took up the position of drishti srishti, that we create and then see, that is to say that the world has no objective reality apart from our minds, while Arunachala Sastri took up the opposite view of srishti drishti,
(1, 236, 0, 1, 438065) that creation exists objectively before we see it.
(1, 236, 0, 2, 438116) Arunachala Sastri argued first and upheld his standpoint with a great display of logic and learning and many quotations.
(1, 236, 0, 3, 438237) Then Ganapati Sastri wrote down in the form of sutras all that he had maintained and asked him whether the sutras gave a faithful summary of everything he had said.
(1, 236, 0, 4, 438402) He agreed that they did, so Ganapati Sastri said: Then now you will have my criticism and condemnation of it.
(1, 236, 0, 5, 438512) He then expounded very ably the advaitic point of view, that the world is an illusion as world but real as Brahman, that it does not exist as world but exists and is real as Brahman.
(1, 236, 0, 6, 438695) In the same way he could record any discussion he heard; so remarkable was his power of memory, that he must have reproduced the Ramana Gita in that way.
(1, 236, 0, 7, 438849) It would have been mere childs play for him.

(1, 239, 3, 6, 444185) Bose: When the Upanishads say that all is Brahman, how can we say, like Shankara, that this world is mithya or illusory?
(1, 239, 4, 7, 444306) Bhagavan: Shankara also said that this world is Brahman or the Self.
(1, 239, 4, 8, 444375) What he objected to is ones imagining that the Self is limited by the names and forms that constitute the world.
(1, 239, 4, 9, 444488) He only said that the world does not exist apart from Brahman.
(1, 239, 4, 10, 444551) Brahman or the Self is like the screen and the world is like the pictures on it.
(1, 239, 4, 11, 444632) You can see the picture only so long as there is a screen.
(1, 239, 4, 12, 444691) But when the seer himself becomes the screen only the Self remains.
(1, 239, 4, 13, 444759) Kaivalya Navaneeta has asked and answered six questions about maya.
(1, 239, 4, 14, 444827) They are instructive.
(1, 239, 5, 15, 444849) The first question is: What is maya?
(1, 239, 5, 16, 444886) And the answer is: It is anirvachaniya or indescribable.
(1, 239, 6, 17, 444943) The second question is: To whom does it come?
(1, 239, 6, 18, 444989) And the answer is: To the mind or ego who feels that he is a separate entity, who thinks: I do this or this is mine.
(1, 240, 0, 1, 445106) The third question is: Where does it come from and how did it originate?
(1, 240, 0, 2, 445179) And the answer is: Nobody can say.
(1, 240, 1, 3, 445214) The fourth question is: How did it arise?
(1, 240, 1, 4, 445256) And the answer is: Through non vichara, through failure to ask: who am I?
(1, 240, 2, 5, 445330) The fifth question is: If the Self and maya both exist does not this invalidate the theory of Advaita?
(1, 240, 2, 6, 445433) The answer is: It need not, since maya is dependent on the Self as the picture is on the screen.
(1, 240, 2, 7, 445530) The picture is not real in the sense that the screen is real.
(1, 240, 3, 8, 445592) The sixth question is: If the Self and maya are one, could it not be argued that the Self is of the nature of maya, that is illusory?
(1, 240, 3, 9, 445726) And the answer is: No; the Self can be capable of producing illusion without being illusory.
(1, 240, 3, 10, 445819) A conjuror may create for our entertainment the illusion of people, animals and things, and we see all of them as clearly as we see him; but after the performance he alone remains and all the visions he had created have disappeared.
(1, 240, 3, 11, 446052) He is not a part of the illusion but is real and solid.
(1, 240, 4, 12, 446108) 30 5 46 30 5 46 30 5 46 30 5 46 30 5 46
(1, 240, 5, 13, 446148) Today again Bose reverted to the subject of maya and asked Bhagavan, What is Hiranyagarbha?
(1, 240, 6, 14, 446240) Bhagavan replied, Hiranyagarbha is only another name for the sukshma sarira or Ishwara.
(1, 240, 6, 15, 446328) The books use the following illustration to help explain creation.
(1, 240, 6, 16, 446395) The Self is like the canvas for a painting.
(1, 240, 6, 17, 446439) First a paste is smeared over it to close up the small holes that are in any cloth.
(1, 240, 6, 18, 446523) This paste can be compared to the antaryami in all creation.
(1, 240, 6, 19, 446584) Then the artist makes an outline on the canvas, and this can be compared to the sukshma sarira of all creation, for instance the light and sound, nada, bindu, out of which all things arise.
(1, 240, 6, 20, 446774) Then the artist paints his picture with colours etc., in this outline, and this can be compared to the gross forms that constitute the world.

(1, 241, 3, 13, 448048) I have sometimes received stale gruel at some house and taken it without salt or any other flavouring, in the open street, before great pandits and other important men who used to come and prostrate themselves before me at my Asramam, then wiped my hands on my head and passed on supremely happy and in a state of mind in which even emperors were mere straw in my sight.
(1, 241, 3, 14, 448419) You cant imagine it.

(1, 241, 4, 16, 448563) In illustration of this, Bhagavan told us a story of a king who renounced his throne and went begging, first outside the limits of his State, then in his own State, then in its capital city, and finally in the royal palace itself, and thus at last got rid of his ego sense.
(1, 241, 4, 17, 448837) After some time, when he was wandering as an ascetic in another State, he was chosen to be its king and accepted because
(1, 242, 0, 1, 448958) now that he had completely lost the sense of I he could act any part in life as a mere witness and the cares of kingship no longer worried him.
(1, 242, 0, 2, 449102) When his own former State heard of it, they also asked him to resume his kingship, and he did so, because however many kingdoms he might rule over, he realized now that he was not the doer but simply an instrument in Gods hands.

(1, 242, 4, 19, 450538) However, the wrong one was reported dead, and the result was that the mother who had lost her son went about as cheerful as ever, while the one who had still got her son was weeping and lamenting.
(1, 242, 4, 20, 450735) So it is not any object or condition that causes grief but only our thought about it.
(1, 242, 4, 21, 450821) Your son came from the Self and
(1, 243, 0, 1, 450853) was absorbed back into the Self.

(1, 244, 0, 1, 452722) liked and then put me back to bed, and I would know nothing about it until they told me in the morning.
(1, 244, 1, 2, 452826) I said, It would seem that even in those days Bhagavans sleep was not ordinary sleep but some state like samadhi.
(1, 244, 2, 3, 452940) Bhagavan: I dont know what state it was, but that is the fact.
(1, 244, 2, 4, 453003) Some who have written about my life have called it somnambulism.
(1, 244, 3, 5, 453068) I: It was certainly not somnambulism; that is walking in ones sleep.
(1, 244, 3, 6, 453137) This was more like samadhi or absorption in the Self.
(1, 244, 4, 7, 453191) In the evening Bose asked, Is it good to do japa and puja and so on when we know that enquiry into the Self is the real thing?
(1, 244, 5, 8, 453318) Bhagavan: All are good.
(1, 244, 5, 9, 453342) They will lead to this eventually.
(1, 244, 5, 10, 453377) Japa is our real nature.
(1, 244, 5, 11, 453402) When we realize the Self then japa goes on without effort.
(1, 244, 5, 12, 453461) What is the means at one stage becomes the goal at another.
(1, 244, 5, 13, 453521) When effortless, constant japa goes on, it is realisation.

(1, 244, 11, 19, 453841) When Bhagavan returned from his morning walk at about 7 45, the attendant Sivananda offered to massage his legs.
(1, 244, 11, 20, 453954) Bhagavan forbade him and said: If I let them they go on massaging for a long time.
(1, 244, 11, 21, 454037) This morning too, at parayana, I did not let them.
(1, 244, 11, 22, 454088) They begin with the parayana and dont stop till it is finished, and sometimes I am unaware of it.
(1, 245, 0, 1, 454186) G.V. Subbaramayya: Bhagavan once told me that Bhagavan is aware of the beginning of parayana and knows nothing more till the end of it.
(1, 245, 1, 2, 454322) Bhagavan: Yes, it often happens that I hear the beginning and then the end and have been absorbed so that I have lost count of time in between, and then I have wondered whether they had left out whole passages to get to the end so soon.
(1, 245, 2, 3, 454559) After a moment, Bhagavan continued: Similarly, those people go on massaging and I am sometimes not at all aware that I am being massaged.
(1, 245, 2, 4, 454697) So now I am not going to let them.
(1, 245, 2, 5, 454732) I will do it myself. So saying, Bhagavan took the liniment and rubbed it over his knees.
(1, 245, 3, 6, 454821) In the afternoon Bhagavan explained in answer to Mr. H.C. Khanna of Kanpur:
(1, 245, 4, 7, 454897) Why should your occupation or duties in life interfere with your spiritual effort?
(1, 245, 4, 8, 454980) For instance, there is a difference between your activities at home and in the office.
(1, 245, 4, 9, 455067) In your office activities you are detached and so long as you do your duty you do not care what happens or whether it results in gain or loss to the employer.
(1, 245, 4, 10, 455226) But your duties at home are performed with attachment and you are all the time anxious as to whether they will bring advantage or disadvantage to you and your family.
(1, 245, 4, 11, 455393) But it is possible to perform all the activities of life with detachment and regard only the Self as real.
(1, 245, 4, 12, 455500) It is wrong to suppose that if one is fixed in the Self ones duties in life will not be properly performed.
(1, 245, 4, 13, 455608) It is like an actor.
(1, 245, 4, 14, 455629) He dresses and acts and even feels the part he is playing, but he knows really that he is not that character but someone else in real life.
(1, 245, 4, 15, 455769) In the same way, why should the body consciousness or the feeling I am the body disturb you, once you know for certain that you are not the body but the Self?
(1, 245, 4, 16, 455928) Nothing that the body does should shake you from abidance in the Self.
(1, 245, 4, 17, 455999) Such abidance will never interfere with
(1, 246, 0, 1, 456039) the proper and effective discharge of whatever duties the body has, any more than the actors being aware of his real status in life interferes with his acting a part on the stage.
(1, 246, 1, 2, 456219) You ask whether you can tell yourself: I am not the body but the Self.
(1, 246, 1, 3, 456290) Of course, whenever you feel tempted to identify yourself with the body (as you may often have to, owing to old vasanas) it may be a help to remind yourself that you are not the body but the Self.
(1, 246, 1, 4, 456487) But you should not make such repetition a mantram, constantly saying: I am not the body but the Self.
(1, 246, 1, 5, 456589) By proper enquiry into the Self, the notion I am this body will gradually vanish and in time the faith that you are the Self will become unshakeable.
(1, 246, 2, 6, 456739) K.M. Jivrajani: In the early stages would it not be a help to man to seek solitude and give up his outer duties in life?
(1, 246, 3, 7, 456860) Bhagavan: Renunciation is always in the mind, not in going to forests or solitary places or giving up ones duties.
(1, 246, 3, 8, 456975) The main thing is to see that the mind does not turn outward but inward.
(1, 246, 3, 9, 457048) It does not really rest with a man whether he goes to this place or that or whether he gives up his duties or not.
(1, 246, 3, 10, 457163) All that happens according to destiny.
(1, 246, 3, 11, 457202) All the activities that the body is to go through are determined when it first comes into existence.
(1, 246, 3, 12, 457303) It does not rest with you to accept or reject them.
(1, 246, 3, 13, 457355) The only freedom you have is to turn your mind inward and renounce activities there.
(1, 246, 4, 14, 457440) K.M. Jivrajani: But is it not possible for something to be a help, especially to a beginner?
(1, 246, 4, 15, 457533) Like a fence round a young tree.
(1, 246, 4, 16, 457566) For instance, dont our books say that it is helpful to go on pilgrimage to sacred shrines or to get sat sang.
(1, 246, 5, 17, 457676) Bhagavan: Who said they are not helpful?
(1, 246, 5, 18, 457717) Only such things do not rest with you, as turning your mind inward does.
(1, 246, 5, 19, 457790) Many people desire the pilgrimage or sat sang that you mention, but do they all get it?
(1, 247, 0, 1, 457878) K.M. Jivrajani: Why is it that turning inward alone is left to us and not any outer things?
(1, 247, 1, 2, 457970) I answered: Nobody can answer that.
(1, 247, 1, 3, 458006) That is the Divine scheme.
(1, 247, 2, 4, 458033) Bhagavan: If you want to go to fundamentals, you must enquire who you are and find out who it is who has freedom or destiny.
(1, 247, 2, 5, 458158) Who are you and why did you get this body that has these limitations?
(1, 247, 3, 6, 458228) 3 6 46 3 6 46 3 6 46 3 6 46 3 6 46
(1, 247, 4, 7, 458263) G.V. Subbaramayya: Did Subramania Bharati ever come to Bhagavan?
(1, 247, 5, 8, 458328) Bhagavan: I think he did once.
(1, 247, 5, 9, 458359) It was when we were on the hill.
(1, 247, 5, 10, 458392) One evening when only Sivayya (the late Mauni Swami of Kutralam), who is dead now, was with me, someone came and sat for nearly an hour before me and then went away without saying a word.
(1, 247, 5, 11, 458580) Later, when I saw pictures of Bharati I thought it must have been he.
(1, 247, 6, 12, 458650) G.V. Subbaramayya: Was it Sivayya who beat a monkey and the monkey was so grieved that it went and drowned itself?
(1, 247, 7, 13, 458765) Bhagavan: No, it was someone else.
(1, 247, 7, 14, 458800) And the monkey was not even beaten, it was only scolded.
(1, 247, 7, 15, 458857) Even that was more than it could stand and it went and drowned itself very soon after.
(1, 247, 7, 16, 458944) It was a dog that was beaten.
(1, 247, 7, 17, 458974) He was a very strange dog.
(1, 247, 7, 18, 459001) All day he would lie quiet in a place among the rocks, higher up than our Asramam, and where it was not easy to see him, and he would only go out at night.
(1, 247, 7, 19, 459157) Seeing something black going out and coming back at night, we looked during the day time and found that it was a dog.
(1, 247, 7, 20, 459275) He continued in this way for many days, so we took pity on him and began giving him food.
(1, 247, 7, 21, 459365) But even then he would not come near us.
(1, 247, 7, 22, 459406) We used to put some food a little distance away from us and he would come and eat it and then go away.
(1, 248, 0, 1, 459509) we went near he would run away.
(1, 248, 0, 2, 459541) And then one day, when a number of us had been out and were returning, this dog ran up to us, and he came straight to me out of all the crowd and jumped up on me and tried to make friends with me.
(1, 248, 0, 3, 459738) After that he stayed with us and he would go and lie in the lap of any devotee.
(1, 248, 0, 4, 459818) Some of the orthodox ones didnt like it, and one day Iswara Swami beat him for interfering when a devotee was doing puja.
(1, 248, 0, 5, 459940) This was more than the dog could stand and he immediately disappeared.
(1, 248, 0, 6, 460011) We dont know what happened to him.
(1, 248, 0, 7, 460046) We searched for him but could never find out.

(1, 249, 1, 5, 461559) In the afternoon K.S.S. (Ramanadasa) narrated the following incident:
(1, 249, 2, 6, 461629) When Bhagavan was living at Skandasramam I was once alone with him, sitting on the steps leading up to the Asramam when a man came to the gate with his family and stopped there and called out to me.
(1, 249, 2, 7, 461828) When I went there he asked me to go and ask the Swami whether they could approach him and receive his darshan.
(1, 249, 2, 8, 461939) I was surprised and said, Why do you ask permission? And he said, We are untouchables.
(1, 249, 3, 9, 462026) I started to go back to Bhagavan, but then it occurred to me that even to ask Bhagavan would be an injustice to him, so I told the man that caste had no meaning with Bhagavan and that they would be welcome.
(1, 249, 3, 10, 462233) The whole party came and prostrated before Bhagavan, and I well remember how for about ten minutes his gracious look dwelt on that untouchable and his family; and how many rich and notable people have I seen fall at his feet without being vouchsafed such grace.

(1, 250, 3, 6, 463526) Bhagavan: They are the same.
(1, 250, 3, 7, 463555) In both, the mind is concentrated on one thing, the mantra or the Self.
(1, 250, 3, 8, 463627) Mantra, japa, dhyana  are only different names.
(1, 250, 3, 9, 463675) So long as they require effort we call them by these names, but when the Self is realized this goes on without any effort and what was the means becomes the goal.

(1, 251, 3, 8, 465362) Dr. Haridas, a disciple of Swami Madhava Theertha and a relative of Mahatma Gandhi by marriage, asked Bhagavan, If ajnana is also Brahman, why is Brahman not visible but only ajnana or the world?
(1, 251, 4, 9, 465558) Bhagavan: Brahman is not to be seen or known.
(1, 251, 4, 10, 465604) It is beyond the triputis (triads) of seer, seen and seeing or knower, knowledge and knowing.
(1, 251, 4, 11, 465698) The Reality remains ever as it is; that there is ajnana or the world is due to our moham or illusion.
(1, 251, 4, 12, 465800) Neither knowledge nor ignorance is real; what is beyond this, as all other pairs of opposites, is the Reality.
(1, 251, 4, 13, 465911) It is neither light nor darkness but beyond both, though we sometimes have to speak of it as light and of ignorance as its shadow.
(1, 251, 5, 14, 466042) G.V.S.: It is said that the Self cannot be realized by reading books but only by anubhava (personal experience).
(1, 251, 6, 15, 466155) Bhagavan: What is anubhava?
(1, 251, 6, 16, 466183) It is only going beyond the pairs of opposites or the triputis.
(1, 251, 7, 17, 466247) In the evening Bhagavan said with reference to a question somebody had asked: During sleep there is both the Self and ajnana  ajnana because we knew nothing and the Self
(1, 252, 0, 1, 466417) because we existed, and when we wake we say, I slept well, although we knew nothing.
(1, 252, 0, 2, 466502) If one asks how the Self and ajnana can exist together, any more than light and darkness, the answer is that to one who realises, the Self is all light and there is no such thing as darkness at all, but to one who has not realised we say that there can be ajnana in the Self like the seeming shadows on the moon.

(1, 255, 1, 2, 471327) When Bhagavan returned from his morning walk on the Hill, a Bangalore photographer took a photograph of him in Padmasanam posture for inclusion in the Golden Jubilee Souvenir that is to be brought out in September.
(1, 255, 1, 3, 471542) Sri Gunaji, a retired advocate who is now a naturopath at Belgaum, has been here for some days, massaging Bhagavans legs for rheumatism, and today he sang a song he had composed in Hindi.
(1, 255, 1, 4, 471730) He gave its meaning in English as: I ask nothing of Thee, Lord; but if Thou art disposed to grant me any favour, then take away this ego sense, kill all my thoughts, destroy the world and let my mind be dissolved in the ocean of Self. (1, 255, 2, 9, 472238) In continuation of yesterdays conversation about Tennyson, the relevant passage was found in a footnote to the English translation of Upadesa Saram.
(1, 255, 2, 10, 472387) It was not in a poem but in a letter to B.P. Blood.
(1, 255, 2, 11, 472439) Bhagavan asked me to read it out, so I did: .
(1, 255, 2, 12, 472485) .a kind of waking trance I have frequently had, quite up from boyhood, when I have been all alone.
(1, 255, 2, 13, 472584) This has generally come upon me through repeating my own name two or three times to myself, silently, till all at once, as it were out of the intensity of consciousness of individuality, the individuality itself seemed to dissolve and fade away into boundless being: and this not a confused state but the clearest of the clearest, the surest of the surest, the weirdest of the weirdest, utterly beyond words, where death was an almost laughable impossibility, the loss of personality (if so it were) seeming no extinction but the only true life.

(1, 256, 6, 14, 474684) A newcomer called Gajendra Mehta asked Bhagavan about the state of the soul after death.

(1, 256, 6, 16, 474807) He has been writing to Bhagavan for four years but this is the first time he has come here.
(1, 257, 0, 1, 474899) Bhagavan: If you know the present you will know the future.
(1, 257, 0, 2, 474959) It is strange that people dont want to know about the present, about whose existence nobody can have any doubt, but are always eager to know about the past or the future, both of which are unknown.
(1, 257, 0, 3, 475157) What is birth and what is death?

(1, 257, 0, 7, 475470) It is only when you wake up that you have a body and see the world.

(1, 257, 1, 10, 475741) G. Mehta: Is there a rebirth?

(1, 257, 2, 14, 475980) But if you ask who has the birth and whether birth and death are for you or for somebody distinct from you, then you realize the truth and the truth burns up all karma and frees you from all births.
(1, 257, 2, 15, 476179) The books graphically describe how all sanchita karma, which would take countless lives to exhaust, is burnt up by one little spark of jnana, just as a mountain of gunpowder will be blown up by a single spark of fire.

(1, 263, 3, 6, 486420) Khanna then asked, The illumination plus mind is jivatma and the illumination alone is paramatma; is that right?
(1, 263, 4, 7, 486533) Bhagavan assented and then pointed to his towel and said, We call this a white cloth, but the cloth and its whiteness cannot be separated, and it is the same with the illumination and the mind that unite to form the ego. Then he added: The following illustration that is often given in books will also help you.
(1, 263, 4, 8, 486845) The lamp in the theatre is the Parabrahman or the illumination, as you put it.
(1, 263, 4, 9, 486924) It illumines itself and the stage and actors.
(1, 263, 4, 10, 486970) We see the stage and the actors by its light, but its light still continues when there is no more play.
(1, 263, 4, 11, 487074) Another illustration is an iron rod that is compared to the mind.
(1, 263, 4, 12, 487140) Fire joins it and it becomes red hot.
(1, 263, 4, 13, 487178) It glows and can burn things, like fire, but still it has a definite shape, unlike fire.
(1, 263, 4, 14, 487267) If we hammer it, it is the rod that receives the blows, not the fire.
(1, 263, 4, 15, 487337) The rod is the jivatma and the fire the Self or Paramatma.

(1, 264, 0, 2, 487837) In the old days some Vaishnavites used to come to me, and when they were wearing the U mark they would put it on me also, and when they were wearing the Y mark they would put that on me, and then they would prostrate themselves before me.
(1, 264, 0, 3, 488076) I used to let them do what they liked with me.
(1, 264, 1, 4, 488123) T.V.K. then told Bhagavan, Recently a man of the thengalai school who is well versed in the esoteric meaning of Vaishnavite literature initiated me and gave me samasanam and sama asrayam and taught me their esoteric meaning.
(1, 264, 1, 5, 488348) He gives discourses and does good work among the poor, but he would not admit vadakalais to his discourses; according to the Vaishnavite teaching one must do kainkaryam or service to God.
(1, 264, 2, 6, 488536) Bhagavan replied rather sarcastically: So God cant get on without their services?
(1, 264, 2, 7, 488618) On the contrary, God asks: Who are you to do service to Me? He is always saying: I am within you; who are you? One must try to realize that and not speak of service.
(1, 264, 2, 8, 488784) Submission or surrender is the basic teaching of Vaishnavism, but it does not consist in paying a Guru a fee for initiation and telling him that you have surrendered.
(1, 264, 2, 9, 488951) As often as one tries to surrender, the ego raises its head and one has to try to suppress it.
(1, 264, 2, 10, 489046) Surrender is not an easy thing.
(1, 264, 2, 11, 489078) Killing the ego is not an easy thing.
(1, 264, 2, 12, 489116) It is only when God Himself by His grace draws the mind inwards that complete surrender can be achieved.
(1, 264, 2, 13, 489221) But such grace comes only to those who have already, in this or previous lives, gone through all the struggles and sadhanas preparatory to the extinction of the mind and killing of the ego.
(1, 264, 3, 14, 489411) Bhagavan added, In the old days these Vaishnavites used to come and advise me to undergo a samasanam but I used to keep silent.

(1, 265, 0, 2, 489729) Then I discovered that I was You and mine was Yours, oh God. He said: This is clear Advaita, but these Vaishnavites would give it some interpretation to make it accord with their feeling of duality.
(1, 265, 0, 3, 489928) They hold that they must exist and God must exist, but how is that possible?

(1, 265, 1, 5, 490173) Bhagavan said this laughing, and then, after a pause, he added, On the other hand, Advaita does not mean that a man must always sit in samadhi and never engage in action.
(1, 265, 1, 6, 490344) Many things are necessary to keep up the life of the body, and action can never be avoided.
(1, 265, 1, 7, 490436) Nor is bhakti ruled out in Advaita.
(1, 265, 1, 8, 490472) Shankara is rightly regarded as the foremost exponent of Advaita, and yet look at the number of shrines he visited (action), and the devotional songs he wrote.

(1, 266, 3, 9, 492387) In the afternoon Khannas wife appealed to Bhagavan in writing: I am not learned in the scriptures and I find the method of Self enquiry too hard for me.
(1, 266, 3, 10, 492540) I am a woman with seven children and a lot of household cares, and it leaves me little time for meditation.

(1, 266, 4, 13, 492834) All knowledge is required only to be given up eventually as not Self.

(1, 266, 4, 16, 493173) I is the name of God.
(1, 266, 4, 17, 493195) It is the first and greatest of all mantras.
(1, 266, 4, 18, 493240) Even OM is second to it.
(1, 267, 0, 1, 493265) Khanna: The jiva is said to be mind plus illumination.
(1, 267, 0, 2, 493320) What is it that desires Self realization and what is it that obstructs our path to Self realization?
(1, 267, 0, 3, 493421) It is said that the mind obstructs and the illumination helps.
(1, 267, 1, 4, 493484) Bhagavan: Although we describe the jiva as mind plus the reflected light of the Self, in actual practice, in life, you cannot separate the two, just as, in the illustrations we used yesterday, you cant separate cloth and whiteness in a white cloth or fire and iron in a red hot rod.
(1, 267, 1, 5, 493767) The mind can do nothing by itself.
(1, 267, 1, 6, 493802) It emerges only with the illumination and can do no action, good or bad, except with the illumination.
(1, 267, 1, 7, 493905) But while the illumination is always there, enabling the mind to act well or ill, the pleasure or pain resulting from such action is not felt by the illumination, just as when you hammer a red hot rod it is not the fire but the iron that gets the hammering.
(1, 267, 2, 8, 494163) Khanna: Is there destiny?
(1, 267, 2, 9, 494189) And if what is destined to happen will happen is there any use in prayer or effort or should we just remain idle?
(1, 267, 3, 10, 494303) Bhagavan: There are only two ways to conquer destiny or be independent of it.
(1, 267, 3, 11, 494381) One is to enquire for whom is this destiny and discover that only the ego is bound by destiny and not the Self, and that the ego is non existent.
(1, 267, 3, 12, 494527) The other way is to kill the ego by completely surrendering to the Lord, by realizing ones helplessness and saying all the time: Not I but Thou, oh Lord!, and giving up all sense of I and mine and leaving it to the Lord to do what he likes with you.
(1, 267, 3, 13, 494777) Surrender can never be regarded as complete so long as the devotee wants this or that from the Lord.
(1, 267, 3, 14, 494878) True surrender is love of God for the sake of love and nothing else, not even for the sake of salvation.
(1, 267, 3, 15, 494983) In other words, complete effacement of the ego is necessary to conquer destiny, whether you achieve this effacement through Self enquiry or through bhakti marga.
(1, 267, 4, 16, 495145) Khanna: Are our prayers granted?

(1, 268, 4, 11, 496031) A visitor said: I am told that according to your school I must find out the source of my thoughts.

(1, 268, 7, 16, 496491) All those are also thoughts.

(1, 268, 7, 22, 496794) Because perception or memory or any other experience only comes to that I.

(1, 269, 0, 1, 496935) you existed during sleep.

(1, 269, 3, 8, 497373) Some of us advised the visitor to read Who am I?

(1, 269, 6, 14, 497788) Instead of looking outwards, look inwards and see where the I thought arises.
(1, 269, 7, 15, 497866) Visitor: And Bhagavan says that if I see that, I shall realise the Self?

(1, 269, 8, 19, 498143) When you do that you will remain as you always are and the Real will be Real.
(1, 269, 8, 20, 498221) It is only to help people give up regarding the unreal as real that all the religions and the practices taught by them have come into being.

(1, 269, 11, 23, 498420) Visitor: The Upanishads say He who knows Brahman becomes Brahman.

(1, 270, 2, 3, 498618) Bhagavan: He who is Brahman or the Self will not value those siddhis.
(1, 270, 2, 4, 498688) Patanjali himself says that they are all exercised with the mind and that they impede Self realisation.
(1, 270, 3, 5, 498792) Visitor: What about the powers of supermen?

(1, 270, 5, 7, 498993) Visitor: When one attains Self realisation, what is the guarantee that one has really attained it and is not under an illusion like the lunatic who thinks he is Napoleon or some such thing?
(1, 270, 6, 8, 499183) Bhagavan: In a sense, speaking of Self realisation is a delusion.
(1, 270, 6, 9, 499249) It is only because people have been under the delusion that the non Self is the Self and the unreal the Real that they have to be weaned out of it by the other delusion called Self realisation; because actually the Self always is the Self and there is no such thing as realising it.
(1, 270, 6, 10, 499532) Who is to realise what, and how, when all that exists is the Self and nothing but the Self?

(1, 270, 8, 17, 499983) If you regard the world as not Self it is not real.
(1, 270, 8, 18, 500035) Everything, whether you call it world or maya or lila or sakti, must be within the Self and not apart from it.
(1, 270, 8, 19, 500146) There can be no sakti apart from the sakta.

(1, 271, 4, 8, 500914) Nagamma has been keeping a record of interesting events that she writes to her brother, D.S. Sastri, at Madras in the form of letters.

(1, 271, 5, 11, 501269) There was once a regular war between the people here and the squirrels for a whole month.
(1, 271, 5, 12, 501359) They used to build their nests over my head.
(1, 271, 5, 13, 501404) Each day the people would destroy them and the next day the squirrels would have built them again.
(1, 271, 5, 14, 501503) At last all the holes in the roof were stopped up and the squirrels could do nothing.
(1, 271, 5, 15, 501589) At one time they used to run all over my couch and get into the sides and under the pillows and everywhere, and I had to look carefully before I sat down or leaned back.
(1, 271, 5, 16, 501759) It has sometimes happened that I have accidentally leaned heavily on some small squirrel and given it samadhi without knowing.
(1, 271, 5, 17, 501886) The same thing sometimes happened on the Hill too, at Skandasramam.
(1, 271, 5, 18, 501954) There too the squirrels used to nestle in my mattress and pillows.
(1, 271, 5, 19, 502021) It began even before that.
(1, 272, 0, 1, 502048) when I was at Gurumoortham birds and squirrels used to build their nests all round me.
(1, 272, 0, 2, 502135) There is a bird that builds its nest of mud.
(1, 272, 0, 3, 502180) Once while I was there such a nest was built and after the birds had left it squirrels occupied it.

(1, 272, 2, 5, 502320) On the 8th news had come of the death of Madhava Swami and Bhagavan had spoken a good deal about it.
