(1, 272, 5, 23, 503925) It is only those
(1, 273, 0, 1, 503942) who are left behind who feel miserable.
(1, 273, 0, 2, 503982) It is our constant concern to bear the burden of this body and look after its needs.
(1, 273, 0, 3, 504067) Day in, day out, this is our occupation  bathing, eating, massaging our legs, and so on  no end to it.
(1, 273, 0, 4, 504170) When we die it takes four persons to carry this body and yet we carry it about constantly without even stopping to think that we are doing so.
(1, 273, 0, 5, 504313) We can easily lift a heavy stone under water, but as soon as we take it out we find how heavy it is, and in the same way we dont feel the weight of the body as long as a chaitanya or life force permeates it.
(1, 273, 1, 6, 504521) Deathlessness is our real nature, and we falsely ascribe it to the body, imagining that it will live for ever and losing sight of what is really immortal, simply because we identify ourselves with the body.
(1, 273, 1, 7, 504728) It says in the Upanishads that the jnani looks forward eagerly to the time when he can throw off the body, just as a labourer carrying a heavy load looks forward to reaching his destination and laying it down.

(1, 275, 4, 9, 508408) This morning questions were put by a visitor, by name S.P. Tayal.
(1, 275, 5, 10, 508474) S.P. Tayal: I have been doing sadhana for nearly 20 years and I can see no progress.
(1, 275, 5, 11, 508559) What should I do?
(1, 275, 6, 12, 508577) Bhagavan: I may be able to say something if I know what the sadhana is.
(1, 275, 7, 13, 508649) S.P. Tayal: From about 5 oclock every morning I concentrate on the thought that the Self alone is real and all else unreal.
(1, 275, 7, 14, 508773) Although I have been doing this for about 20 years I cannot concentrate for more than two or three minutes without my thoughts wandering.
(1, 275, 8, 15, 508911) Bhagavan: There is no other way to succeed than to draw the mind back every time it turns outwards and fix it in the Self.
(1, 275, 8, 16, 509034) There is no need for meditation or mantra or japa or dhyana or
(1, 276, 0, 1, 509097) anything of the sort, because these are our real nature.
(1, 276, 0, 2, 509154) All that is needed is to give up thinking of objects other than the Self.
(1, 276, 0, 3, 509228) Meditation is not so much thinking of the Self as giving up thinking of the not Self.
(1, 276, 0, 4, 509314) When you give up thinking of outward objects and prevent your mind from going outwards and turn it inward and fix it in the Self, the Self alone will remain.
(1, 276, 1, 5, 509472) S.P. Tayal: What should I do to overcome the pull of these thoughts and desires?
(1, 276, 1, 6, 509553) How should I regulate my life so as to attain control over my thoughts?
(1, 276, 2, 7, 509625) Bhagavan: The more you get fixed in the Self, the more other thoughts will drop off by themselves.
(1, 276, 2, 8, 509724) The mind is nothing but a bundle of thoughts, and the I thought is the root of all of them.
(1, 276, 2, 9, 509816) When you see who this I is and whence it proceeds all thoughts get merged in the Self.
(1, 276, 3, 10, 509903) Regulation of life, such as getting up at a fixed hour, bathing, doing mantra, japa, etc., observing ritual, all this is for people who do not feel drawn to Self enquiry or are not capable of it.
(1, 276, 3, 11, 510099) But for those who can practise this method all rules and discipline are unnecessary.
(1, 276, 4, 12, 510184) At this point K.M. Jivrajani interposed, Has one necessarily to pass through the stage of seeing occult visions before attaining Self realization?
(1, 276, 5, 13, 510331) Bhagavan: Why do you bother about visions and whether they come or not?
(1, 276, 6, 14, 510403) K.M. Jivrajani: I dont.
(1, 276, 6, 15, 510427) I only want to know so that I shant be disappointed if I dont have them.
(1, 276, 7, 16, 510500) Bhagavan: Visions are not a necessary stage.
(1, 276, 7, 17, 510545) To some they come and to others they dont, but whether they come or not you always exist and you must stick to that.
(1, 276, 8, 18, 510662) K.M. Jivrajani: I sometimes concentrate on the brain centre and sometimes on the heart  not always on the same centre.
(1, 276, 8, 19, 510781) Is that wrong?
(1, 277, 0, 1, 510796) Bhagavan: Wherever you concentrate and on whatever centre there must be a you to concentrate, and that is what you must concentrate on.
(1, 277, 0, 2, 510932) Different people concentrate on different centres, not only the brain and the heart but also the space between the eyebrows, the tip of the nose, the tip of the tongue, the lowermost chakra and even external objects.
(1, 277, 0, 3, 511149) Such concentration may lead to a sort of laya in which you will feel a certain bliss, but care must be taken not to lose the thought I Am in all this.
(1, 277, 0, 4, 511300) You never cease to exist in all these experiences.
(1, 277, 1, 5, 511351) K.M. Jivrajani: That is to say that I must be a witness?
(1, 277, 2, 6, 511408) Bhagavan: Talking of the witness should not lead to the idea that there is a witness and something else apart from him that he is witnessing.
(1, 277, 2, 7, 511550) The witness really means the light that illumines the seer, the seen and the process of seeing.
(1, 277, 2, 8, 511646) Before, during and after the triads of seer, seen and seeing, the illumination exists.
(1, 277, 2, 9, 511733) It alone exists always.
(1, 277, 3, 10, 511757) K.M. Jivrajani: It is said in books that one should cultivate all the good or daivic qualities in order to prepare oneself for Self realisation.
(1, 277, 4, 11, 511902) Bhagavan: All good or daivic qualities are included in jnana and all bad asuric qualities are included in ajnana.
(1, 277, 4, 12, 512016) When jnana comes all ajnana goes and all daivic qualities come automatically.
(1, 277, 4, 13, 512094) If a man is a jnani he cannot utter a lie or do anything wrong.
(1, 277, 4, 14, 512158) It is, no doubt, said in some books that one should cultivate one quality after another and thus prepare for ultimate moksha, but for those who follow the jnana or vichara marga their sadhana is itself quite enough for acquiring all daivic qualities; they need not do anything else.
(1, 277, 5, 15, 512441) 111119 7 46 9 7 46 9 7 46 9 7 46 9 7 46
(1, 277, 6, 16, 512481) Again today a visitor put questions: I do not understand how to make the enquiry Who am I?
(1, 278, 0, 1, 512572) Bhagavan: Find out whence the I arises.
(1, 278, 0, 2, 512612) Self enquiry does not mean argument or reasoning such as goes on when you say, I am not this body, I am not the senses, etc.: all that may also help but it is not the enquiry.
(1, 278, 0, 3, 512788) Watch and find out where in the body the I arises and fix your mind on that.

(1, 278, 2, 5, 512893) Bhagavan: What is gayatri?
(1, 278, 2, 6, 512920) It really means: Let me concentrate on that which illumines all. Dhyana really means only concentrating or fixing the mind on the object of dhyana.
(1, 278, 2, 7, 513068) But meditation is our real nature.
(1, 278, 2, 8, 513103) If we give up other thoughts what remains is I and its nature is dhyana or meditation or jnana, whichever we choose to call it.
(1, 278, 2, 9, 513231) What is at one time the means later becomes the end; unless meditation or dhyana were the nature of the Self it could not take you to the Self.
(1, 278, 2, 10, 513375) If the means were not of the nature of the goal, it could not bring you to the goal.

(1, 278, 6, 16, 513821) In the afternoon the following two questions were put by Mr. Bhargava, an elderly visitor from Jhansi in U.P.:
(1, 278, 7, 17, 513932) (1) How am I to search for the I from start to finish?
(1, 278, 8, 18, 513987) (2) When I meditate I reach a stage where there is a vacuum or void.
(1, 278, 8, 19, 514056) How should I proceed from there?
(1, 278, 9, 20, 514089) Bhagavan: Never mind whether there are visions or sounds or anything else or whether there is a void.
(1, 278, 9, 21, 514191) Are you present
(1, 279, 0, 1, 514207) during all this or are you not?
(1, 279, 0, 2, 514239) You must have been there even during the void to be able to say that you experienced a void.
(1, 279, 0, 3, 514332) To be fixed in that you is the quest for the I from start to finish.
(1, 279, 0, 4, 514401) In all books on Vedanta you will find this question of a void or of nothing being left, raised by the disciple and answered by the Guru.
(1, 279, 0, 5, 514538) It is the mind that sees objects and has experiences and that finds a void when it ceases to see and experience, but that is not you.
(1, 279, 0, 6, 514672) You are the constant illumination that lights up both the experiences and the void.
(1, 279, 0, 7, 514756) It is like the theatre light that enables you to see the theatre, the actors and the play while the play is going on but also remains alight and enables you to say that there is no play on when it is all finished.
(1, 279, 0, 8, 514970) Or there is another illustration.
(1, 279, 0, 9, 515004) We see objects all around us, but in complete darkness we do not see them and we say, I see nothing; even then the eyes are there to say that they see nothing.
(1, 279, 0, 10, 515164) In the same way, you are there even in the void you mention.
(1, 279, 1, 11, 515225) You are the witness of the three bodies: the gross, the subtle and the causal, and of the three states: waking, dream and deep sleep, and of the three times: past, present and future, and also of this void.
(1, 279, 1, 12, 515432) In the story of the tenth man, when each of the ten counted and thought there were only nine, each one forgetting to count himself, there is a stage when they think one is missing and dont know who it is; and that corresponds to the void.
(1, 279, 1, 13, 515671) We are so accustomed to the notion that all that we see around us is permanent and that we are this body, that when all this ceases to exist we imagine and fear that we also have ceased to exist.
(1, 279, 2, 14, 515867) Bhagavan also quoted verses 212 and 213 from Vivekachudamani, in which the disciple says: After I eliminate the five sheaths as not Self, I find that nothing at all remains, and the Guru replied that the Self or That by which all modifications (including the ego and its creatures) and their absence (that is the void) are perceived is always there.
(1, 280, 0, 1, 516217) Then Bhagavan continued speaking on the subject and said: The nature of the Self or I must be illumination.
(1, 280, 0, 2, 516325) You perceive all modifications and their absence.
(1, 280, 0, 3, 516375) To say that you get the illumination from another would raise the question how he got it and there would be no end to the chain of reasoning.
(1, 280, 0, 4, 516517) So you yourself are the illumination.
(1, 280, 0, 5, 516555) The usual illustration of this is the following: You make all kinds of sweets of various ingredients and in various shapes and they all taste sweet because there is sugar in all of them and sweetness is the nature of sugar.
(1, 280, 0, 6, 516779) And in the same way all experiences and the absence of them contain the illumination which is the nature of the Self.
(1, 280, 0, 7, 516897) Without the Self they cannot be experienced, just as without sugar not one of the articles you make can taste sweet.
(1, 280, 1, 8, 517014) A little later Bhagavan also said: First one sees the Self as objects, then one sees the Self as void, then one sees the Self as Self, only in this last there is no seeing because seeing is being.
(1, 280, 2, 9, 517211) Mr. Bhargava also said something about sleep, and this led Bhagavan to speak about sleep as follows:
(1, 280, 3, 10, 517312) What is required is to remain fixed in the Self always.
(1, 280, 3, 11, 517368) The obstacles to that are distraction by the things of the world (including sense objects, desires and tendencies) on the one hand, and sleep on the other.
(1, 280, 3, 12, 517524) Sleep is always mentioned in books as the first obstacle to samadhi and various methods are prescribed for overcoming it according to the stage of evolution of the person concerned.
(1, 280, 3, 13, 517706) First, one is enjoined to give up all distraction by the world and its objects or by sleep.
(1, 280, 3, 14, 517798) But then it is said, for instance in the Gita, that one need not give up sleep entirely.
(1, 280, 3, 15, 517887) Too much and too little are alike undesirable.
(1, 280, 3, 16, 517934) One should not sleep at all during the daytime and even during the night restrict sleep to the middle portion, from about ten to two.
(1, 280, 3, 17, 518068) But another method that is prescribed is not to bother about sleep at all.
(1, 280, 3, 18, 518143) When it overtakes you, you can do nothing about it, so simply remain fixed in the Self or in meditation every
(1, 281, 0, 1, 518253) moment of your waking life and take up the meditation again the moment you wake, and that will be enough.
(1, 281, 0, 2, 518359) Then even during sleep the same current of thought or meditation will be working.
(1, 281, 0, 3, 518441) This is evident because if a man goes to sleep with any strong thought working in his mind he finds the same thought there when he wakes.
(1, 281, 0, 4, 518579) It is of the man who does this with meditation that it is said that even his sleep is samadhi.
(1, 281, 0, 5, 518674) A good way to reduce the amount of sleep needed is to take only sattvic food and that in moderation and to avoid work or activity of any kind.
(1, 281, 1, 6, 518817) 22 7 46 22 7 46 22 7 46 22 7 46 22 7 46
(1, 281, 2, 7, 518857) This morning Vaidyanathan, the R.D.O., came into the hall and asked whether he could bring in the adviser, Ramamurti.
(1, 281, 2, 8, 518975) Bhagavan gave permission and he brought in Ramamurti and his party.

(1, 281, 2, 10, 519234) This (pointing to the man next to him) is my brother.

(1, 281, 2, 12, 519344) Kameswara Sarma is also working there.

(1, 281, 3, 14, 519556) In fact I find it impossible.
(1, 281, 3, 15, 519586) But I can believe in an impersonal God, a Divine Force which rules and guides the world, and it would be a great help to me, even in my work of healing, if this faith were increased.
(1, 281, 3, 16, 519769) May I know how to increase this faith?
(1, 281, 4, 17, 519808) After a slight pause Bhagavan replied, Faith is in things unknown; but the Self is self evident.
(1, 281, 4, 18, 519905) Even the greatest egoist cannot deny his own existence, that is to say, cannot deny the Self.
(1, 281, 4, 19, 519999) You can call the ultimate Reality by whatever name you like and say that you have faith in it or love for it, but who is there who will not have faith in his own existence or love for himself?
(1, 281, 4, 20, 520192) That is because faith and love are our real nature.
(1, 282, 0, 1, 520244) A little later Ramamurti asked, That which rises as I within us is the Self, is it not?
(1, 282, 1, 2, 520332) Bhagavan: No; it is the ego that rises as I.
(1, 282, 1, 3, 520377) That from which it arises is the Self.
(1, 282, 2, 4, 520416) Ramamurti: They speak of a lower and a higher atman.
(1, 282, 3, 5, 520469) Bhagavan: There is no such thing as lower or higher in atman.
(1, 282, 3, 6, 520531) Lower and higher apply to the forms, not to the Self or atman.
(1, 282, 4, 7, 520594) Soon after, the party took leave, declining an invitation to stay to lunch, as they had already arranged for lunch elsewhere.
(1, 282, 5, 8, 520720) In the afternoon Mr. Tayal of Calcutta spoke with Bhagavan again.
(1, 282, 6, 9, 520786) Tayal: I do not always concentrate on the same centre in the body.
(1, 282, 6, 10, 520853) Sometimes I find it easier to concentrate on one centre and sometimes on another.
(1, 282, 6, 11, 520935) And sometimes when I concentrate on one centre the thought of its own accord goes and fixes itself in another.
(1, 282, 6, 12, 521046) Why is that?
(1, 282, 7, 13, 521059) Bhagavan: It may be because of past practices of yours.
(1, 282, 7, 14, 521115) But in any case it is immaterial on which centre you concentrate since the real heart is in every centre and even outside the body.
(1, 282, 7, 15, 521247) On whatever part of the body you may concentrate or on whatever external object, the heart is there.
(1, 282, 8, 16, 521348) K.M. Jivrajani, intervening, asked: Can one concentrate at one time on one centre and at another time on another or should one concentrate always consistently on the same centre?
(1, 282, 9, 17, 521527) Bhagavan: As I have just said, there can be no harm wherever you concentrate, because concentration is only a means of giving up thoughts.
(1, 282, 9, 18, 521666) Whatever the centre or object on which you concentrate, he who concentrates is always the same.
(1, 283, 0, 1, 521762) 222224 7 46 4 7 46 4 7 46 4 7 46 4 7 46
(1, 283, 1, 2, 521802) Bhargava: What is awareness and how can one obtain and cultivate it?
(1, 283, 2, 3, 521871) Bhagavan: You are awareness.
(1, 283, 2, 4, 521900) Awareness is another name for you.
(1, 283, 2, 5, 521935) Since you are awareness there is no need to attain or cultivate it.
(1, 283, 3, 6, 522003) This was obviously a bit too much for Bhargava and he was wondering how it was an answer to his question, but Bhagavan came to his help by adding: All that you have to do is to give up being aware of other things, that is of the not Self.
(1, 283, 3, 7, 522242) If one gives up being aware of them then pure awareness alone remains, and that is the Self.

(1, 298, 2, 3, 549428) This morning, a number of Gujerati visitors arrived here, evidently returning from Pondicherry, after darshan there on the 15th.
(1, 298, 2, 4, 549557) One of them asked Bhagavan, What is meant by Self realisation?
(1, 298, 2, 5, 549620) Materialists say there is no such thing as God or Self. Bhagavan said, Never mind what the materialists or others say; and dont bother about Self or God.
(1, 298, 2, 6, 549774) Do you exist or not?
(1, 298, 2, 7, 549795) What is your idea of yourself?
(1, 298, 2, 8, 549826) What do you mean by I? The visitor said he did not understand by I his body, but something within his body.
(1, 298, 2, 9, 549934) Thereupon, Bhagavan continued, You concede I is not the body but something within it.
(1, 298, 2, 10, 550020) See then from whence the I arises within the body.
(1, 298, 2, 11, 550071) See whether it arises and disappears, or is always present.
(1, 298, 2, 12, 550131) You will admit there is an I which emerges as soon as you wake up, sees the body, the world and all else, and ceases to exist when you sleep; and that there is another I which exists apart from the body, independently of it, and which alone is with you when the body and the world do not exist for you, as for instance in sleep.
(1, 298, 2, 13, 550460) Then ask yourself if you are not the same I during sleep and during the other states.
(1, 298, 2, 14, 550546) Are there two Is?
(1, 298, 2, 15, 550564) You are the same one person always.
(1, 298, 2, 16, 550600) Now, which can be real, the I which comes and goes, or the I which always abides?
(1, 298, 2, 17, 550682) Then you will know that you are the Self.
(1, 298, 2, 18, 550724) This is called Self realisation.
(1, 298, 2, 19, 550757) Self realisation is not however a state which is foreign to you, which is far from you, and which has to be reached by you.
(1, 298, 2, 20, 550881) You are always in that state.
(1, 298, 2, 21, 550911) You forget it, and identify yourself with the mind and its creation.
(1, 298, 2, 22, 550980) To cease to identify yourself with the mind is all that is required.
(1, 298, 2, 23, 551049) We have so long identified ourselves with the not Self that we find it difficult to regard ourselves as the Self.
(1, 298, 2, 24, 551163) Giving up this identification with the not Self is all
(1, 299, 0, 1, 551218) that is meant by Self realisation.
(1, 299, 0, 2, 551253) How to realise, i.e., make real, the Self?
(1, 299, 0, 3, 551296) We have realised, i.e., regarded as real, what is unreal, the not Self.
(1, 299, 0, 4, 551368) To give up such false realisation is Self realisation.
(1, 299, 1, 5, 551423) In the evening, after parayana, a visitor asked Bhagavan, How to control the wandering mind? He prefaced the question with the remark, I want to ask Bhagavan a question which is troubling me. Bhagavan replied, after laughing, This is nothing peculiar to you.
(1, 299, 1, 6, 551682) This is the question which is always asked by everybody and which is dealt with in all the books like the Gita.
(1, 299, 1, 7, 551794) What way is there, except to draw in the mind as often as it strays or goes outward, and to fix it in the Self, as the Gita advises?
(1, 299, 1, 8, 551927) Of course, it wont be easy to do it.
(1, 299, 1, 9, 551964) It will come only with practice or sadhana. The visitor said, The mind goes after only what it desires and wont get fixed on the object we set before it. Bhagavan said, Everybody will go after only what gives happiness to him.
(1, 299, 1, 10, 552191) Thinking that happiness comes from some object or other, you go after it.
(1, 299, 1, 11, 552265) See from whence all happiness, including the happiness you regard as coming from sense objects, really comes.
(1, 299, 1, 12, 552375) You will understand all happiness comes only from the Self, and then you will always abide in the Self.

(1, 304, 2, 11, 561721) It seems they had no rains for a long time then.
(1, 304, 2, 12, 561770) But on that night there was a heavy downpour.

(1, 304, 2, 14, 561879) Only that morning for the first time I had discarded all my clothes, except a cod piece and, on account of the rains beating in, and the cold winds blowing about, I found the cold unbearable, and so I ran from there and took shelter on the pial of a house nearby.

(1, 305, 2, 12, 563681) Question: It is said that the old lady Keerai Patti was born as Lakshmi.
(1, 305, 2, 13, 563754) How can one, who had the unique good fortune of serving Bhagavan well and lovingly, have to be born again at all, and even if she had to be born, how could she be born as a cow?
(1, 305, 2, 14, 563932) Is it not said in all our books that birth as a human being is the best birth one can have?

(1, 305, 4, 16, 564084) I said, I have already told Rani so.

(1, 306, 0, 1, 564204) and Bhagavan has not denied it.

I added, But she puts the question on the assumption that the cow is the old woman reborn, whether Bhagavan has said so or not, and she desires an answer. (1, 306, 0, 3, 564571) Even an animal can attain Self realisation.

(1, 308, 2, 8, 568370) Casually going through T.P.R.s notebook I came across an entry there  Mithya=Jagat; Brahma bhavam=Satyam.
(1, 308, 3, 9, 568476) As I remembered Bhagavan occasionally saying mithya means satyam, but did not quite grasp its significance, I asked Bhagavan about it.
(1, 308, 3, 10, 568611) He said, Yes.
(1, 308, 3, 11, 568625) I say that now and then.
(1, 308, 3, 12, 568650) What do you mean by real or satyam?
(1, 308, 3, 13, 568686) Which do you call real? I answered, According to Vedanta, that which is permanent and unchanging, that alone is real.
(1, 308, 3, 14, 568804) That of course is the definition of Reality. Then, Bhagavan said, These names and forms which constitute the world always change and perish.
(1, 308, 3, 15, 568945) Hence they are called mithya.
(1, 308, 3, 16, 568975) To limit the Self and regard it as these names and form is mithya.
(1, 308, 3, 17, 569042) To regard all as Self is the Reality.
(1, 308, 3, 18, 569080) The Advaitin says jagat is mithya, but he also says All this is Brahman.
(1, 308, 3, 19, 569153) So it is clear that what he condemns is regarding the world as such to be real, not regarding the world as Brahman.
(1, 308, 3, 20, 569269) He who sees the Self, sees only the Self in the world also.
(1, 308, 3, 21, 569329) To the jnani it is immaterial whether the world appears or not.
(1, 308, 3, 22, 569393) Whether it appears or not, his attention is always on the Self.
(1, 308, 3, 23, 569457) It is like the letters and the paper on which the letters are printed.
(1, 308, 3, 24, 569528) You are wholly
(1, 309, 0, 1, 569543) engrossed with the letters and have no attention left for the paper.
(1, 309, 0, 2, 569612) But the jnani thinks only of the paper as the real substratum, whether the letters appear on it or not.

(1, 313, 0, 1, 576556) few minutes, the child was suffering very much, vomiting and perspiring profusely.

(1, 313, 0, 3, 576760) In a few minutes he felt the childs pulse and advised them it would be better to take the child to Bhagavan.
(1, 313, 0, 4, 576869) They accordingly brought the child and when they entered the Asramam compound the child was in a state almost of collapse, the body having become chill and the breath almost ceasing.
(1, 313, 0, 5, 577052) They entered the hall, and told Bhagavan, and he touched the child, passing his hand all over the childs body as if soothing the child, and said, It is nothing.
(1, 313, 0, 6, 577213) He will be all right. It was only after that, the parents had some hope that the child would survive.
(1, 313, 0, 7, 577315) When they came out of the hall, they came across our Ramaswami Pillai, and he showed them another visitor who had come to the Asramam only this afternoon, who was an expert in saving people from snake bites, etc.
(1, 313, 0, 8, 577528) and pronounced some mantras on the child and declared the poison had been got rid of by his mantras.
(1, 313, 0, 9, 577629) The child recovered gradually, and the parents have told me that it was saved only through Bhagavans grace.
(1, 313, 0, 10, 577737) Another thing which may also be mentioned here is that the child himself, as soon as he felt pain, cried out, Let us go to Bhagavan.
(1, 313, 0, 11, 577870) The pain will go if we go there, though on some occasions he would even refuse to be taken to Bhagavan when the parents proposed to take him there.

(1, 314, 3, 9, 579492) This afternoon, from a book that Anandammal brought, Bhagavan was able to find out the story of how Goraknath killed his Master Maschendras child, etc., which Bhagavan was trying to trace on the 5th instant after having seen the film Bhartruhari the previous night.
(1, 314, 3, 10, 579758) In this story it is said that Chandu Nath wanted to write to Goraknath, but not being sure how to address him, in a patronising manner as a superior, or as a junior writing to a senior, finally sent a blank piece of paper.
(1, 314, 3, 11, 579981) In this connection, Bhagavan said, This reminds me of an incident in my boyhood.
(1, 314, 3, 12, 580062) I was quite young and did not know much about letter writing and I wrote to my aunts son (fathers sisters son) aneka asirvadam (i.e., many blessings, in the manner of an elder giving his blessings).
(1, 314, 3, 13, 580261) When he came, he ridiculed me for having sent blessings to him (who was about 10 years older than myself).
(1, 314, 3, 14, 580368) But I did not know then who should bless whom.
(1, 314, 3, 15, 580415) I only knew
(1, 315, 0, 1, 580427) that whenever my father wrote to him, he used to write My blessings to Ramu, and so I thought that was the way a letter ought to be written.
(1, 315, 0, 2, 580568) That to some, blessings had to be given and to others salutations  I did not know then.

(1, 316, 5, 11, 583112) Dilip Kumar Roy of Aurobindos Ashram came here last night, and this morning he sang a few songs before Bhagavan.
(1, 316, 5, 12, 583225) Later when Bhagavan was perusing The New Times of today, he read out to us that at Mount Abu, two serpents fought each other, that one vanquished the other which became unconscious and at that stage a boy who came across the scene did some first aid to the defeated serpent and put a cold bandage over it, that the injured serpent slowly revived, that seeing all this, the victor serpent was enraged and bit the boy, that the vanquished snake, which had by now recovered and revived under the boys treatment, ran to the boy, sucked out the other serpents poison and saved the boy.
(1, 316, 5, 13, 583806) When Bhagavan read all this out to us, I said, It looks incredible. Mrs. T. to whom T.P.R. recounted the story also remarked, Is this a story or what? Then Dilip asked Bhagavan whether all this was possible.
(1, 316, 5, 14, 584014) Bhagavan said, Why not?
(1, 316, 5, 15, 584038) Quite possible.
(1, 317, 0, 1, 584054) Roy even asked, How could the vanquished snake know and do all this? Bhagavan said, Why?
(1, 317, 0, 2, 584143) It was watching what the boy did to it, what the other snake did to the boy and so it ran and sucked out the poison.
(1, 317, 0, 3, 584260) Snakes see and observe and can do such things.
(1, 317, 0, 4, 584307) Many stories like this have been told of serpents.

(1, 318, 1, 10, 586697) This evening, D.S. Sarma, asked Bhagavan: In Western mysticism three definite stages are often spoken of  viz., Purgation, illumination and union.
(1, 318, 1, 11, 586844) Was there any such stage as purgation  corresponding to what we call sadhana  in Bhagavans life? Bhagavan replied, I have never done any sadhana.
(1, 318, 1, 12, 586990) I did not even know what sadhana was.
(1, 318, 1, 13, 587028) Only long afterwards I came to know what sadhana was and how many different kinds of it there were.
(1, 318, 1, 14, 587128) It is only if there was any object or anything different from me that I could think of it.
(1, 318, 1, 15, 587219) Only if there was a goal to attain, I should have made sadhana to attain that goal.
(1, 318, 1, 16, 587303) There was nothing which I wanted to obtain.
(1, 318, 1, 17, 587347) I am now sitting with my eyes open.
(1, 318, 1, 18, 587383) I was then sitting with my eyes closed.
(1, 318, 1, 19, 587423) That was all the difference.
(1, 318, 1, 20, 587452) I was not doing any sadhana even then.
(1, 318, 1, 21, 587491) As I sat with my eyes closed, people said I was in samadhi.
(1, 318, 1, 22, 587551) As I was not talking, they said I was in mauna.
(1, 318, 1, 23, 587599) The fact is, I did nothing.
(1, 318, 1, 24, 587627) Some Higher Power took hold of me and I was entirely in Its hand. Bhagavan further added, The books no doubt speak of sravana, manana, nididhyasana, samadhi and sakshatkara.
(1, 318, 1, 25, 587801) We are always sakshat and what is there for one to attain karam of that?
(1, 318, 1, 26, 587874) We call this world sakshat or pratyaksha.
(1, 318, 1, 27, 587916) What is changing, what appears and disappears, what is not sakshat, we
(1, 319, 0, 1, 587987) regard as sakshat.
(1, 319, 0, 2, 588006) We are always and nothing can be more directly present pratyaksha than we, and about that we say we have to attain sakshatkaram after all these sadhanas.
(1, 319, 0, 3, 588160) Nothing can be more strange than this.
(1, 319, 0, 4, 588199) The Self is not attained by doing anything, but remaining still and being as we are.

(1, 322, 0, 1, 594034) Vasudeva Sastri recounted another incident, which he had seen:
(1, 322, 1, 2, 594097) One day, when we were at Skandasramam, I was aghast to find a scorpion climbing up over Bhagavans body in the front and another at the same time climbing down his back.
(1, 322, 1, 3, 594266) I was terrified and wanted to do something.
(1, 322, 1, 4, 594310) But Bhagavan remained calm, as if nothing happened, and the two scorpions, after crawling over his body as if over a wall, eventually left him.
(1, 322, 1, 5, 594454) After they left, Bhagavan explained to us, They crawl over you just as they would crawl on the floor or a wall or tree.
(1, 322, 1, 6, 594574) Do they crawl over these, stinging as they go?
(1, 322, 1, 7, 594621) It is only because you fear them and do something that they fear you and do something in return.

(1, 322, 3, 9, 594762) This afternoon Bhagavan spoke of his days at Pachaiamman Koil, when he had to remind the office to send a reply to a relation of Rangachari (who used to go to Bhagavan daily in those days, and remained with him, during the plague scare, at the above Pachaiamman Koil).
(1, 322, 3, 10, 595031) Bhagavan said, On account of plague, the whole town was completely evacuated for six months.
(1, 322, 3, 11, 595124) There was a staff of about two hundred people who went on daily disinfecting house after house and they lived in two camps, one of about one hundred and fifty near Chetti Kolam Koil and another of fifty at the other end of the town.
(1, 322, 3, 12, 595357) I stayed at Pachaiamman Koil, with two or three others.
(1, 322, 3, 13, 595413) The disinfecting staff used to go to me frequently.
(1, 322, 3, 14, 595465) They said they were going to organise a bhajana at the end of their stay and that I should attend it.
(1, 322, 3, 15, 595567) I did not say I would not go, thinking their proposed bhajana might not come off at all.
(1, 322, 3, 16, 595656) But one night, suddenly, a party of thirty or forty people with torches in their hands came up to us, after we had gone to sleep, and woke us up.
(1, 322, 3, 17, 595802) I asked, What is the matter? Then they revealed that the bhajana had been arranged, that everything was ready and that I should go with them.
(1, 322, 3, 18, 595944) I could not say No when so
(1, 323, 0, 1, 595971) many of them came like that, and so I went.
(1, 323, 0, 2, 596015) They had made elaborate arrangements.
(1, 323, 0, 3, 596053) So many lights, so many eatables, so many garlands and musicians of repute sent for from various places.
(1, 323, 0, 4, 596158) They had arranged a seat for me and another platform for those who were to do bhajana.
(1, 323, 0, 5, 596245) They garlanded me.
(1, 323, 0, 6, 596264) All the people in the town were there.
(1, 323, 0, 7, 596303) All the benches and chairs also were there.
(1, 323, 0, 8, 596347) Several of the people assembled there were also drunk and so they were all in high spirits.
(1, 323, 0, 9, 596439) I remained with them for some time and then took leave and came away.
(1, 323, 0, 10, 596509) Some of them again came back with me with their torches and left me at Pachaiamman Koil and returned.
(1, 323, 1, 11, 596611) T.S.R. then asked, It seems Bhagavan once had a dream and saw so many siddhas assembled before him, that they looked all familiar to him and that he sat there on a dais with chinmudra. Bhagavan replied, Is that the only thing?
(1, 323, 1, 12, 596838) I have seen several such visions.
(1, 323, 1, 13, 596872) What am I to say? He continued, Once I came across a sunai (spring in a cave); I went towards it.
(1, 323, 1, 14, 596970) As I approached, it was getting wider, and there were trees on either side.
(1, 323, 1, 15, 597046) It became broader and broader.
(1, 323, 1, 16, 597077) There was good light and the passage led to a big tank.
(1, 323, 1, 17, 597133) In the middle of the tank was a temple. I asked, This was not a dream? Bhagavan said, Whether it was a dream or jagrat (waking), call it what you like. (Somasundaram Pillai says the words Bhagavan used were L]Y, LhV).
(1, 323, 1, 18, 597351) Bhagavan also recounted that after he came here, within the last six years or so, he saw huge streets, lined with imposing houses on either side leading to the Asramam; that Chadwick and others were following him in that dream, and Bhagavan asked Chadwick, Can anyone call all this a dream? and that Chadwick replied, Which fool will call all this a dream? At that stage, he woke up.
(1, 323, 1, 19, 597735) When Bhagavan distinctly calls this a dream and the previous experience he leaves to others to call, dream or waking, I am led to believe that the other vision of the tank and temple was in the waking or some other stage, which was not dream.
(1, 324, 0, 1, 597978) Mr. T.V. Krishnaswami Aiyer asked, Were Bhagavans brother and others aware of Bhagavans absorption in the Self and indifference to external things? Bhagavan said, Yes.
(1, 324, 0, 2, 598146) They could not but be aware.
(1, 324, 0, 3, 598175) For though I tried my best to appear as if I was attending to external affairs, I could not succeed fully in the attempt.
(1, 324, 0, 4, 598297) I would sit down to read like others, open a book, pretend to read it and after some time turn the page.
(1, 324, 0, 5, 598402) Similarly, after some time I would take up another book.
(1, 324, 0, 6, 598459) But all knew that my attitude had changed.
(1, 324, 0, 7, 598502) They used to make fun of me for this abstraction of mine.
(1, 324, 0, 8, 598560) I never took offence, as I was totally indifferent to their taunts.
(1, 324, 0, 9, 598628) This encouraged them to go on with their mockery.
(1, 324, 0, 10, 598678) If I was so minded, I could have silenced them all with one blow.
(1, 324, 0, 11, 598744) But I did not care at all.
(1, 324, 0, 12, 598771) After the death experience I was living in a different world.
(1, 324, 0, 13, 598833) How could I turn my attention to books?
(1, 324, 0, 14, 598873) Before that, I would at least attend to what the other boys repeated and repeat the same myself.
(1, 324, 0, 15, 598970) But afterwards, I could not do even that.
(1, 324, 0, 16, 599012) At school, my mind would not dwell on study at all.
(1, 324, 0, 17, 599064) I would be imagining and expecting God would suddenly drop down from Heaven before me.
(1, 324, 1, 18, 599151) Someone asked Bhagavan whether he deliberately went in for a study of Periapuranam.
(1, 324, 1, 19, 599235) Thereupon Bhagavan said, No.
(1, 324, 1, 20, 599264) It was a mere accident.
(1, 324, 1, 21, 599288) A relation of mine, my uncle, was given the book by a swami who was living near our house and was advised to read it.
(1, 324, 1, 22, 599406) Thus the book happened to be in our house and, coming across it, I looked into it first out of curiosity and then, becoming interested, read the whole book.
(1, 324, 1, 23, 599563) It made a great impression on me.
(1, 324, 1, 24, 599597) Before that, the sixty three images of the Nayanars in the temple were mere images and no more.
(1, 324, 1, 25, 599693) But afterwards, they gained new significance for me.

(1, 325, 0, 1, 600062) before those images?

(1, 325, 0, 3, 600173) I only wanted the same grace as was shown to those saints.
(1, 325, 0, 4, 600232) I prayed I should have the same bhakti that they had.
(1, 325, 0, 5, 600286) I knew nothing of freedom from births or bondage.

(1, 325, 2, 7, 600380) This afternoon, a visitor asked Bhagavan, No doubt the method taught by Bhagavan is direct.
(1, 325, 2, 8, 600472) But it is so difficult.
(1, 325, 2, 9, 600496) We do not know how to begin it.
(1, 325, 2, 10, 600528) If we go on asking, Who am I? Who am I? like a japa, with Who am I? for mantra, it becomes dull.
(1, 325, 2, 11, 600625) In other methods, there is something preliminary and positive with which one can begin and then go step by step.
(1, 325, 2, 12, 600738) But in Bhagavans method, there is no such thing, and to seek the Self at once, though direct, is difficult.
(1, 325, 3, 13, 600846) Bhagavan: You yourself concede, it is the direct method.
(1, 325, 3, 14, 600903) It is the direct and easy method.
(1, 325, 3, 15, 600937) When going after other things, alien to us, is so easy, how can it be difficult for one to go to ones own Self?
(1, 325, 3, 16, 601049) You talk of Where to begin.
(1, 325, 3, 17, 601077) There is no beginning and no end.
(1, 325, 3, 18, 601111) You are yourself the beginning and the end.
(1, 325, 3, 19, 601155) If you are here and the Self somewhere else, and you have to reach that Self, you may be told how to start, how to travel and then how to reach.
(1, 325, 3, 20, 601300) Suppose you who are now in Ramana Asramam ask, I want to go to Ramana Asramam.
(1, 325, 3, 21, 601379) How shall I start and how to reach it?, what is one to say?
(1, 325, 3, 22, 601439) A mans search for the Self is like that.
(1, 325, 3, 23, 601480) He is always the Self and nothing else.
(1, 325, 3, 24, 601520) You say Who am I? becomes a japa.
(1, 325, 3, 25, 601554) It is not meant that you should go on asking Who am I? In that case, thought will not so easily die.
(1, 325, 3, 26, 601655) All japas are intended, by the use of one thought, the mantra, to exclude all other thoughts.
(1, 325, 3, 27, 601749) This, japa eventually does for a man.
(1, 325, 3, 28, 601787) All other thoughts, except the thought of the mantra, gradually die and then even that one thought dies.
(1, 325, 3, 29, 601892) Our Self is of the nature of japa.
(1, 325, 3, 30, 601927) Japa is always going on there.
(1, 325, 3, 31, 601958) If we give up all thoughts, we shall find japa is always there
(1, 326, 0, 1, 602021) without any effort on our part.
(1, 326, 0, 2, 602053) In the direct method, as you call it, by saying ask yourself Who am I? you are told to concentrate within yourself where the I thought (the root of all other thoughts) arises.
(1, 326, 0, 3, 602229) As the Self is not outside but inside you, you are asked to dive within, instead of going without, and what can be more easy than going to yourself?
(1, 326, 0, 4, 602378) But the fact remains that to some this method will seem difficult and will not appeal.
(1, 326, 0, 5, 602465) That is why so many different methods have been taught.
(1, 326, 0, 6, 602521) Each of them will appeal to some as the best and easiest.
(1, 326, 0, 7, 602579) That is according to their pakva or fitness.
(1, 326, 0, 8, 602624) But to some, nothing except the vichara marga will appeal.
(1, 326, 0, 9, 602683) They will ask, You want me to know or to see this or that.
(1, 326, 0, 10, 602742) But who is the knower, the seer? Whatever other method may be chosen, there will be always a doer.
(1, 326, 0, 11, 602841) That cannot be escaped.
(1, 326, 0, 12, 602865) Who is that doer must be found out.
(1, 326, 0, 13, 602901) Till that, the sadhana cannot be ended.
(1, 326, 0, 14, 602941) So eventually, all must come to find out Who am I?.
(1, 326, 0, 15, 602993) You complain that there is nothing preliminary or positive to start with.
(1, 326, 0, 16, 603067) You have the I to start with.
(1, 326, 0, 17, 603097) You know you exist always, whereas the body does not exist always, e.g., in sleep.
(1, 326, 0, 18, 603180) Sleep reveals that you exist even without a body.
(1, 326, 0, 19, 603230) We identify the I with a body, we regard the Self as having a body, and as having limits, and hence all our trouble.
(1, 326, 0, 20, 603347) All that we have to do is to give up identifying our Self with the body, with forms and limits, and then we shall know ourselves as the Self that we always are.
(1, 326, 1, 21, 603508) The visitor further asked, May I believe that there is nothing more to be known now, so far as the technique of sadhana is concerned, than that which has been written in your books from time to time?
(1, 326, 1, 22, 603708) This question arises from the fact that, in all other systems of sadhana, the sadguru unfolds some secret technique of meditation to his disciple at the time of initiation or diksha, as it is called.

(1, 326, 2, 24, 603981) No secret technique.
(1, 326, 2, 25, 604002) It is all an open secret, in this system.

(1, 332, 3, 8, 614253) In the afternoon, when I entered the hall about 3 p.m., Dr. Roy was asking Bhagavan, In the case of persons who are not capable of long meditation, will it not be enough if they engage themselves in doing good to others? Bhagavan replied, Yes, it will do.
(1, 332, 3, 9, 614509) The idea of good will be at their heart.
(1, 332, 3, 10, 614550) That is enough.
(1, 332, 3, 11, 614566) Good, God, Love, are all the same thing.
(1, 332, 3, 12, 614607) If the person keeps continuously thinking of anyone of these, it will be enough.
(1, 332, 3, 13, 614688) All meditation is for the purpose of keeping out all other thoughts. After some pause, Bhagavan said, When one realises the Truth and knows that there is neither the seer nor the seen, but only the Self that transcends both, that the Self alone is the screen or the substratum on which the shadow both of the ego and all that it sees, come and go, the feeling that one has not got eyesight, and that therefore one misses the sight of various things, will vanish.
(1, 332, 3, 14, 615151) The realised being, though he has normal eyesight, does not see all these things. (He sees only the Self and nothing but the Self).
(1, 332, 4, 15, 615283) After further discussion with Dr. Roy, Bhagavan added, There is nothing wrong in seeing anything, this body or the world.
(1, 332, 4, 16, 615405) The mistake lies in thinking you are the body.
(1, 332, 4, 17, 615452) There is no harm in thinking the body is in you.
(1, 332, 4, 18, 615501) The body, world, all
(1, 333, 0, 1, 615522) must be in the Self; or rather nothing can exist apart from the Self, as no pictures can be seen without the screen on which the shadows can be cast. In answer to a question as to what is the best way to the goal, Bhagavan said, There is no goal to be reached.
(1, 333, 0, 2, 615783) There is nothing to be attained.
(1, 333, 0, 3, 615816) You are the Self.
(1, 333, 0, 4, 615834) You exist always.
(1, 333, 0, 5, 615852) Nothing more can be predicated of the Self than that it exists.
(1, 333, 0, 6, 615916) Seeing God or the Self is only being the Self or yourself.
(1, 333, 0, 7, 615975) Seeing is being.
(1, 333, 0, 8, 615992) You, being the Self, want to know how to attain the Self.
(1, 333, 0, 9, 616050) It is something like a man being at Ramanasramam asking how many ways are there to reach Ramanasramam and which is the best way for him.
(1, 333, 0, 10, 616187) All that is required of you is to give up the thought that you are this body and to give up all thoughts of the external things or the not Self.
(1, 333, 0, 11, 616332) As often as the mind goes out towards outward objects, prevent it and fix it in the Self or I.
(1, 333, 0, 12, 616427) That is all the effort required on your part.
(1, 333, 0, 13, 616473) The different methods prescribed by different thinkers are all agreed on this.
(1, 333, 0, 14, 616552) The Advaita, Dvaita, Visishtadvaita schools and other schools all agree that the mind must give up thinking of external things and must think of the Self, or God as they may call it.
(1, 333, 0, 15, 616735) That is called meditation.
(1, 333, 0, 16, 616762) But meditation being our nature, you will find when you realise the Self that what was once the means is now the goal, that while once you had to make an effort, now you cannot get away from the Self even if you want.

(1, 333, 2, 18, 617029) This afternoon a visitor from Shimoga asked Bhagavan, How to still the tossing mind? Bhagavan replied, Who asks this question?
(1, 333, 2, 19, 617156) Is it the mind or you? The visitor said, The mind.
(1, 333, 3, 20, 617207) Bhagavan: If you see what this mind is, it will be stilled.
(1, 333, 4, 21, 617267) Visitor: How to see what the mind is?
(1, 333, 5, 22, 617305) Bhagavan: What is your idea of the mind?
(1, 333, 6, 23, 617346) Visitor: My idea is, it is thought.
(1, 334, 0, 1, 617382) Bhagavan: The mind is a bundle of thoughts.
(1, 334, 0, 2, 617426) But the source of all thoughts is the I thought.
(1, 334, 0, 3, 617475) So if you try to find out who this I is, the mind will disappear.
(1, 334, 0, 4, 617541) The mind will exist only so long as you think of external things.
(1, 334, 0, 5, 617607) But when you draw it from external things and make it think of the mind or I  in other words introvert it  it ceases to exist.
(1, 334, 1, 6, 617734) 25 1 25 1 25 1 25 1 25 10 46 0 46 0 46 0 46 0 46
(1, 334, 2, 7, 617783) For the last three or four days, Mr. Subba Rao has been reading out in the hall his Life of Bhagavan in Telugu.
(1, 334, 2, 8, 617895) He has mentioned various new things in this book.
(1, 334, 2, 9, 617945) One is, that the mongoose which came to Bhagavan when he was on the Hill was golden coloured.
(1, 334, 2, 10, 618039) S. also says that Nayana had told him that the mongoose was none other than God Arunachala come to see Bhagavan.
(1, 334, 2, 11, 618152) Another thing I have not recorded before is found in this Life by S. It seems Nayana used to say that dogs cannot long survive contact with a person like Bhagavan whose granthi (knot) has been sundered; and that he used to drive away all dogs.
(1, 334, 2, 12, 618396) In this connection, Bhagavan said, Yes, he used to drive the dogs away.
(1, 334, 2, 13, 618468) But there was an exception.
(1, 334, 2, 14, 618496) It was a dog we used to call Neela.
(1, 334, 2, 15, 618532) She used to come and always sit on my lap.
(1, 334, 2, 16, 618575) But she would not allow any other dog, even her own mother or sisters and brothers, to pass beyond the gate of the Skandasramam.
(1, 334, 2, 17, 618704) Nayana used to say, This has been born a dog by mistake.
(1, 334, 3, 18, 618761) S. has also recorded that whatever Nayana said always came true, and cited an event in his own life to prove this.
(1, 334, 4, 19, 618876) 26 1 26 1 26 1 26 1 26 10 46 0 46 0 46 0 46 0 46
(1, 334, 5, 20, 618925) The morning tapal had brought a letter signed Kannan.
(1, 334, 5, 21, 618979) Bhagavan read the letter but was not sure who wrote it.
(1, 334, 5, 22, 619035) In the afternoon, he sent for the cover in which it came and from various facts made sure the writer was Mr. Krishnamurti of Madura College, son of Mr. Ranganatha Aiyer.
(1, 335, 0, 1, 619205) Bhagavans suggestion, Viswanath added to a letter that was being sent today to Mr. Ranganatha Iyer, Tell Mr. Krishnamurti that the Kannan who escaped detection this morning when the tapals were read was discovered this evening and brought into publicity.
(1, 335, 1, 2, 619460) The following is the English translation of Kannans letter as made by Mr. T.P.R, and myself the next day:
(1, 335, 2, 3, 619566) Oh Emperor Supreme, Ramana, who rules the world under the canopy of universal sovereignty, seated on the throne of the Heart!
(1, 335, 2, 4, 619692) That day you graciously said: Oh child, you being our beloved son, we bestow kingship on you.
(1, 335, 2, 5, 619786) Assuming this sovereignty, be you happy!
(1, 335, 3, 6, 619827) I am seated in the audience hall.
(1, 335, 3, 7, 619861) There have gathered the Prime Minister, mind, the assistant ministers, viz., the five sense organs, and the heads of executive authority, viz., five organs of action.
(1, 335, 3, 8, 620028) Before me, they are making noise as they please.
(1, 335, 3, 9, 620077) They daringly defy my authority.
(1, 335, 3, 10, 620110) Often and suddenly, they darken the audience hall.
(1, 335, 3, 11, 620161) If I say, Enough.
(1, 335, 3, 12, 620179) Leave me alone, all of you, and get away, they are indulging in obstructive tactics and say that they will not go.
(1, 335, 3, 13, 620294) I am having endless trouble.
(1, 335, 3, 14, 620323) Enough for me, this kingship devoid of power.
(1, 335, 3, 15, 620369) I have surrendered this kingship unto the Lotus Feet of Ramana who is my father and Master.
(1, 335, 4, 16, 620461) Bhagavan should release me and give his gracious protection or else teach me the secret of sovereignty, granting the necessary power.
(1, 335, 5, 17, 620595) Oh King, Refuge, Refuge, Refuge I crave.
(1, 335, 6, 18, 620636) Kannan.
(1, 335, 7, 19, 620644) You gave me refuge, saying, Child, when the bell of extroversion rings, the assembly will gather.
(1, 335, 7, 20, 620742) In the audience
(1, 336, 0, 1, 620758) hall, be ever raising the incense of vichara or enquiry.
(1, 336, 0, 2, 620815) Mind, the minister, is a drunkard.
(1, 336, 0, 3, 620850) Confusing himself with the intoxication of thought, he will keep confusing the assembly as well.
(1, 336, 0, 4, 620947) This incense of vichara will clear the intoxication of thought.
(1, 336, 0, 5, 621011) The assembly will function in order.
(1, 336, 0, 6, 621048) As this incense of vichara increases more and more, those assembled will take leave.
(1, 336, 0, 7, 621133) When the bell of abidance rings, mind will finally disappear.
(1, 336, 0, 8, 621195) All that incense of vichara transformed into light, you will abide as yourself, alone and blessed.
(1, 336, 1, 9, 621294) Therefore, you should not give up even for a moment this Self Enquiry of Who am I? With the progressive increase of vichara, jagrat and swapna will merge in sahaja nirvikalpa samadhi.
(1, 336, 1, 10, 621478) All sleep will become kevala nirvikalpa samadhi.
(1, 336, 1, 11, 621527) The vichara will merge in swarupa.
(1, 336, 3, 12, 621562) Ramana, my mother and father, you gave me the sword of jnana, termed vichara.
(1, 336, 3, 13, 621640) Grant to this humble self, that has sought refuge at your feet, the necessary desirelessness to lay low and destroy the demon of thought as and when it arises, with determination, and without any pity or compassion.
(1, 336, 4, 14, 621856) Lord, I surrender myself.
(1, 336, 5, 15, 621882) Kannan.
(1, 336, 6, 16, 621890) Mr. Thiagaraja Iyer, Official Receiver of Madras, who was in the hall, asked Bhagavan, Is this all imagination, the creation of the writers fancy, or real? Bhagavan replied, We dont know.
(1, 336, 6, 17, 622078) How can we say anything? Next Bhagavan asked me to read out an article entitled Ramanas Grace which was not in the first edition of the Souvenir Volume, but has been included in the second Edition, which arrived here yesterday or so.
(1, 336, 6, 18, 622312) I read it out accordingly.

(1, 337, 0, 1, 622423) experience of the Self or the awareness of I, in Bhagavans hall for some little time, and describes it vividly and in detail.
(1, 337, 0, 2, 622549) After I finished reading the article, Bhagavan remarked in answer to Mr. T. Iyers original question, Now, what are we to say about this?
(1, 337, 0, 3, 622686) Was it all real or fancy?
(1, 337, 1, 4, 622712) In the evening, after parayana, Alamelu Ammal got up and told Bhagavan that she was present at Seshadri Swamis samadhi, this morning when the following incident took place.
(1, 337, 1, 5, 622885) She said, The party from Coimbatore including the man who says Seshadri Swami is speaking and writing through him on a planchette came to the samadhi and found the place locked.
(1, 337, 1, 6, 623063) They went round the samadhi shrine three times and meanwhile Thiruvengadam Pillai, the retired Police constable who is in charge of the shrine, came and opened the temple.

(1, 337, 1, 8, 623367) There was some writing produced by the planchette.

(1, 337, 2, 18, 624332) It is a pity he does not come and speak to us.

(1, 338, 2, 5, 624933) So I waited and went in along with others at about 2 55 p.m.

(1, 338, 2, 7, 625234) Today, it was obvious, the pain was severe.
(1, 338, 2, 8, 625278) But he made light of it and would not allow anything else to be done for it.

(1, 338, 2, 10, 625435) Seeing this, I suggested to friends that we could all clear out of the hall and leave Bhagavan to lie down if he felt like that.
(1, 338, 2, 11, 625564) But Bhagavan would not allow it.
(1, 338, 2, 12, 625597) A little later, Dr. Anantanarayana Rao came into the hall, and he offered to massage the part and give some relief.
(1, 338, 2, 13, 625713) Bhagavan however would not have it and humorously remarked, It is enough the matter has reached your ears.
(1, 338, 2, 14, 625820) Your hands need not be employed.
(1, 338, 2, 15, 625853) I am already feeling better. (This was in reference to our common belief that if we have any trouble it is enough if our complaint reaches Bhagavans ears).
(1, 338, 2, 16, 626009) Bhagavan continued to have this pain at intervals till we left the hall at 7 30 p.m.

(1, 341, 6, 19, 630894) The following was supplied to me by Mr. G.V. Subba Rao.
(1, 341, 6, 20, 630950) A visitor introduced by T.S.R. asked Bhagavan whether by doing annual ceremonies, etc., to the dead, we can confer any benefit on them.
(1, 341, 6, 21, 631086) To this Bhagavan replied, Yes.
(1, 341, 6, 22, 631117) It all depends on ones belief.
(1, 341, 7, 23, 631148) Mr. Somasundaram Pillais version of the above question and answer is given below:
(1, 341, 8, 24, 631230) Question: If such rites as the annual ceremony performed by descendants are able to do away with the karma of the
(1, 342, 0, 1, 631344) dead, it seems to strike at the root of the theory of karma.
(1, 342, 0, 2, 631405) For then a man may escape the evil consequences of his bad acts through the help of the rites performed by his sons, etc.
(1, 342, 1, 3, 631527) Answer: Such rites only help the deceased to a small extent.
(1, 342, 1, 4, 631588) It is on the same principle that prayaschittam and good deeds are said to mitigate the evil consequences of ones bad actions.
(1, 342, 2, 5, 631714) After the visitor went away I asked Bhagavan, Till three years ago, I was under the impression that doing annual ceremonies to the dead would confer benefit on them so long as they are not reborn. Bhagavan intervened with the remark, They will receive benefit though they are reborn several times and there is an agency to look after all this.
(1, 342, 2, 6, 632058) Of course, Jnana marga does not say all this. After a while I said, Bhagavan used to say that if one believes in the existence of this world, one should also believe in the existence of other worlds. Bhagavan said that it was so.
(1, 342, 2, 7, 632288) I asked, The jnani transcends all stages and he is not bound by any karma (vidhi or nisheda).
(1, 342, 2, 8, 632382) The ajnani should do his own dharma prescribed by sastras till he gets jnana.
(1, 342, 2, 9, 632460) But while he is attempting to reach jnana, will he be held responsible for the consequences of not doing the ordinary karma or will he be presumed to have done all this karma, just as a person reading in a higher class is presumed to have finished the lower classes? Bhagavan said, It depends on the superiority of the path one pursues.
(1, 342, 2, 10, 632797) Unless a person has finished (in this or previous births) the other paths, he will not pursue the jnana path; and he need not bother himself that he has not done the various karmas prescribed by sastras.
(1, 342, 2, 11, 633001) But he should not wilfully transgress the sastraic injunctions by doing things prohibited by them.
(1, 342, 3, 12, 633100) 111119 1 9 1 9 1 9 1 9 11 46 1 46 1 46 1 46 1 46
(1, 342, 4, 13, 633149) About 10 30 a.m.
(1, 342, 4, 14, 633166) today a visitor asked Bhagavan, The realised man has no further karma.
(1, 342, 4, 15, 633237) He is not bound by his karma.
(1, 343, 0, 1, 633267) Why should he still remain with his body? Bhagavan replied, Who asks this question?
(1, 343, 0, 2, 633351) Is it the realised man or the ajnani?
(1, 343, 0, 3, 633389) Why should you bother what the jnani does or why he does anything?
(1, 343, 0, 4, 633456) You look after yourself. A little later he added, You are under the impression you are the body.
(1, 343, 0, 5, 633553) So you think the jnani also has a body.
(1, 343, 0, 6, 633593) Does the jnani say he has a body?
(1, 343, 0, 7, 633627) He may look to you as having a body and doing things with the body, as others do.
(1, 343, 0, 8, 633709) The burnt rope still looks like a rope, but it cant serve as a rope if you try to bind anything with it.
(1, 343, 0, 9, 633814) So long as one identifies oneself with the body, all this is difficult to understand.
(1, 343, 0, 10, 633900) That is why it is sometimes said in reply to such questions, The body of the jnani will continue till the force of prarabdha works itself out, and after the prarabdha is exhausted it will drop off.
(1, 343, 0, 11, 634098) An illustration made use of in this connection is that of an arrow already discharged which will continue to advance and strike its target.
(1, 343, 0, 12, 634238) But the truth is the jnani has transcended all karmas, including the prarabdha karma, and he is not bound by the body or its karmas.
(1, 343, 1, 13, 634371) The visitor also asked, When a man realises the Self, what will he see? Bhagavan replied, There is no seeing.
(1, 343, 1, 14, 634481) Seeing is only Being.
(1, 343, 1, 15, 634503) The state of Self realisation, as we call it, is not attaining something new or reaching some goal which is far away, but simply being that which you always are and which you always have been.
(1, 343, 1, 16, 634696) All that is needed is that you give up your realisation of the not true as true.
(1, 343, 1, 17, 634777) All of us are realising, i.e., regarding as real, that which is not real.
(1, 343, 1, 18, 634851) We have only to give up this practice on our part.
(1, 343, 1, 19, 634902) Then we shall realise the Self as the Self, or in other words, Be the Self.
(1, 343, 1, 20, 634978) At one stage one would laugh at oneself that one tried to discover the Self which is so self evident.
(1, 343, 1, 21, 635080) So, what can we say to this question?
(1, 343, 2, 22, 635118) That stage transcends the seer and the seen.
(1, 343, 2, 23, 635163) There is no seer there to see anything.
(1, 343, 2, 24, 635203) The seer who is seeing all this now ceases to exist and the Self alone remains.
(1, 344, 0, 1, 635283) 23 1 23 1 23 1 23 1 23 11 46 1 46 1 46 1 46 1 46
(1, 344, 1, 2, 635332) A letter was received from Dr. Mees in which he has described all his doings and experiences at Madura and Tiruchuzhi.
(1, 344, 1, 3, 635451) He says there, besides other things, I went from the place where the river has joined the ocean (Tiruvannamalai), to the source of the river (Tiruchuzhi), past the place where the river came down as a waterfall to the level of the ocean (Madura).
(1, 344, 2, 4, 635698) 222224 1 4 1 4 1 4 1 4 11 46 1 46 1 46 1 46 1 46
(1, 344, 3, 5, 635747) Mrs. Chenoy (from Bombay) asked Bhagavan this evening (after reading Who am I?) whether it was the proper thing to do if she asked herself Who am I? and told herself she was not this body but a spirit, a spark from the divine flame.
(1, 344, 3, 6, 635980) Bhagavan first said, Yes, you might do that or whatever appeals to you.
(1, 344, 3, 7, 636052) It will come right in the end. But, after a little while, he told her: There is a stage in the beginning, when you identify yourself with the body, when you are still having the body consciousness.
(1, 344, 3, 8, 636250) At that stage, you have the feeling you are different from the reality or God, and then it is, you think of yourself as a devotee of God or as a servant or lover of God.
(1, 344, 3, 9, 636420) This is the first stage.
(1, 344, 3, 10, 636445) The second stage is when you think of yourself as a spark of the divine fire or a ray from the divine Sun.
(1, 344, 3, 11, 636552) Even then there is still that sense of difference and the body consciousness.
(1, 344, 3, 12, 636630) The third stage will come when all such difference ceases to exist, and you realise that the Self alone exists.
(1, 344, 3, 13, 636742) There is an I which comes and goes, and another I which always exists and abides.
(1, 344, 3, 14, 636824) So long as the first I exists, the body consciousness and the sense of diversity or bheda buddhi will persist.
(1, 344, 3, 15, 636935) Only when that I dies, the reality will reveal itself.
(1, 344, 3, 16, 636990) For instance, in sleep, the first I does not exist.
(1, 344, 3, 17, 637042) You are not then conscious of a body or the world.
(1, 344, 3, 18, 637093) Only when that I again comes up, as soon as you get out of sleep, do you become conscious of the body and this world.
(1, 344, 3, 19, 637211) But in sleep you alone existed.
(1, 344, 3, 20, 637243) For, when you wake up, you are able to say I
(1, 345, 0, 1, 637288) slept soundly. You, that wake up and say so, are the same that existed during sleep.
(1, 345, 0, 2, 637373) You dont say that the I which persisted during sleep was a different I from the I present in the waking state.
(1, 345, 0, 3, 637484) That I which persists always and does not come and go is the reality.
(1, 345, 0, 4, 637554) The other I which disappears in sleep is not real.
(1, 345, 0, 5, 637605) One should try and realise in the waking state that state which unconsciously everyone attains in sleep, the state where the small I disappears and the real I alone is. At this stage, Mrs. C. Asked, But how is it to be done? Bhagavan replied, By enquiring from whence and how does this small I arise.
(1, 345, 0, 6, 637906) The root of all bheda buddhi is this I.
(1, 345, 0, 7, 637946) It is at the root of all thoughts.
(1, 345, 0, 8, 637981) If you enquire wherefrom it arises, it disappears.
(1, 345, 1, 9, 638032) Mrs. C. then asked, Am I not then to say (in answer to my own question Who am I?) I am not this body but a spirit etc.? Bhagavan then said, No.
(1, 345, 1, 10, 638176) The enquiry Who am I? means really the enquiry within oneself as to wherefrom within the body the I thought arises.
(1, 345, 1, 11, 638292) If you concentrate your attention on such an enquiry, the I thought being the root of all other thoughts, all thoughts will be destroyed and then the Self or the Big I alone will remain as ever.
(1, 345, 1, 12, 638487) You do not get anything new, or reach somewhere where you were not before.
(1, 345, 1, 13, 638562) When all other thoughts which were hiding the Self are removed, the Self shines by itself.
(1, 345, 2, 14, 638653) Mrs. C. then referred to the portion in the book (Who am I ?) where it is said, Even if you keep on saying I, I, it will take you to the Self or reality and asked whether that was not the proper thing to be done.
(1, 345, 2, 15, 638866) I explained, The book says one must try and follow the enquiry method which consists in turning ones thoughts inwards and trying to find out wherefrom the I, which is the root of all thoughts, arises.
(1, 345, 2, 16, 639067) If one finds one is not able to do it, one may simply go on repeating I, I, as if it were a mantram like Krishna or Rama which people use in their japa.
(1, 345, 2, 17, 639220) The idea is to concentrate on one thought to exclude all other thoughts and then eventually even the one thought will die. On this, Mrs. C. asked me, Will it be of any use if
(1, 346, 0, 1, 639395) one simply repeats I, I mechanically? I replied, When one uses I or other words like Krishna, one surely has in ones own mind some idea of the God one calls by the name I or anything else.
(1, 346, 0, 2, 639584) When a man goes on repeating Rama or Krishna, he cant be thinking of a tree as the meaning behind it. After all this, Bhagavan said, Now you consider you are making an effort and uttering I, I or other mantrams and making meditation.
(1, 346, 0, 3, 639818) But when you reach the final stage, meditation will go on without any effort on your part.
(1, 346, 0, 4, 639909) You cant get away from it or stop it, for meditation, japa, or whatever else you call it, is your real nature.
